## Instruction Priority

Superpowers skills override default system prompt behavior, but **user instructions always take precedence**:

1. **User's explicit instructions** (CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, AGENTS.md, direct requests) — highest priority
2. **Superpowers skills** — override default system behavior where they conflict
3. **Default system prompt** — lowest priority

If CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, or AGENTS.md says "don't use TDD" and a skill says "always use TDD," follow the user's instructions. The user is in control.

## How to Access Skills

**In Claude Code:** Use the `Skill` tool. When you invoke a skill, its content is loaded and presented to you—follow it directly. Never use the Read tool on skill files.

**In Copilot CLI:** Use the `skill` tool. Skills are auto-discovered from installed plugins. The `skill` tool works the same as Claude Code's `Skill` tool.

**In Gemini CLI:** Skills activate via the `activate_skill` tool. Gemini loads skill metadata at session start and activates the full content on demand.

**In other environments:** Check your platform's documentation for how skills are loaded.

## Platform Adaptation

Skills use Claude Code tool names. Non-CC platforms: see `references/copilot-tools.md` (Copilot CLI), `references/codex-tools.md` (Codex) for tool equivalents. Gemini CLI users get the tool mapping loaded automatically via GEMINI.md.

# Using Skills

## The Rule

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action.** Even a 1% chance a skill might apply means that you should invoke the skill to check. If an invoked skill turns out to be wrong for the situation, you don't need to use it.


## Red Flags

These thoughts mean STOP—you're rationalizing:

| Thought | Reality |
|---------|---------|
| "This is just a simple question" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |
| "I need more context first" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |
| "Let me explore the codebase first" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |
| "I can check git/files quickly" | Files lack conversation context. Check for skills. |
| "Let me gather information first" | Skills tell you HOW to gather information. |
| "This doesn't need a formal skill" | If a skill exists, use it. |
| "I remember this skill" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |
| "This doesn't count as a task" | Action = task. Check for skills. |
| "The skill is overkill" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |
| "I'll just do this one thing first" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |
| "This feels productive" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |
| "I know what that means" | Knowing the concept ≠ using the skill. Invoke it. |

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills could apply, use this order:

1. **Process skills first** (brainstorming, debugging) - these determine HOW to approach the task
2. **Implementation skills second** (frontend-design, mcp-builder) - these guide execution

"Let's build X" → brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
"Fix this bug" → debugging first, then domain-specific skills.

## Skill Types

**Rigid** (TDD, debugging): Follow exactly. Don't adapt away discipline.

**Flexible** (patterns): Adapt principles to context.

The skill itself tells you which.

name: sysndd-security-bug-scan
description: Use when reviewing or writing SysNDD code for security vulnerabilities or correctness bugs — authorization/role gates, SQL/expression injection, credential and secret handling, data exposure through public or MCP surfaces, resource-exhaustion/DoS from external calls, error/info leakage, and the repo's known R/Plumber footguns — especially before merging a diff or PR

# SysNDD Security & Bug Scan

A focused **defect + vulnerability** review pass over a diff or PR. Distinct from `sysndd-code-quality` (maintainability) — this hunts for exploitable and correctness-breaking defects. It complements the generic `/security-review` and `/code-review` by encoding SysNDD's specific gates, helpers, and footguns.

Core insight: almost every SysNDD vulnerability is **"bypassed a safe helper that already exists."** For each finding, prefer the in-repo helper over a hand-rolled fix.

## Workflow

1. Scope the diff. For each new/changed **endpoint, DB query, external call, or auth path**, run the relevant checks below.
2. Flag any hand-rolled code that a listed helper already covers.
3. Run the guard tests for the touched areas (see Verify) — a failing guard test usually means the change is wrong, not the guard.
4. Report findings by severity with `file:line` and the concrete in-repo fix; separate must-fix from optional.

## Security Checks

### Authorization & privilege escalation
- Every write / admin / curation endpoint must call `require_role(req, res, "<Role>")`. Auth is **per-endpoint** (no global deny filter) — a handler with no gate is reachable **unauthenticated**.
- `direct_approval` escalates the gate to **Curator** server-side; never trust the client flag (re-checked in `svc_status_apply_direct_approval` / `review_apply_direct_approval`). The frontend `hasMinRole` is UX, not a control.
- Attribution is server-set: `status_user_id <- req$user_id`. Never accept `*_user_id` from the request body.

### Injection (SQL / expression / RCE)
- User `filter` / `sort` tokens must pass through `validate_query_column()` via `generate_filter_expressions()` / `generate_sort_expressions()` with `allowed_columns_for_view()`. **Never `paste0()` or raw input into `rlang::parse_exprs()`** — over a dbplyr `tbl` that is SQL injection **and** R-side RCE (local partial-eval runs `system(...)` etc.).
- Parameterize SQL with `?` placeholders + `DBI::dbBind(stmt, unname(params))`. No string-interpolated values.
- URL-encode external path/query segments: `utils::URLencode(x, reserved = TRUE)`.

### Data exposure (public / MCP)
- MCP and public reads are **approved-public only**: reviews gated `is_primary = 1 AND review_approved = 1`; records from `ndd_entity_view` (active only). A query dropping these leaks **draft/unapproved** curation. See `sysndd-mcp-readonly`.
- MCP must not write, generate LLM summaries, or call live external providers.

### Secrets & credentials
- Auth-sensitive inputs (`/auth/signup`, `/auth/authenticate`, password change) are **JSON body only** — never query string (leaks into access/Traefik logs, browser history).
- Log through `sanitize_request()` / `sanitize_object()` (`SENSITIVE_FIELDS` redaction in `core/logging_sanitizer.R`); never log tokens, passwords, or secrets.
- Do not bake `config.yml` / secrets into image layers (no `COPY config.yml` in `api/Dockerfile`; use the runtime mount).
- Passwords use Argon2id/sodium (`hash_password` / `verify_password` in `core/security.R`); never plaintext comparison.

### Resource exhaustion / DoS
- Every external HTTP call derives its timeout/retry from `external_proxy_budget()` or `make_external_request()` — **no hardcoded `req_timeout(<n>)`** (enforced by `test-unit-external-budget-guard.R`). Wrap fetchers in `memoise_external_success_only(source = "<provider>")`.
- Cheap routes (`/health`, `/auth`, `/statistics`) must never call an external fetcher (`test-unit-cheap-route-isolation.R`).
- Public expensive operations are throttled or cache-only (async submit cap; LLM generation is Curator+ only).

### Error / info leakage
- Mount every endpoint sub-router via `mount_endpoint()` (attaches the RFC 9457 `errorHandler` + `notFoundHandler`). A bare `plumber::pr_mount(...)` leaks opaque `500`s with internal detail and drops correct status codes. Throw classed errors (`stop_for_bad_request` / `stop_for_unauthorized` / …), not bare `stop()`.

## Correctness Footguns (SysNDD-specific)

- `DBI::dbBind()` with `?` placeholders needs `unname(params)`; named lists fail silently.
- `dplyr::select` / `filter` are masked (biomaRt/AnnotationDbi) — namespace them explicitly.
- `config::get` masks `base::get` in the loaded API/worker env — bare `get(x, mode = "function")` errors "unused argument (mode)"; use `base::get` or direct dispatch (`test-unit-base-exists-get-guard.R`).
- Plumber returns JSON scalars as arrays — unwrap before feeding back into params.
- Use `inherits(x, "Date")`, not `is.Date()`.
- Worker-executed code is sourced at worker start — a change is not live until the worker restarts.

## Verify

Run the guard tests for the touched areas, then `make lint-api` and the appropriate test lane:

`test-unit-security.R`, `test-unit-filter-column-allowlist.R`, `test-unit-endpoint-error-handler.R`, `test-endpoint-auth.R` / `test-integration-auth.R`, `test-unit-*-endpoint-guard.R`, `test-unit-external-budget-guard.R`, `test-unit-cheap-route-isolation.R`.

Lead with findings ordered by severity, each with `file:line` and the in-repo fix. If nothing is found, say so and list the checks run plus residual risk.

name: sysndd-code-quality
description: Use when reviewing or changing SysNDD code for maintainability, modularity, file size, duplication, simplicity, typed boundaries, tests, or architecture quality before handoff

# SysNDD Code Quality

Use this skill as a focused review pass before handoff, during refactors, or when touching large or shared SysNDD files.

## Review Workflow

1. Inspect the diff and the nearby implementation patterns before judging the change.
2. Run deterministic checks first when they are relevant: `make code-quality-audit`, `git diff --check`, targeted tests, `make lint-api`, `make lint-app`, `cd app && npm run type-check`, `cd app && npm run type-check:strict`, or the smallest useful single-test command from `AGENTS.md`.
3. Review the changed files for the quality risks below.
4. Report concrete findings with file and line references. Distinguish must-fix issues from optional cleanup.

## Quality Checks

- **Modularity:** each file/module should have one clear responsibility and a readable public surface. Prefer cohesive helpers, composables, services, or repository functions over adding another mode to an already broad file.
- **600-line soft ceiling:** flag handwritten source files that exceed or approach 600 lines when the change makes them larger. `make code-quality-audit` enforces the deterministic ratchet: new oversized files fail, and baseline oversized files may not grow. Tests, migrations, fixtures, generated files, and tightly coupled implementations may exceed the ceiling when splitting would reduce clarity.
- **KISS:** prefer direct, local solutions that match existing patterns. Push back on speculative abstractions, new dependencies, clever generic utilities, and cross-layer shortcuts.
- **DRY:** remove meaningful duplicated business logic, API normalization, query construction, or UI state handling. Do not extract tiny one-off code if it makes call flow harder to follow.
- **SOLID, pragmatically:** apply dependency direction and single-responsibility thinking, but do not introduce class-heavy architecture just to satisfy a slogan.
- **Frontend boundaries:** views and components should use typed clients from `app/src/api/*`; do not add raw axios calls or direct `localStorage.token` / `localStorage.user` access.
- **API boundaries:** endpoint files should stay thin and delegate reusable logic to services/repositories/helpers without dropping required `svc_` or `service_` prefixes.
- **Tests:** behavior changes need targeted tests or a documented deterministic check. API integration tests that write DB state should use `with_test_db_transaction()` or document why rollback is not possible.
- **Docs:** update durable docs when behavior, commands, runtime assumptions, or contributor expectations change.

## Output

Lead with findings ordered by severity. If there are no findings, say that and list any checks run plus residual risk.
---
name: sysndd-api-testing
description: Use when writing, running, or fixing SysNDD R/Plumber API tests (testthat) — including database-writing tests, running a single test inside the API container, mocking external providers, or diagnosing SKIP-vs-PASS, helper-loading, or path-resolution issues
---

# SysNDD API Testing

Use this skill before adding or running R API tests under `api/tests/testthat/`. The suite is large (200+ files) and has non-obvious container, database, and helper conventions. The authoritative helpers are `helper-db.R`, `helper-paths.R`, and `setup.R`.

## Run Lanes

- `make test-api-fast` — fast PR gate (also what `make pre-commit` runs).
- `make test-api` — full suite locally.
- `make ci-local` — closest local mirror of CI (lint + tests with DB). Prefer before handoff.
- Single file (host): `cd api && Rscript -e "testthat::test_file('tests/testthat/test-unit-foo.R')"`
- Single file (running container): `docker exec sysndd-api-1 Rscript -e "testthat::test_file('/app/tests/testthat/test-foo.R')"`

## Container Boundary (the #1 trap)

`api/tests/` is **not** bind-mounted (only `functions/`, `services/`, `endpoints/`, `core/` are). A new or edited test must be copied in or the image rebuilt:

```bash
docker cp api/tests/testthat/test-foo.R sysndd-api-1:/app/tests/testthat/test-foo.R
```

Inside the container the default `sysndd_db_test` config points at a host-published port that the container can't reach, so `skip_if_no_test_db()` **SKIPs**. `get_test_config()` prefers `MYSQL_*` env when `MYSQL_HOST` is set, so pass DB creds to reach the DB service:

```bash
docker exec -e MYSQL_HOST=mysql -e MYSQL_DATABASE=sysndd_db_test \
  -e MYSQL_USER=<u> -e MYSQL_PASSWORD=<p> sysndd-api-1 \
  Rscript -e "testthat::test_file('/app/tests/testthat/test-foo.R')"
```

**SKIP is not PASS.** Read the summary: `[ FAIL 0 | SKIP 1 ]` means the DB test did not run. Only `PASS n` with `SKIP 0` is a real green.

## Patterns

- **Load code under test:** `source_api_file("services/foo-service.R", local = FALSE)` — resolves `/app` in-container via `get_api_dir()`. `helper-*.R` auto-load through `setup.R`.
- **DB-writing tests:** wrap in `with_test_db_transaction({ conn <- getOption(".test_db_con"); ... })` — always rolls back. It calls `skip_if_no_test_db()` for you. See AGENTS.md: prefer this or document why rollback is impossible.
- **Schema setup goes OUTSIDE the transaction.** `CREATE TABLE`/`TRUNCATE` are DDL and auto-commit — they break rollback isolation. Create fixtures on a separate connection first (mirror `ensure_test_user_table()`).
- **`DBI::dbBind()` with `?` placeholders needs `unname(params)`** (named lists fail silently); positional `params = list(x)` is safe.
- **Mock external providers**, not `httr2`: PubMed tests stub `pubmed_esearch_count()` / `pubmed_fetch_xml()`; see `helper-mock-apis.R` and `dittodb`.

## Don't Trip the Static Guards

Behavior changes must not break the guard tests that encode invariants: `test-unit-filter-column-allowlist.R`, `test-unit-endpoint-error-handler.R`, `test-unit-external-budget-guard.R`, `test-unit-cheap-route-isolation.R`, `test-unit-analysis-snapshot-coherence.R`, `test-unit-llm-model-default-guard.R`. If your change makes one fail, the change is likely wrong — not the guard.

## Output

Report which lane you ran and paste the real summary line. Never claim green on a run that only SKIPped.

     2	#### Per-caller submit throttle for the public clustering job routes (#535 S6).
     3	#### Extracted from async-job-service.R to keep both files < 600 lines. Loaded
     4	#### right after async-job-service.R in bootstrap/load_modules.R.
     5	
     6	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
     7	# Per-caller submit throttle (#535 S6 — clustering admission controls)
     8	#
     9	# async_job_capacity_exceeded() bounds the TOTAL in-flight public jobs but lets a
    10	# single caller consume every slot. This adds a per-caller sliding-window submit
    11	# rate limit as a SECOND admission dimension layered on the global cap (it does not
    12	# replace it). It is process-local (in-memory) defense-in-depth: a fresh window per
    13	# API process, so with multiple API replicas each enforces independently while the
    14	# DB-backed global cap remains the cross-process backstop.
    15	# ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    16	
    17	# Parse a positive-ish integer env var, falling back to a safe default on any
    18	# invalid/empty/non-integer value (rather than silently disabling or corrupting the
    19	# limiter, which `as.integer("abc")` -> NA would do). `max_value` clamps the accepted
    20	# value so an operator typo (e.g. MAX=1000000000) cannot make a per-caller timestamp
    21	# vector grow without bound; a value above the ceiling is clamped, not rejected.
    22	.async_job_submit_env_int <- function(name, default, min_value, max_value = NULL) {
    23	  raw <- trimws(Sys.getenv(name, ""))
    24	  if (!nzchar(raw) || !grepl("^-?[0-9]+$", raw)) {
    25	    return(as.integer(default))
    26	  }
    27	  value <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(raw))
    28	  if (is.na(value) || value < min_value) {
    29	    return(as.integer(default))
    30	  }
    31	  if (!is.null(max_value) && value > max_value) {
    32	    return(as.integer(max_value))
    33	  }
    34	  value
    35	}
    36	
    37	# Max submissions per caller per window, and the window length (seconds). Read once
    38	# at source/startup; changing the env var requires an API restart. MAX floors at 1 so
    39	# a stray `=0` (or any invalid value) falls back to the default rather than SILENTLY
    40	# disabling the control; it is clamped to a sane ceiling. WINDOW must be >= 1.
    41	CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX <-
    42	  .async_job_submit_env_int("CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX", 5L, 1L, max_value = 1000L)
    43	# WINDOW floors at 5s (a 1s window would let a tiny MAX sustain a high rate) and caps
    44	# at a day.
    45	CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS <-
    46	  .async_job_submit_env_int("CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS", 60L, 5L, max_value = 86400L)
    47	# Trusted reverse-proxy source CIDRs (comma-separated; IPv4 CIDR or exact IP). The
    48	# fingerprint walks X-Forwarded-For right-to-left and selects the first address NOT in
    49	# this set — the address our nearest proxy appended, which is non-spoofable. Empty
    50	# (the default, single-Traefik direct-edge topology) trusts nothing upstream, so the
    51	# rightmost (Traefik-appended) hop is used. Set it to the front-proxy CIDR(s) only when
    52	# an additional trusted proxy sits in front of Traefik.
    53	CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS <- local({
    54	  raw <- trimws(Sys.getenv("CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS", ""))
    55	  if (!nzchar(raw)) {
    56	    character(0)
    57	  } else {
    58	    parts <- trimws(strsplit(raw, ",", fixed = TRUE)[[1]])
    59	    parts[nzchar(parts)]
    60	  }
    61	})
    62	# Hard cap on distinct tracked fingerprints — bounds memory against X-Forwarded-For
    63	# rotation (each spoofed value would otherwise create a permanent 1-entry bucket).
    64	CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED <-
    65	  .async_job_submit_env_int("CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED", 20000L, 100L, max_value = 200000L)
    66	
    67	# fingerprint -> numeric vector of recent submit epoch-seconds.
    68	.clustering_submit_history <- new.env(parent = emptyenv())
    69	
    70	# Dotted IPv4 -> numeric (0..2^32-1), or NA for anything else (incl. IPv6).
    71	.async_job_submit_ipv4_num <- function(ip) {
    72	  m <- regmatches(ip, regexec("^([0-9]{1,3})\\.([0-9]{1,3})\\.([0-9]{1,3})\\.([0-9]{1,3})$", ip))[[1]]
    73	  if (length(m) != 5L) {
    74	    return(NA_real_)
    75	  }
    76	  o <- as.numeric(m[2:5])
    77	  if (any(o < 0 | o > 255)) {
    78	    return(NA_real_)
    79	  }
    80	  o[[1]] * 16777216 + o[[2]] * 65536 + o[[3]] * 256 + o[[4]]
    81	}
    82	
    83	# Expand an IPv6 string to its eight integer hextets (0..65535), or NULL when invalid
    84	# (bad hextet, wrong group count, >1 or malformed "::"). Fully expands "::" to the
    85	# exact zero run so the SAME address in any compression yields identical hextets.
    86	.async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets <- function(token) {
    87	  low <- tolower(token)
    88	  if (!grepl(":", low, fixed = TRUE) || !grepl("^[0-9a-f:]+$", low) ||
    89	        grepl(":::", low, fixed = TRUE)) {
    90	    return(NULL)
    91	  }
    92	  dbl <- gregexpr("::", low, fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
    93	  if (length(dbl) == 1L && dbl[[1]] != -1L) {
    94	    left <- sub("::.*$", "", low)
    95	    right <- sub("^.*::", "", low)
    96	    lg <- if (nzchar(left)) strsplit(left, ":", fixed = TRUE)[[1]] else character(0)
    97	    rg <- if (nzchar(right)) strsplit(right, ":", fixed = TRUE)[[1]] else character(0)
    98	    zeros <- 8L - length(lg) - length(rg)
    99	    if (zeros < 1L) {
   100	      return(NULL)
   101	    }
   102	    groups <- c(lg, rep("0", zeros), rg)
   103	  } else if (length(dbl) == 1L && dbl[[1]] == -1L) {
   104	    groups <- strsplit(low, ":", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   105	  } else {
   106	    return(NULL)
   107	  }
   108	  if (length(groups) != 8L || !all(grepl("^[0-9a-f]{1,4}$", groups))) {
   109	    return(NULL)
   110	  }
   111	  strtoi(groups, base = 16L)
   112	}
   113	
   114	#' Classify a candidate client identifier into (family, canonical full IP, bucket key),
   115	#' or family = NA when it is not a plausible IP.
   116	#'
   117	#' Rejecting non-IP tokens (an attacker-injected `X_Forwarded_For` header-alias value,
   118	#' junk) stops arbitrary strings from becoming rotating throttle keys. `canonical` is
   119	#' the FULL address (used for trusted-proxy matching); `key` is the bucket key: the bare
   120	#' IPv4, or the IPv6 `/64` prefix so a whole allocation is ONE caller. `/64` grouping is
   121	#' applied ONLY to the key, never to the trust check — so an IPv6 trusted proxy still
   122	#' matches its configured CIDR/address.
   123	#'
   124	#' @param token Candidate identifier (an XFF hop or REMOTE_ADDR).
   125	#' @return list(family = "v4"/"v6"/NA, canonical, key).
   126	.async_job_submit_ip_classify <- function(token) {
   127	  na <- list(family = NA_character_, canonical = NA_character_, key = NA_character_)
   128	  if (is.null(token) || length(token) != 1L || is.na(token)) {
   129	    return(na)
   130	  }
   131	  token <- trimws(as.character(token))
   132	  token <- sub("^\\[(.*)\\]$", "\\1", token) # [::1]:port already portless -> ::1
   133	  if (!nzchar(token) || nchar(token) > 64L) {
   134	    return(na)
   135	  }
   136	  ipv4 <- sub(":[0-9]+$", "", token) # IPv4 may carry a :port we drop
   137	  if (grepl("^[0-9]{1,3}(\\.[0-9]{1,3}){3}$", ipv4)) {
   138	    octets <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(strsplit(ipv4, ".", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]))
   139	    if (!anyNA(octets) && all(octets >= 0L & octets <= 255L)) {
   140	      return(list(family = "v4", canonical = ipv4, key = ipv4))
   141	    }
   142	    return(na)
   143	  }
   144	  hex <- .async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(token)
   145	  if (!is.null(hex)) {
   146	    hx <- sprintf("%x", hex) # canonical hextets, leading zeros stripped
   147	    return(list(
   148	      family = "v6",
   149	      canonical = paste(hx, collapse = ":"),
   150	      key = paste0(paste(hx[1:4], collapse = ":"), "::/64")
   151	    ))
   152	  }
   153	  na
   154	}
   155	
   156	#' Bucket key for a candidate identifier (bare IPv4 / IPv6 `/64`), or NA if not an IP.
   157	.async_job_submit_normalize_ip <- function(token) {
   158	  .async_job_submit_ip_classify(token)$key
   159	}
   160	
   161	# TRUE when the IPv4 `ip` matches CIDR `c` (`a.b.c.d/n`) or an exact IPv4. Prefix compare
   162	# uses integer division on the 32-bit value (no bitwAnd -> no 2^31 overflow).
   163	.async_job_submit_v4_match <- function(ip, c) {
   164	  ip_num <- .async_job_submit_ipv4_num(ip)
   165	  if (is.na(ip_num)) {
   166	    return(FALSE)
   167	  }
   168	  if (grepl("/", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   169	    seg <- strsplit(c, "/", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   170	    if (length(seg) != 2L) {
   171	      return(FALSE)
   172	    }
   173	    bits <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(seg[[2]]))
   174	    net <- .async_job_submit_ipv4_num(seg[[1]])
   175	    if (is.na(bits) || bits < 0L || bits > 32L || is.na(net)) {
   176	      return(FALSE)
   177	    }
   178	    shift <- 2^(32 - bits)
   179	    return(floor(ip_num / shift) == floor(net / shift))
   180	  }
   181	  identical(.async_job_submit_ipv4_num(c), ip_num)
   182	}
   183	
   184	# TRUE when the IPv6 `ip_canonical` matches CIDR `c` (`.../n`, 0..128) or an exact IPv6.
   185	# Compares full hextets, then the boundary hextet under a mask (values <=65535, so no
   186	# bitwAnd overflow).
   187	.async_job_submit_v6_match <- function(ip_canonical, c) {
   188	  ih <- .async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(ip_canonical)
   189	  if (is.null(ih)) {
   190	    return(FALSE)
   191	  }
   192	  if (grepl("/", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   193	    seg <- strsplit(c, "/", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   194	    if (length(seg) != 2L) {
   195	      return(FALSE)
   196	    }
   197	    bits <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(seg[[2]]))
   198	    nh <- .async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(seg[[1]])
   199	    if (is.na(bits) || bits < 0L || bits > 128L || is.null(nh)) {
   200	      return(FALSE)
   201	    }
   202	    full <- bits %/% 16L
   203	    rem <- bits %% 16L
   204	    if (full > 0L && !all(ih[seq_len(full)] == nh[seq_len(full)])) {
   205	      return(FALSE)
   206	    }
   207	    if (rem > 0L) {
   208	      mask <- 65536L - as.integer(2^(16L - rem))
   209	      if (bitwAnd(ih[[full + 1L]], mask) != bitwAnd(nh[[full + 1L]], mask)) {
   210	        return(FALSE)
   211	      }
   212	    }
   213	    return(TRUE)
   214	  }
   215	  nh <- .async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(c)
   216	  !is.null(nh) && all(ih == nh)
   217	}
   218	
   219	# TRUE when the classified candidate (family + canonical full IP) is inside one of the
   220	# trusted-proxy `cidrs`. IPv4 candidates match only IPv4 CIDRs/addresses and IPv6 only
   221	# IPv6 — evaluated on the CANONICAL address, never the /64 bucket key.
   222	.async_job_submit_ip_trusted <- function(family, canonical, cidrs) {
   223	  if (length(cidrs) == 0L || is.null(family) || is.na(family)) {
   224	    return(FALSE)
   225	  }
   226	  for (c in cidrs) {
   227	    c <- trimws(c)
   228	    cidr_is_v6 <- grepl(":", c, fixed = TRUE)
   229	    if (family == "v4" && !cidr_is_v6 && .async_job_submit_v4_match(canonical, c)) {
   230	      return(TRUE)
   231	    }
   232	    if (family == "v6" && cidr_is_v6 && .async_job_submit_v6_match(canonical, c)) {
   233	      return(TRUE)
   234	    }
   235	  }
   236	  FALSE
   237	}
   238	
   239	# TRUE when `c` is a syntactically valid IPv4/IPv6 CIDR or exact address.
   240	.async_job_submit_valid_cidr <- function(c) {
   241	  c <- trimws(c)
   242	  if (grepl(":", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   243	    if (grepl("/", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   244	      seg <- strsplit(c, "/", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   245	      bits <- if (length(seg) == 2L) suppressWarnings(as.integer(seg[[2]])) else NA_integer_
   246	      return(!is.na(bits) && bits >= 0L && bits <= 128L &&
   247	               !is.null(.async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(seg[[1]])))
   248	    }
   249	    return(!is.null(.async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(c)))
   250	  }
   251	  if (grepl("/", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   252	    seg <- strsplit(c, "/", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   253	    bits <- if (length(seg) == 2L) suppressWarnings(as.integer(seg[[2]])) else NA_integer_
   254	    return(!is.na(bits) && bits >= 0L && bits <= 32L && !is.na(.async_job_submit_ipv4_num(seg[[1]])))
   255	  }
   256	  !is.na(.async_job_submit_ipv4_num(c))
   257	}
   258	
   259	# Surface (but do not fail boot on) malformed trusted-proxy CIDRs: an invalid entry
   260	# simply never matches (safe — it trusts nothing), so log it for visibility.
   261	local({
   262	  bad <- Filter(function(c) !.async_job_submit_valid_cidr(c), CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS)
   263	  if (length(bad) > 0L && base::exists("log_warn", mode = "function")) {
   264	    log_warn(paste0(
   265	      "CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS has invalid entries (ignored): ",
   266	      paste(bad, collapse = ", ")
   267	    ))
   268	  }
   269	})
   270	
   271	#' Resolve the client fingerprint for submit throttling.
   272	#'
   273	#' Walks `X-Forwarded-For` RIGHT-TO-LEFT and returns the first address that is NOT a
   274	#' known trusted proxy (`CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS`). Our nearest proxy
   275	#' appends the address of the peer it actually saw at the RIGHT, so the first untrusted
   276	#' address from the right is the real client and is NOT spoofable: an attacker can put
   277	#' anything in the leftmost entries, but the rightmost hop it cannot forge is the peer
   278	#' our proxy observed. With the default empty trust set (single-Traefik direct edge)
   279	#' this is simply the rightmost hop. Each candidate must validate as an IP
   280	#' (`.async_job_submit_normalize_ip()`); non-IP tokens (header-alias injection, junk)
   281	#' are skipped. Falls back to a validated `REMOTE_ADDR`, then a constant. Never throws:
   282	#' crafted headers degrade to the `"unknown"` bucket, they cannot fail the request.
   283	#'
   284	#' @param req Plumber request object.
   285	#' @param trusted_cidrs Trusted reverse-proxy source CIDRs (default env).
   286	#' @return Character fingerprint (never empty).
   287	#' @export
   288	async_job_submit_fingerprint <- function(req,
   289	                                         trusted_cidrs = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS) {
   290	  xff <- tryCatch(req$HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR, error = function(e) NULL)
   291	  if (!is.null(xff) && length(xff) == 1L && nzchar(xff)) {
   292	    parts <- trimws(strsplit(as.character(xff), ",", fixed = TRUE)[[1]])
   293	    parts <- parts[nzchar(parts)]
   294	    for (i in rev(seq_along(parts))) {
   295	      p <- .async_job_submit_ip_classify(parts[[i]])
   296	      if (is.na(p$family)) next                                        # non-IP -> ignore
   297	      if (.async_job_submit_ip_trusted(p$family, p$canonical, trusted_cidrs)) next # our proxy
   298	      return(p$key)                                                    # first untrusted from right
   299	    }
   300	  }
   301	  addr <- .async_job_submit_normalize_ip(tryCatch(req$REMOTE_ADDR, error = function(e) NULL))
   302	  if (!is.na(addr)) {
   303	    return(addr)
   304	  }
   305	  "unknown"
   306	}
   307	
   308	# Reserved store keys (control-char prefix -> never a valid IP / "unknown", so they
   309	# cannot collide with a real fingerprint). The overflow bucket collectively throttles
   310	# brand-new callers once the store is saturated with ACTIVE callers; the sweep marker
   311	# time-gates the reclaim scan; the count marker holds the O(1) tracked-bucket count.
   312	.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY <- "\001overflow"
   313	.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY <- "\001sweep_at"
   314	.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY <- "\001count"
   315	
   316	# O(1) tracked-caller count (real fingerprints, EXCLUDING the shared overflow and the
   317	# reserved markers). Maintained on insert/reclaim so the hot path never scans the env.
   318	.async_job_submit_size <- function(store) {
   319	  if (base::exists(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)) {
   320	    base::get(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   321	  } else {
   322	    0L
   323	  }
   324	}
   325	
   326	.async_job_submit_size_add <- function(store, delta) {
   327	  assign(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY, .async_job_submit_size(store) + as.integer(delta), envir = store)
   328	}
   329	
   330	#' Reclaim store space by dropping ONLY fully-idle fingerprints (every timestamp aged
   331	#' out) — an active caller's window is never evicted. Sort-free (`names()`, not the
   332	#' sorting `ls()`), and time-gated to at most once per window so a rotation flood
   333	#' cannot force an O(n) scan on every request. Keeps the O(1) counter in sync.
   334	.async_job_submit_reclaim <- function(store, cutoff, now, window_s) {
   335	  sweep_at <- if (base::exists(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)) {
   336	    base::get(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   337	  } else {
   338	    -Inf
   339	  }
   340	  if ((now - sweep_at) < window_s) {
   341	    return(invisible(NULL))
   342	  }
   343	  reserved <- c(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY)
   344	  keys <- setdiff(names(store), reserved)
   345	  removed_real <- 0L
   346	  for (k in keys) {
   347	    ts <- base::get(k, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   348	    if (length(ts) == 0L || max(ts) <= cutoff) {
   349	      rm(list = k, envir = store)
   350	      if (!identical(k, .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY)) {
   351	        removed_real <- removed_real + 1L
   352	      }
   353	    }
   354	  }
   355	  assign(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, now, envir = store)
   356	  if (removed_real > 0L) {
   357	    .async_job_submit_size_add(store, -removed_real)
   358	  }
   359	  invisible(NULL)
   360	}
   361	
   362	#' Sliding-window per-caller submit rate limit.
   363	#'
   364	#' Pure except for the module-level `store`; the clock is injected so tests are
   365	#' deterministic. Records the attempt when allowed. Memory is bounded at `max_tracked`
   366	#' fingerprints: once the store is saturated with ACTIVE callers, a brand-new
   367	#' fingerprint is routed into a single shared overflow bucket (collectively throttled)
   368	#' rather than evicting a legitimate caller's window — so an attacker rotating
   369	#' X-Forwarded-For values can neither exhaust memory nor reset an innocent caller.
   370	#' Invalid `max_n`/`window_s` FAIL CLOSED (`stop()`): the admission guard maps the
   371	#' error to a 503, so an internal misconfiguration can never silently admit.
   372	#'
   373	#' @param fingerprint Caller fingerprint (see async_job_submit_fingerprint()).
   374	#' @param now Current epoch-seconds (injected for tests).
   375	#' @param max_n Max allowed submissions in the window.
   376	#' @param window_s Window length in seconds.
   377	#' @param store Environment mapping fingerprint -> recent timestamps.
   378	#' @param max_tracked Hard cap on distinct tracked fingerprints.
   379	#' @return list(allowed, retry_after, count).
   380	#' @export
   381	async_job_submit_rate_limit <- function(fingerprint,
   382	                                        now = as.numeric(Sys.time()),
   383	                                        max_n = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX,
   384	                                        window_s = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS,
   385	                                        store = .clustering_submit_history,
   386	                                        max_tracked = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED) {
   387	  if (is.null(fingerprint) || length(fingerprint) != 1L || is.na(fingerprint) || !nzchar(fingerprint)) {
   388	    fingerprint <- "unknown"
   389	  }
   390	  # Invalid limiter parameters are an internal error, not a disable switch: fail CLOSED
   391	  # so the admission guard returns 503 THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE rather than silently admit.
   392	  if (length(max_n) != 1L || !is.finite(max_n) || max_n < 1L ||
   393	        length(window_s) != 1L || !is.finite(window_s) || window_s < 1L) {
   394	    stop("clustering submit throttle misconfigured: max_n and window_s must be finite and >= 1")
   395	  }
   396	  cutoff <- now - window_s
   397	  is_new <- !base::exists(fingerprint, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   398	  # Bound the store BEFORE recording a brand-new fingerprint.
   399	  if (is_new && .async_job_submit_size(store) >= max_tracked) {
   400	    .async_job_submit_reclaim(store, cutoff, now, window_s)
   401	    if (.async_job_submit_size(store) >= max_tracked) {
   402	      fingerprint <- .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY # saturated -> shared bucket
   403	      is_new <- !base::exists(fingerprint, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   404	    }
   405	  }
   406	  prev <- if (!is_new) {
   407	    base::get(fingerprint, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   408	  } else {
   409	    numeric(0)
   410	  }
   411	  recent <- prev[prev > cutoff]
   412	  if (length(recent) >= max_n) {
   413	    # The oldest in-window submission ages out at recent[1] + window_s.
   414	    retry_after <- max(1L, as.integer(ceiling((recent[[1]] + window_s) - now)))
   415	    assign(fingerprint, recent, envir = store) # persist the prune
   416	    return(list(allowed = FALSE, retry_after = retry_after, count = length(recent)))
   417	  }
   418	  assign(fingerprint, c(recent, now), envir = store)
   419	  # Count only real distinct callers (never the shared overflow) toward the bound.
   420	  if (is_new && !identical(fingerprint, .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY)) {
   421	    .async_job_submit_size_add(store, 1L)
   422	  }
   423	  list(allowed = TRUE, retry_after = 0L, count = length(recent) + 1L)
   424	}
   425	
   426	#' Admission guard for the public clustering submit routes.
   427	#'
   428	#' The single entry point both submit services call FIRST (before any DB/cache/
   429	#' duplicate work) so an abusive caller is rejected before it can do — or provoke —
   430	#' any expensive work. Derives the caller fingerprint, applies the per-caller
   431	#' throttle, and translates the decision to an HTTP response on `res`:
   432	#'   * allowed  -> `list(admitted = TRUE)` (caller proceeds)
   433	#'   * throttled-> `429` + `Retry-After`, `error = "RATE_LIMITED"`
   434	#'   * internal error -> **fail CLOSED** `503` + `Retry-After`,
   435	#'     `error = "THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE"` (a throttle bug must neither 500 the
   436	#'     endpoint nor silently admit an abusive caller).
   437	#'
   438	#' @param req Plumber request.
   439	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated in place on a block).
   440	#' @return list(admitted = TRUE) or list(admitted = FALSE, response = <payload>).
   441	#' @export
   442	# Emit the fail-closed 503 on a fresh `res`. Kept as one non-throwing helper so every
   443	# error/malformed-decision path routes through exactly one place.
   444	.async_job_submit_unavailable <- function(res) {
   445	  res$status <- 503L
   446	  res$setHeader("Retry-After", "5")
   447	  list(admitted = FALSE, response = list(
   448	    error = "THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE",
   449	    message = "Submission throttling is temporarily unavailable. Please retry shortly.",
   450	    retry_after = 5L
   451	  ))
   452	}
   453	
   454	async_job_submit_admission_guard <- function(req, res) {
   455	  decision <- tryCatch(
   456	    async_job_submit_rate_limit(async_job_submit_fingerprint(req)),
   457	    error = function(e) {
   458	      # Logging must never itself fail the request (log_warn may be absent in a
   459	      # library-light env, or a glue interpolation could throw) -> swallow it.
   460	      try(
   461	        if (base::exists("log_warn", mode = "function")) {
   462	          log_warn("clustering submit throttle failed (fail-closed 503): {conditionMessage(e)}")
   463	        },
   464	        silent = TRUE
   465	      )
   466	      NULL
   467	    }
   468	  )
   469	  # Fail CLOSED on a NULL OR malformed decision (schema-validate before use, so a bad
   470	  # shape can never reach setHeader() with an invalid value and 500 the endpoint).
   471	  valid <- is.list(decision) &&
   472	    length(decision$allowed) == 1L && is.logical(decision$allowed) && !is.na(decision$allowed)
   473	  if (!valid) {
   474	    return(.async_job_submit_unavailable(res))
   475	  }
   476	  if (!isTRUE(decision$allowed)) {
   477	    retry_after <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(decision$retry_after))
   478	    if (length(retry_after) != 1L || is.na(retry_after) || retry_after < 1L) {
   479	      retry_after <- 1L
   480	    }
   481	    res$status <- 429L
   482	    res$setHeader("Retry-After", as.character(retry_after))
   483	    return(list(admitted = FALSE, response = list(
   484	      error = "RATE_LIMITED",
   485	      message = "Too many analysis submissions from your client. Please retry shortly.",
   486	      retry_after = retry_after
   487	    )))
   488	  }
   489	  list(admitted = TRUE)
   490	}
   491	
   492	#' Reset the in-memory submit-throttle store (tests only).
   493	#' @export
   494	async_job_submit_rate_limit_reset <- function(store = .clustering_submit_history) {
   495	  rm(list = ls(envir = store, all.names = TRUE), envir = store)
   496	  invisible(NULL)
   497	}

     1	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
     2	# api/bootstrap/load_modules.R
     3	#
     4	# Part of the Phase D.D6 extract-bootstrap refactor.
     5	#
     6	# Loads every R source file required by the running API into the
     7	# global environment, in the correct order:
     8	#   1. functions/* (repositories, helpers, clients, etc.)
     9	#   2. core/* (security, errors, responses, middleware, filters)
    10	#   3. services/* (transactional orchestration)
    11	#
    12	# Source order matters. Repository functions are loaded BEFORE
    13	# services so that any `svc_`/`service_`-prefixed function in
    14	# services/* can still call the underlying repository helpers.
    15	# (A service that accidentally drops its prefix will shadow the
    16	# repository function — see CLAUDE.md.)
    17	#
    18	# Mirai daemon workers do NOT use this module. They re-source a
    19	# hand-picked subset of functions/* via `everywhere({...})` in
    20	# api/bootstrap/setup_workers.R. Changes here do not automatically
    21	# propagate to workers — update setup_workers.R as well when a
    22	# function file is needed inside a daemon.
    23	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    24	
    25	#' Source a file into .GlobalEnv with a helpful error if missing.
    26	#'
    27	#' `source(..., local = FALSE)` puts the bindings into the global
    28	#' environment — that is what endpoint files expect at runtime.
    29	#' Top-level `source("...", local = TRUE)` in start_sysndd_api.R
    30	#' previously had the same effect by accident of being at the top
    31	#' level of the script; here we make the intent explicit.
    32	#'
    33	#' @param path Relative path from api/ to the source file.
    34	#' @noRd
    35	.bootstrap_source <- function(path) {
    36	  if (!file.exists(path)) {
    37	    stop(sprintf("bootstrap: source file not found: %s", path))
    38	  }
    39	  source(path, local = FALSE)
    40	  invisible(NULL)
    41	}

     1	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
     2	# api/bootstrap/mount_endpoints.R
     3	#
     4	# Part of the Phase D.D6 extract-bootstrap refactor.
     5	#
     6	# Builds the root Plumber router:
     7	#   - attaches the RFC 9457 error handler + 404 handler
     8	#   - wires the OpenAPI spec callback (reads version_spec.json)
     9	#   - attaches the `cors` and `require_auth` filters
    10	#   - installs the exit hook that closes the DB pool and the
    11	#     mirai daemon pool
    12	#   - mounts every endpoint file under /api/<subpath>
    13	#   - installs the preroute/postroute timing + logging hook
    14	#
    15	# The composer in start_sysndd_api.R passes the pool and the
    16	# temporary log-file path; they are captured by closure so the
    17	# exit hook and the postroute hook can reach them without needing
    18	# top-level globals.
    19	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    20	
    21	#' Build the fully-mounted root Plumber router.
    22	#'
    23	#' @param api_spec The parsed `config/api_spec.json` list, used by
    24	#'   `update_api_spec_examples()` inside the OpenAPI spec callback.
    25	#' @param pool The shared DBI pool; closed by the exit hook.
    26	#' @param logging_temp_file Path to the Plumber access log file; the
    27	#'   postroute hook passes this to `log_message_to_db()` so entries
    28	#'   can be correlated with the on-disk logs.
    29	#' @return A Plumber router ready to be started with `pr_run()`.
    30	#' @export
    31	bootstrap_mount_endpoints <- function(api_spec, pool, logging_temp_file) {
    32	
    33	  # Named closure for the exit hook so the pool reference travels
    34	  # via closure instead of via a global lookup.
    35	  cleanupHook <- function(pr) {
    36	    pr %>%
    37	      plumber::pr_hook("exit", function() {
    38	        pool::poolClose(pool)
    39	        message("Disconnected from DB")
    40	        mirai::daemons(0) # Shutdown mirai daemon pool
    41	        message("Shutdown mirai daemon pool")
    42	      })
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  # Build a mounted endpoint sub-router that inherits the API's RFC 9457 error
    46	  # and 404 handling. Plumber does NOT propagate the root router's error/404
    47	  # handlers to mounted sub-routers (each router keeps its own), so a thrown
    48	  # classed error (e.g. stop_for_bad_request() -> error_400) or an unknown
    49	  # sub-path would otherwise fall back to plumber's default opaque
    50	  # `{"error":"500 ..."}` / `{"error":"404 ..."}` instead of being mapped to the
    51	  # correct status + problem+json by errorHandler / notFoundHandler. Attaching
    52	  # them here keeps error and not-found responses consistent across every
    53	  # /api/<subpath>. Static guard: tests/testthat/test-unit-endpoint-error-handler.R
    54	  mount_endpoint <- function(file) {
    55	    plumber::pr(file) %>%
    56	      plumber::pr_set_error(errorHandler) %>%
    57	      plumber::pr_set_404(notFoundHandler)
    58	  }
    59	
    60	  plumber::pr() %>%
    61	    # Install error handler middleware
    62	    plumber::pr_set_error(errorHandler) %>%
    63	    # Install 404 handler for non-existent routes (RFC 9457 compliant)
    64	    plumber::pr_set_404(notFoundHandler) %>%
    65	    # Insert doc info in pr_set_api_spec
    66	    plumber::pr_set_api_spec(function(spec) {
    67	      # Read version info from version_spec.json
    68	      version_info <- jsonlite::fromJSON("version_spec.json")
    69	      spec$info$title <- version_info$title
    70	      spec$info$description <- version_info$description
    71	      spec$info$version <- version_info$version
    72	
    73	      if (!is.null(version_info$contact)) {
    74	        spec$info$contact <- version_info$contact
    75	      }
    76	      if (!is.null(version_info$license)) {
    77	        spec$info$license <- version_info$license
    78	      }
    79	
    80	      spec$components$securitySchemes$bearerAuth$type <- "http"
    81	      spec$components$securitySchemes$bearerAuth$scheme <- "bearer"
    82	      spec$components$securitySchemes$bearerAuth$bearerFormat <- "JWT"
    83	      spec$security[[1]]$bearerAuth <- ""
    84	
    85	      # Insert example requests from your api_spec.json (optional)
    86	      spec <- update_api_spec_examples(spec, api_spec)
    87	
    88	      # Enhance with modular schemas and standard error responses
    89	      spec <- enhance_openapi_spec(
    90	        spec,
    91	        config_dir = "config/openapi",
    92	        add_error_responses = TRUE,
    93	        public_paths = c(
    94	          "/api/health", "/api/version", "/api/about",
    95	          "/api/seo/routes", "/api/seo/gene", "/api/seo/entity", "/api/seo/static",
    96	          "/__docs__", "/__swagger__"
    97	        )
    98	      )
    99	
   100	      spec
   101	    }) %>%
   102	    ####################################################################
   103	    # Attach filters
   104	    ####################################################################
   105	    plumber::pr_filter("cors", corsFilter) %>%
   106	    plumber::pr_filter("require_auth", require_auth) %>%
   107	    ####################################################################
   108	    # Attach exit hook
   109	    ####################################################################
   110	    cleanupHook() %>%
   111	    ####################################################################
   112	    # Mount health endpoint for Docker HEALTHCHECK
   113	    ####################################################################
   114	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/health", mount_endpoint("endpoints/health_endpoints.R")) %>%
   115	    ####################################################################
   116	    # Mount version endpoint for API version discovery
   117	    ####################################################################
   118	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/version", mount_endpoint("endpoints/version_endpoints.R")) %>%
   119	    ####################################################################
   120	    # Mount each endpoint file at /api/<subpath>
   121	    ####################################################################
   122	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/entity", mount_endpoint("endpoints/entity_endpoints.R")) %>%
   123	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/review", mount_endpoint("endpoints/review_endpoints.R")) %>%
   124	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/re_review", mount_endpoint("endpoints/re_review_endpoints.R")) %>%
   125	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/publication", mount_endpoint("endpoints/publication_endpoints.R")) %>%
   126	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/gene", mount_endpoint("endpoints/gene_endpoints.R")) %>%
   127	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/ontology", mount_endpoint("endpoints/ontology_endpoints.R")) %>%
   128	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/phenotype", mount_endpoint("endpoints/phenotype_endpoints.R")) %>%
   129	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/status", mount_endpoint("endpoints/status_endpoints.R")) %>%
   130	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/panels", mount_endpoint("endpoints/panels_endpoints.R")) %>%
   131	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/comparisons", mount_endpoint("endpoints/comparisons_endpoints.R")) %>%
   132	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/analysis", mount_endpoint("endpoints/analysis_endpoints.R")) %>%
   133	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/jobs/network_layout", mount_endpoint("endpoints/jobs_network_layout_endpoints.R")) %>%
   134	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/jobs", mount_endpoint("endpoints/jobs_endpoints.R")) %>%
   135	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/hash", mount_endpoint("endpoints/hash_endpoints.R")) %>%
   136	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/search", mount_endpoint("endpoints/search_endpoints.R")) %>%
   137	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/list", mount_endpoint("endpoints/list_endpoints.R")) %>%
   138	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/metadata", mount_endpoint("endpoints/metadata_endpoints.R")) %>%
   139	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/logs", mount_endpoint("endpoints/logging_endpoints.R")) %>%
   140	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/user", mount_endpoint("endpoints/user_endpoints.R")) %>%
   141	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/auth", mount_endpoint("endpoints/authentication_endpoints.R")) %>%

   190	        convert_empty(req$HTTP_HOST),
     1	# Authentication and Authorization Middleware for SysNDD API
     2	# Provides centralized JWT validation and role-based access control via Plumber filters
     3	#
     4	# Usage:
     5	#   source("core/middleware.R")
     6	#   pr_filter("require_auth", require_auth)
     7	#
     8	# Exports:
     9	#   - require_auth: Filter for JWT validation and user context attachment
    10	#   - require_role: Helper function for endpoint-level role enforcement
    11	#   - AUTH_ALLOWLIST: Public endpoints that bypass authentication
    12	
    13	library(jose)
    14	library(stringr)
    15	library(logger)

    17	# Public endpoints that bypass authentication
    18	# These endpoints are accessible without Bearer tokens
    19	AUTH_ALLOWLIST <- c(
    20	  "/api/gene/hash",
    21	  "/api/entity/hash",
    22	  "/api/jobs/clustering/submit",
    23	  "/api/jobs/clustering/submit/",

    56	#' Authentication Filter
    57	#'
    58	#' Validates JWT tokens for protected endpoints. Implements allowlist pattern
    59	#' for public endpoints and provides public read access for GET requests.
    60	#'
    61	#' Authentication flow:
    62	#' 1. OPTIONS requests (CORS preflight) -> forward
    63	#' 2. Paths in AUTH_ALLOWLIST -> forward
    64	#' 3. GET requests without auth -> forward (public read access)
    65	#' 4. All other requests -> require valid Bearer token
    66	#'
    67	#' On successful authentication, attaches to req object:
    68	#' - req$user_id: Numeric user ID
    69	#' - req$user_role: String user role (Viewer, Reviewer, Curator, Administrator)
    70	#' - req$user_name: String user name
    71	#'
    72	#' @param req Plumber request object
    73	#' @param res Plumber response object
    74	#' @return Forwards to next filter/endpoint on success, returns 401 error on failure
    75	#'
    76	#' @examples
    77	#' \dontrun{
    78	#' pr_filter("require_auth", require_auth)
    79	#' }
    80	require_auth <- function(req, res) {
    81	  # OPTIONS requests (CORS preflight) always forward
    82	  if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "OPTIONS") {
    83	    log_debug("require_auth: OPTIONS request, forwarding")
    84	    return(plumber::forward())
    85	  }
    86	
    87	  # Check if path is in allowlist (public endpoints)
    88	  if (req$PATH_INFO %in% AUTH_ALLOWLIST) {
    89	    log_debug("require_auth: Path in allowlist, forwarding", path = req$PATH_INFO)
    90	    return(plumber::forward())
    91	  }
    92	
    93	  # GET requests without auth get public read access
    94	  if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "GET" && is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
    95	    log_debug("require_auth: GET without auth, forwarding (public read)")
    96	    return(plumber::forward())
    97	  }
    98	
    99	  # All other cases require authentication
   100	  if (is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   101	    log_warn("require_auth: Missing authorization header",
   102	             method = req$REQUEST_METHOD,
   103	             path = req$PATH_INFO)
   104	    res$status <- 401
   105	    stop(error_unauthorized("Authorization header missing. Please provide a Bearer token."))
   106	  }
   107	
   108	  # Extract and validate Bearer token
   109	  token <- stringr::str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "^Bearer\\s+")
   110	
   111	  # Decode JWT using global secret (dw$secret is approved global)
   112	  key <- charToRaw(if (is.list(dw$secret)) as.character(dw$secret[[1]]) else as.character(dw$secret))
   113	
   114	  tryCatch({
   115	    user <- jose::jwt_decode_hmac(token, secret = key)
   116	
   117	    # Check token expiration
   118	    if (!is.null(user$exp) && user$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   119	      log_warn("require_auth: Token expired", user_id = user$user_id)
   120	      res$status <- 401
   121	      stop(error_unauthorized("Token expired. Please refresh your authentication."))
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    # Attach user context to request for downstream use
   125	    req$user_id <- as.integer(user$user_id)
   126	    req$user_role <- user$user_role
   127	    req$user_name <- user$user_name %||% "Unknown"
   128	
   129	    log_debug("require_auth: Authentication successful",
   130	              user_id = req$user_id,
   130	  }
   131	
   132	  plumber::forward()
   133	}
   134	
   135	#* @filter check_signin
   136	# DEPRECATED: Use require_auth filter instead.
   137	# This will be removed after Phase 22 endpoint migration.
   138	checkSignInFilter <- function(req, res) {
   139	  key <- charToRaw(if (is.list(dw$secret)) as.character(dw$secret[[1]]) else as.character(dw$secret))
   140	
   141	  # GET without auth => forward
   142	  if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "GET" && is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   143	    plumber::forward()
   144	  } else if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "GET" && !is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   145	    # GET with Bearer token => decode
   146	    jwt <- str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "Bearer ")
   147	    tryCatch(
   148	      {
   149	        user <- jwt_decode_hmac(jwt, secret = key)
   150	      },
   151	      error = function(e) {
   152	        res$status <- 401
   153	        return(list(error = "Token expired or invalid."))
   154	      }
   155	    )
   156	    req$user_id <- as.integer(user$user_id)
   157	    req$user_role <- user$user_role
   158	    plumber::forward()
   159	  } else if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "POST" &&
   160	    (req$PATH_INFO == "/api/gene/hash" || req$PATH_INFO == "/api/entity/hash")) {
   161	    # POST to /api/entity/hash or /api/gene/hash => forward
   162	    plumber::forward()
   163	  } else if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "POST" &&
   164	    (req$PATH_INFO %in% c(
   165	      "/api/jobs/clustering/submit",
   166	      "/api/jobs/clustering/submit/",
   167	      "/api/jobs/phenotype_clustering/submit",
   168	      "/api/jobs/phenotype_clustering/submit/"
   169	    ))) {
   170	    # POST to public async job endpoints => forward
   171	    # (clustering and phenotype_clustering are public, ontology_update requires auth handled internally)
   172	    plumber::forward()
   173	  } else if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "PUT" &&
   174	    (req$PATH_INFO == "/api/user/password/reset/request")) {
   175	    # PUT to /api/user/password/reset/request
   176	    plumber::forward()
   177	  } else {
   178	    # Otherwise require Bearer token
   179	    if (is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   180	      res$status <- 401
   181	      return(list(error = "Authorization http header missing."))
   182	    } else {
   183	      decoded_jwt <- jwt_decode_hmac(
   184	        str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "Bearer "),
   185	        secret = key
   186	      )
   187	      if (decoded_jwt$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   188	        res$status <- 401
   189	        return(list(error = "Token expired."))
   190	      } else {
   191	        req$user_id <- as.integer(decoded_jwt$user_id)
   192	        req$user_role <- decoded_jwt$user_role
   193	        plumber::forward()
   194	      }
   195	    }
   196	  }
   197	}

   199	#' Route-level 404 Not Found Handler (RFC 9457 compliant)
   200	#'
   201	#' Handles requests to non-existent routes/endpoints.
   202	#' This is separate from resource-level 404s handled by error_404.
   203	#'
   204	#' @param req Plumber request object
   205	#' @param res Plumber response object
   206	#' @return RFC 9457 problem details response
   207	notFoundHandler <- function(req, res) {
   208	  res$status <- 404
   209	  # Let the serializer set Content-Type so problem+json is emitted exactly once
   210	  # (a manual setHeader plus the serializer's own type yields a duplicate header).
   150	      - ./api/scripts:/app/scripts:ro
   151	      - ./api/layout/gene-network-fcose-layout.mjs:/app/layout/gene-network-fcose-layout.mjs:ro
   152	      - ./api/layout/package.json:/app/layout/package.json:ro
   153	      - ./api/layout/package-lock.json:/app/layout/package-lock.json:ro
   154	      - ./api/data:/app/data
   155	      - ./api/results:/app/results
   156	      - ./db/migrations:/app/db/migrations:ro
   157	      - api_cache:/app/cache
   158	      - mysql_backup:/backup:rw
   159	      - ./api/config.yml:/app/config.yml:ro
   160	      - ./api/version_spec.json:/app/version_spec.json
   161	      - ./api/start_sysndd_api.R:/app/start_sysndd_api.R
   162	    environment:
   163	      ENVIRONMENT: production
   164	      PASSWORD: ${PASSWORD}
   165	      SMTP_PASSWORD: ${SMTP_PASSWORD}
   166	      DB_POOL_SIZE: ${DB_POOL_SIZE:-5}
   167	      MIRAI_WORKERS: ${MIRAI_WORKERS:-2}
   168	      GEMINI_API_KEY: ${GEMINI_API_KEY:-}
   169	      # NCBI E-utilities identity/rate-limit (#494/#499): raises the per-IP EUtils
   170	      # cap from the anonymous 3 req/s to 10 req/s so publication ingestion and the
   171	      # publication_date_backfill do not 429. Inert when unset (anonymous is valid).
   172	      NCBI_API_KEY: ${NCBI_API_KEY:-}
   173	      NCBI_EUTILS_EMAIL: ${NCBI_EUTILS_EMAIL:-}
   174	      # CORS configuration: comma-separated list of allowed origins
   175	      # Critical for Firefox compatibility (issue #143)
   176	      CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS: ${CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS:-}
   177	      CACHE_VERSION: ${CACHE_VERSION:-3}
   178	      # #535 S6: per-caller throttle on the public clustering submit routes. Compose
   179	      # uses explicit env maps, so these must be passed through to be tunable via .env.
   180	      # ASYNC_PUBLIC_JOB_CAP is the global queue-depth backstop (invalid -> default 8).
   181	      ASYNC_PUBLIC_JOB_CAP: ${ASYNC_PUBLIC_JOB_CAP:-8}
   182	      CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX: ${CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX:-5}
   183	      CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS: ${CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS:-60}
   184	      CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED: ${CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED:-20000}
   185	      # Trusted reverse-proxy source CIDRs (comma-separated). Empty for the shipped
   186	      # single-Traefik direct-edge topology; set to the front-proxy CIDR(s) ONLY when an
   187	      # additional trusted proxy sits in front of Traefik (see 09-deployment.qmd).
   188	      CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS: ${CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS:-}
   189	      # OMIM download key for genemap2.txt (required for ontology/comparisons)
   190	      OMIM_DOWNLOAD_KEY: ${OMIM_DOWNLOAD_KEY}
   191	      # NDDScore release source; defaults match api/config.yml.
   192	      NDDSCORE_ZENODO_RECORD_ID: "${NDDSCORE_ZENODO_RECORD_ID:-20258027}"
   193	      NDDSCORE_ZENODO_API_BASE_URL: "${NDDSCORE_ZENODO_API_BASE_URL:-https://zenodo.org/api/records}"
   194	      # Database version surface (issue #22). Optional release-time injection;
   195	      # when set, the API refreshes the db_version row at startup. The migration
   196	      # seeds a baseline so the surface works even when these are unset.
   197	      DB_VERSION: "${DB_VERSION:-}"
   198	      DB_COMMIT: "${DB_COMMIT:-}"
   199	      # Auto-bootstrap public analysis snapshots on startup (#420). Default on;
   200	      # set to false to disable the post-migration enqueue of missing presets.
   201	      ANALYSIS_SNAPSHOT_BOOTSTRAP_ON_STARTUP: "${ANALYSIS_SNAPSHOT_BOOTSTRAP_ON_STARTUP:-true}"
   202	    networks:
   203	      - proxy
   204	      - backend
   205	    healthcheck:
   206	      test: ["CMD", "curl", "-sf", "http://localhost:7777/api/health/ready"]
   207	      interval: 30s
   208	      timeout: 10s
   209	      retries: 3
   210	      start_period: 60s
   211	    deploy:
   212	      resources:
   213	        limits:
   214	          memory: 4608M
   215	          cpus: '2.0'
   216	    develop:

   218	        - action: sync

   233	        - action: rebuild
   234	          path: ./api/renv.lock

   236	      - "traefik.enable=true"

   238	      - "traefik.http.routers.api.entrypoints=web"
   239	      - "traefik.http.routers.api.priority=100"
   240	      # #535 S6: strip client-supplied X-Forwarded-For *underscore aliases* so only
   241	      # Traefik's canonical (hyphenated) X-Forwarded-For chain reaches the API. Plumber
   242	      # folds `X_Forwarded_For` (and mixed `X-Forwarded_For` / `X_Forwarded-For`) into
   243	      # the SAME CGI field as the canonical header; without this an attacker could
   244	      # inject a rotating IP that collides with the proxy-owned value and defeats the
   245	      # per-caller submit throttle. Empty value = delete the header before forwarding.
   246	      - "traefik.http.middlewares.api-strip-xff-alias.headers.customRequestHeaders.X_Forwarded_For="
   247	      - "traefik.http.middlewares.api-strip-xff-alias.headers.customRequestHeaders.X-Forwarded_For="
   248	      - "traefik.http.middlewares.api-strip-xff-alias.headers.customRequestHeaders.X_Forwarded-For="
   249	      - "traefik.http.routers.api.middlewares=api-strip-xff-alias@docker"
   250	      - "traefik.http.services.api.loadbalancer.server.port=7777"

     1	# api/endpoints/authentication_endpoints.R
     2	#
     3	# This file contains all authentication-related endpoints extracted from the
     4	# original sysndd_plumber.R. It follows the Google R Style Guide conventions
     5	# where possible (e.g., two-space indentation, meaningful function names, etc.).
     6	#
     7	# Make sure to source any required helpers or libraries at the top if needed,
     8	# for example:
     9	# source("functions/database-functions.R", local = TRUE)
    10	
    11	# Note: All required modules (security.R, db-helpers.R, auth-service.R)
    12	# are sourced by start_sysndd_api.R before endpoints are loaded.
    13	# Functions are available in the global environment.

    15	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    16	## Authentication section
    17	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    18	
    19	#* User Signup
    20	#*
    21	#* This endpoint handles user signups. It validates the user's provided info
    22	#* (e.g., username, names, email, ORCID, terms agreement), and if valid, inserts
    23	#* a new user record. Then it sends a confirmation email to notify them of the
    24	#* pending request.
    25	#*
    26	#* # `Details`
    27	#* Checks if user input passes basic validations like name length, email format,
    28	#* etc. On success, the user is added to the database with `approved=0`, and a
    29	#* mail is sent to them. If any validation fails, returns an error.
    30	#*
    31	#* # `Return`
    32	#* Returns an error if data is invalid. Otherwise, sends a confirmation email
    33	#* and a success message.
    34	#*
    35	#* @tag authentication
    36	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
    37	#*
    38	#* @response 200 OK. The signup was successful; user added to DB, email sent.
    39	#* @response 400 Bad Request. If the JSON body is missing, malformed, or empty.
    40	#* @response 404 Not Found. Invalid registration data.
    41	#* @response 415 Unsupported Media Type. If the request is not JSON.
    42	#*
    43	#* @post signup
    44	function(req, res) {
    45	  content_type <- req$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE %||% req$CONTENT_TYPE %||% ""
    46	  media_type <- strsplit(tolower(content_type), ";", fixed = TRUE)[[1]][1]
    47	  if (media_type != "application/json") {
    48	    res$status <- 415
    49	    res$body <- "Content-Type must be application/json."
    50	    return(res)
    51	  }
    52	
    53	  signup_body <- tryCatch(
    54	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
    55	    error = function(e) NULL
    56	  )
    57	  required_fields <- c(
    58	    "user_name",
    59	    "first_name",
    60	    "family_name",
    61	    "email",
    62	    "orcid",
    63	    "comment",
    64	    "terms_agreed"
    65	  )
    66	  if (
    67	    is.null(signup_body) ||
    68	      length(signup_body) == 0 ||
    69	      !all(required_fields %in% names(signup_body))
    70	  ) {
    71	    res$status <- 400
    72	    res$body <- "Malformed or empty JSON body."
    73	    return(res)
    74	  }
    75	
    76	  required_fields_are_scalar_strings <- vapply(
    77	    required_fields,
    78	    function(field) {
    79	      value <- signup_body[[field]]
    80	      is.character(value) && length(value) == 1 && !is.na(value)
    81	    },
    82	    logical(1)
    83	  )
    84	  if (!all(required_fields_are_scalar_strings)) {
    85	    res$status <- 400
    86	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: each required field must be a single string value."
    87	    return(res)
    88	  }
    89	
    90	  # Reject control characters (CR/LF/tab) in any account field. Left unchecked,
    91	  # a CR/LF-bearing field is forged into log lines (the best-effort SMTP-failure
    92	  # logger below prints user_name verbatim) and into email headers once the value
    93	  # is emailed to the user/curators. Printable non-ASCII (accents) is allowed.
    94	  fields_have_control_chars <- vapply(
    95	    required_fields,
    96	    function(field) account_field_has_control_char(signup_body[[field]]),
    97	    logical(1)
    98	  )
    99	  if (any(fields_have_control_chars)) {
   100	    res$status <- 400
   101	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: fields must not contain control characters."
   102	    return(res)
   103	  }
   104	
   105	  # Gate the email through the hardened, anchored validator (not the permissive
   106	  # `.+@.+\\..+` shape used below): SMTP recipient grammar such as
   107	  # `<a@example.com> NOTIFY=SUCCESS` must not create an account whose approval
   108	  # credentials are then handed to smtp_send() as a malformed/injectable address.
   109	  if (!is_valid_email(signup_body[["email"]])) {
   110	    res$status <- 400
   111	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: invalid email address."
   112	    return(res)
   113	  }
   114	
   115	  user <- tibble::as_tibble(signup_body) %>%
   116	    dplyr::mutate(
   117	      terms_agreed = dplyr::case_when(
   118	        terms_agreed == "accepted" ~ "1",
   119	        TRUE ~ "0"
   120	      )
   121	    ) %>%
   122	    dplyr::select(
   123	      user_name,
   124	      first_name,
   125	      family_name,
   126	      email,
   127	      orcid,
   128	      comment,
   129	      terms_agreed
   130	    )
   131	
   132	  input_validation <- tidyr::pivot_longer(user, cols = dplyr::everything()) %>%
   133	    dplyr::mutate(
   134	      valid = dplyr::case_when(
   135	        name == "user_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 5 & nchar(value) <= 20),
   136	        name == "first_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 2 & nchar(value) <= 50),
   137	        name == "family_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 2 & nchar(value) <= 50),
   138	        name == "email" ~ stringr::str_detect(
   139	          value,
   140	          stringr::regex(".+@.+\\..+", dotall = TRUE)
   141	        ),
   142	        name == "orcid" ~ stringr::str_detect(
   143	          value,
   144	          stringr::regex("^(([0-9]{4})-){3}[0-9]{3}[0-9X]$")
   145	        ),
   146	        name == "comment" ~ (nchar(value) >= 10 & nchar(value) <= 250),
   147	        name == "terms_agreed" ~ (value == "1")
   148	      )
   149	    ) %>%
   150	    dplyr::mutate(all = "1") %>%
   151	    dplyr::select(all, valid) %>%
   152	    dplyr::group_by(all) %>%
   153	    dplyr::summarize(valid = as.logical(prod(valid)), .groups = "drop") %>%
   154	    dplyr::select(valid)
   155	
   156	  if (input_validation$valid) {
   157	    # Insert user into DB using parameterized query
   158	    # Build INSERT with explicit column names matching tibble structure
   159	    cols <- names(user)
   160	    placeholders <- paste(rep("?", length(cols)), collapse = ", ")
   161	    sql <- sprintf("INSERT INTO user (%s) VALUES (%s)", paste(cols, collapse = ", "), placeholders)
   162	    db_execute_statement(sql, unname(as.list(user)))
   163	
   164	    # Generate professional HTML email using template
   165	    email_html <- email_registration_request(
   166	      user_info = list(
   167	        user_name = user$user_name,
   168	        email = user$email,
   169	        first_name = user$first_name,
   170	        family_name = user$family_name
   171	      )
   172	    )
   173	
   174	    # The registration request is recorded once the user row is inserted above.
   175	    # The notification email is best-effort: a transient SMTP failure must not
   176	    # fail (or half-complete) the registration — the account already exists and
   177	    # is visible to admins for approval. Log loudly and continue with a 200.
   178	    tryCatch(
   179	      send_noreply_email(
   180	        email_body = email_html,
   181	        email_subject = "SysNDD Registration Request Received",
   182	        email_recipient = user$email,
   183	        email_blind_copy = "curator@sysndd.org",
   184	        html_content = TRUE
   185	      ),
   186	      error = function(e) {
   187	        message(sprintf(
   188	          "[signup] registration recorded for '%s' but notification email failed (non-fatal): %s",
   189	          user$user_name, conditionMessage(e)
   190	        ))
   191	      }
   192	    )
   193	  } else {
   194	    res$status <- 404
   195	    res$body <- "Please provide valid registration data."
   196	    return(res)
   197	  }
   198	}
   199	
   200	
   201	#* Authenticate a User with Login
   202	#*
   203	#* Credentials are submitted as a JSON body (POST) instead of query parameters
   204	#* so they never land in access logs, Traefik logs, or browser history.
   205	#*
   206	#* # `Details`
   207	#* Parses `user_name` and `password` from the JSON request body and delegates
   208	#* to `auth_signin`. Returns the JWT access token as a JSON string so the
   209	#* wire format is identical to the legacy `@get` handler — clients only need
   210	#* to switch HTTP method and payload location, not response parsing.
   211	#*
   212	#* # `Return`
   213	#* JWT string on success, error message otherwise.
   214	#*
   215	#* @tag authentication
   216	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
   217	#*
   218	#* @response 200 OK. Returns the JWT.
   219	#* @response 400 Bad Request. If JSON body is missing or malformed.
   220	#* @response 401 Unauthorized. If user or password is wrong or user not approved.
   221	#*
   222	#* @post authenticate
   223	function(req, res) {
   224	  # Parse credentials from JSON body (OWASP: secrets MUST NOT be in URLs)
   225	  body <- tryCatch(
   226	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   227	    error = function(e) list()
   228	  )
   229	  user_name <- body$user_name %||% ""
   230	  password <- body$password %||% ""
   231	
   232	  # Validate inputs before calling service
   233	  if (
   234	    nchar(user_name) < 5 || nchar(user_name) > 20 ||
   235	      nchar(password) < 5 || nchar(password) > 50
   236	  ) {
   237	    res$status <- 400
   238	    res$body <- "Please provide valid username and password."
   239	    return(res)
   240	  }
   241	
   242	  # Call auth service (returns structured response)
   243	  tryCatch(
   244	    {
   245	      result <- auth_signin(user_name, password, pool, dw)
   246	      # Return just the access token for backward compatibility with @get shape
   247	      result$access_token
   248	    },
   249	    error = function(e) {
   250	      res$status <- 401
   251	      res$body <- "User or password wrong."
   252	      return(res)
   253	    }
   254	  )
   255	}
   256	
   257	
   258	#* Authenticate a User (token check)
   259	#*
   260	#* This endpoint verifies the Authorization header for a valid JWT. If valid and
   261	#* not expired, returns the user data. Otherwise, returns an error.
   262	#*
   263	#* # `Details`
   264	#* Uses auth_verify service function to validate JWT token.
   265	#*
   266	#* # `Return`
   267	#* User info if token is valid; 401 otherwise.
   268	#*
   269	#* @tag authentication
   270	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
   271	#*
   272	#* @response 200 OK. Returns user_id, user_name, email, etc.
   273	#* @response 401 Unauthorized. If token is missing or invalid/expired.
   274	#*
   275	#* @get signin
   276	function(req, res) {
   277	  if (is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   278	    res$status <- 401
   279	    return(list(error = "Authorization http header missing."))
   280	  }
     1	# api/endpoints/user_endpoints.R

     4	# Functions (security.R, middleware.R, user-repository.R, services/*) are
     5	# sourced by start_sysndd_api.R before endpoints are loaded and are available
     6	# in the global environment.
     7	#
     8	# Thin authorization/delegation shell (#346): every `require_role()` gate and
     9	# the admin-target shield (`assert_not_targeting_admin()`, #5) live here;
    10	# request processing has moved to the `svc_`-prefixed functions in

    19	#* Retrieves a summary table of users based on role permissions.
    20	#* Admins see all users; Curators see only unapproved users; others are forbidden.
    21	#* Supports server-side filtering, sorting, and cursor pagination.
    22	#* @tag user
    23	#* @serializer json list(na="null")
    24	#* @param filter Filter string (e.g., "user_name:contains:john")
    25	#* @param sort Sort string (e.g., "+user_name" or "-email")
    26	#* @param page_after Cursor after which entries are shown (default: 0)
    27	#* @param page_size Page size in cursor pagination (default: "all")
    28	#* @param fspec Field specification for table columns
    29	#* @get table
    30	function(req, res, filter = "", sort = "+user_id", page_after = 0,
    31	         page_size = "all",
    32	         fspec = "user_id,user_name,email,user_role,approved,abbreviation,first_name,family_name,comment,created_at") {
    33	  require_role(req, res, "Curator")
    34	
    35	  svc_user_table_list(req, filter, sort, page_after, page_size, fspec)
    36	}
    37	
    38	#* Retrieves count statistics of all contributions for a specified user.
    39	#* Users can view their own contributions. Reviewer/Curator/Admin can view any user.
    40	#* @tag user
    41	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
    42	#* @get <user_id>/contributions
    43	function(req, res, user_id) {
    44	  if (as.integer(user_id) != req$user_id) {
    45	    require_role(req, res, "Reviewer")
    46	  }
    47	
    48	  svc_user_contributions(user_id)
    49	}

    51	#* Manages the approval status of a user application.
    52	#* Only Admin/Curator. If approved, sets user as approved=1, generates a password,
    53	#* sends mail, etc. If unapproved, removes user from DB.
    54	#* @tag user
    55	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
    56	#* @put approval
    57	function(req, res, user_id = 0, status_approval = FALSE) {
    58	  require_role(req, res, "Curator")
    59	
    60	  user_id_approval <- as.integer(user_id)
    61	  status_approval <- as.logical(status_approval)
    62	
    63	  user_table <- svc_user_fetch_for_approval(user_id_approval)
    64	
    65	  if (nrow(user_table) == 0) {
    66	    res$status <- 409
    67	    return(list(error = "User account does not exist."))
    68	  }
    69	
    70	  # SECURITY (#5): non-Administrator may not approve/reject a currently-Administrator target.
    71	  if (req$user_role != "Administrator") {
    72	    assert_not_targeting_admin(req$user_role, user_table$user_role)
    73	  }
    74	
    75	  svc_user_approval_apply(req, res, user_table, user_id_approval, status_approval)
    76	}

    80	#* @tag user

    82	function(req, res, user_id, role_assigned = "Viewer") {
    83	  require_role(req, res, "Curator")
    84	
    85	  user_id_role <- as.integer(user_id)
    86	  role_assigned <- as.character(role_assigned)
    87	
    88	  # SECURITY (#5): non-Administrator may not modify a currently-Administrator target.
    89	  if (req$user_role != "Administrator") {
    90	    assert_not_targeting_admin(req$user_role, user_current_roles(user_id_role, pool))
    91	  }
    92	
    93	  svc_user_change_role(req, res, user_id_role, role_assigned)
    94	}
