   116	#* Allows a user or an administrator to change the user's password.
   117	#* Validates old password, checks new password complexity, updates DB.
   118	#* Password input is accepted only via a JSON request body so secrets never
   119	#* appear in URLs or access logs.
   120	#* @tag user
   121	#* @put password/update
   122	function(req, res) {
   123	  content_type <- req$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE %||% req$CONTENT_TYPE %||% ""
   124	  media_type <- strsplit(tolower(content_type), ";", fixed = TRUE)[[1]][1]
   125	  if (media_type != "application/json") {
   126	    res$status <- 415
   127	    return(list(error = "Content-Type must be application/json."))
   128	  }
   129	
   130	  body <- tryCatch(
   131	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   132	    error = function(e) NULL
   133	  )
   134	  required_fields <- c("user_id_pass_change", "old_pass", "new_pass_1", "new_pass_2")
   135	  if (
   136	    is.null(body) ||
   137	      length(body) == 0 ||
   138	      !all(required_fields %in% names(body))
   139	  ) {
   140	    res$status <- 400
   141	    return(list(error = "Malformed or empty JSON body."))
   142	  }
   143	
   144	  is_scalar_string <- function(x) {
   145	    is.character(x) && length(x) == 1 && !is.na(x)
   146	  }
   147	
   148	  is_scalar_integerish <- function(x) {
   149	    if ((is.integer(x) || is.numeric(x)) && length(x) == 1 && !is.na(x) && is.finite(x)) {
   150	      return(x == floor(x))
   151	    }
   152	
   153	    if (is.character(x) && length(x) == 1 && !is.na(x)) {
   154	      return(grepl("^-?\\d+$", x))
   155	    }
   156	
   157	    FALSE
   158	  }
   159	
   160	  if (!is_scalar_integerish(body$user_id_pass_change)) {
   161	    res$status <- 400
   162	    return(list(error = "`user_id_pass_change` must be a scalar integer value."))
   163	  }
   164	
   165	  if (
   166	    !is_scalar_string(body$old_pass) ||
   167	      !is_scalar_string(body$new_pass_1) ||
   168	      !is_scalar_string(body$new_pass_2)
   169	  ) {
   170	    res$status <- 400
   171	    return(list(error = "`old_pass`, `new_pass_1`, and `new_pass_2` must each be scalar strings."))
   172	  }
   173	
   174	  svc_user_password_update(req, res, body)
   175	}
   176	
   177	#* Update User Profile (Self-Service)
   178	#* Allows authenticated users to update their own email and ORCID (self-service
   179	#* only). Validates email format and ORCID format (0000-0000-0000-000X).
   180	#* @tag user
   181	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
   182	#* @response 200 OK. Profile updated successfully.
   183	#* @response 400 Bad Request. Invalid email or ORCID format.
   184	#* @response 401 Unauthorized. Not authenticated.
   185	#* @put profile
   186	function(req, res) {
   187	  svc_user_profile_update(req, res)
   188	}
   189

   234	#* Bulk approve multiple users

   238	#* @serializer json list(na="null")

   241	function(req, res) {

     1	# Authentication Service Layer for SysNDD API
     2	# Provides business logic for signin, verify, and refresh operations
     3	#
     4	# Functions accept pool and config as parameters (dependency injection)
     5	# Uses verify_password from core/security.R for dual-hash support
     6	# Uses jose package for JWT encoding/decoding
     7	# Uses core/errors.R helpers for RFC 9457 errors
     8	
     9	#' Authenticate user and return JWT token
    10	#'
    11	#' Validates credentials against database, checks account status,
    12	#' and generates JWT token pair (access + refresh) on success.
    13	#'
    14	#' @param user_name Username to authenticate
    15	#' @param password Plain text password
    16	#' @param pool Database connection pool
    17	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
    18	#' @return List with access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, and user info
    19	#' @examples
    20	#' \dontrun{
    21	#' result <- auth_signin("johndoe", "password123", pool, config)
    22	#' # Returns: list(access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, user)
    23	#' }
    24	auth_signin <- function(user_name, password, pool, config) {
    25	  # Validate inputs
    26	  if (missing(user_name) || is.null(user_name) || nchar(trimws(user_name)) == 0) {
    27	    stop_for_bad_request("user_name is required")
    28	  }
    29	  if (missing(password) || is.null(password) || nchar(password) == 0) {
    30	    stop_for_bad_request("password is required")
    31	  }
    32	
    33	  # Look up user (include password for verification)
    34	  # Rename created_at to user_created so downstream JWT code works without warning
    35	  user <- pool %>%
    36	    tbl("user") %>%
    37	    filter(user_name == !!user_name) %>%
    38	    dplyr::rename(user_created = created_at) %>%
    39	    collect()
    40	
    41	  if (nrow(user) == 0) {
    42	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid username or password")
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  user <- user[1, ]
    46	
    47	  # Check account status (approved column: 1 = active, 0 = pending)
    48	  if (is.null(user$approved) || user$approved != 1) {
    49	    stop_for_unauthorized("Account is not active")
    50	  }
    51	
    52	  # Verify password using security.R helper (handles legacy + Argon2id)
    53	  if (!verify_password(user$password, password)) {
    54	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid username or password")
    55	  }
    56	
    57	  # Progressive password upgrade if needed
    58	  if (needs_upgrade(user$password)) {
    59	    upgrade_password(pool, user$user_id, password)
    60	  }
    61	
    62	  # Generate JWT token pair
    63	  token <- auth_generate_token(user, config)
    64	
    65	  logger::log_info("User signed in", user_id = user$user_id, user_name = user$user_name)
    66	
    67	  list(
    68	    access_token = token$access_token,
    69	    refresh_token = token$refresh_token,
    70	    token_type = "Bearer",
    71	    expires_in = config$token_expiry %||% 3600,
    72	    user = list(
    73	      user_id = user$user_id,
    74	      user_name = user$user_name,
    75	      user_role = user$user_role,
    76	      email = user$email
    77	    )
    78	  )
    79	}
    80	
    81	
    82	#' Verify JWT token and return user info
    83	#'
    84	#' Validates token signature and expiration without database lookup.
    85	#' Returns user claims if valid, signals error if invalid/expired.
    86	#'
    87	#' @param jwt JWT token string (without "Bearer " prefix)
    88	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret
    89	#' @return List with user info (user_id, user_name, email, user_role, etc.)
    90	#' @examples
    91	#' \dontrun{
    92	#' user_info <- auth_verify("eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5...", config)
    93	#' # Returns: list(user_id, user_name, email, user_role, ...)
    94	#' }
    95	auth_verify <- function(jwt, config) {
    96	  if (missing(jwt) || is.null(jwt) || nchar(jwt) == 0) {
    97	    stop_for_unauthorized("Token is required")
    98	  }
    99	
   100	  # Validate and decode token
   101	  user <- auth_validate_token(jwt, config)
   102	
   103	  if (is.null(user)) {
   104	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid or expired token")
   105	  }
   106	
   107	  # Check expiration
   108	  if (user$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   109	    stop_for_unauthorized("Token has expired")
   110	  }
   111	
   112	  # Return user info (excluding internal fields)
   113	  list(
   114	    user_id = user$user_id,
   115	    user_name = user$user_name,
   116	    email = user$email,
   117	    user_role = user$user_role,
   118	    user_created = user$user_created,
   119	    abbreviation = user$abbreviation,
   120	    orcid = user$orcid,
   121	    exp = user$exp
   122	  )
   123	}
   124	
   125	
   126	#' Refresh JWT token with new expiration
   127	#'
   128	#' Validates existing token and issues new token with extended expiry.
   129	#' Requires token to be valid (not expired).
   130	#'
   131	#' @param refresh_token Current JWT refresh token
   132	#' @param pool Database connection pool (unused but kept for consistency)
   133	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
   134	#' @return New JWT token string
   135	#' @examples
   136	#' \dontrun{
   137	#' new_token <- auth_refresh("eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5...", pool, config)
   138	#' # Returns: "eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5..."
   139	#' }
   140	auth_refresh <- function(refresh_token, pool, config) {
   141	  if (missing(refresh_token) || is.null(refresh_token) || nchar(refresh_token) == 0) {
   142	    stop_for_bad_request("refresh_token is required")
   143	  }
   144	
   145	  # Validate signature + decode the presented token.
   146	  claims <- auth_validate_token(refresh_token, config)
   147	  if (is.null(claims)) {
   148	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   149	  }
   150	  if (is.null(claims$exp) || claims$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   151	    stop_for_unauthorized("Refresh token has expired")
   152	  }
   153	
   154	  # #535 P0-2: a token that predates session-epoch support carries no `sepoch`.
   155	  # Reject it rather than treating it as epoch 0 — otherwise a pre-deploy
   156	  # (possibly compromised) token could be refreshed into a fresh epoch-0 token
   157	  # and renewed indefinitely. This forces exactly one post-deploy sign-in.
   158	  if (is.null(claims$sepoch) || length(claims$sepoch) != 1L) {
   159	    stop_for_unauthorized("Session predates revocation support. Please sign in again.")
   160	  }
   161	  token_epoch <- suppressWarnings(as.numeric(claims$sepoch))
   162	  if (is.na(token_epoch)) {
   163	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   164	  }
   165	
   166	  # Validate the subject id before querying.
   167	  uid <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(claims$user_id))
   168	  if (length(uid) != 1L || is.na(uid) || uid <= 0L) {
   169	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   170	  }
   171	
   172	  # #535 P0-2: read CURRENT account state, verify it, and sign the new token
   173	  # under a single row lock (`SELECT ... FOR UPDATE`) so the read-check-sign is
   174	  # serialized against any concurrent privilege/state mutation. Without the
   175	  # lock a refresh could read the pre-demotion row and then sign a stale-role
   176	  # token after the demotion commits (TOCTOU). Never trust the token's claims.
   177	  issue <- function(conn) {
   178	    user <- DBI::dbGetQuery(
   179	      conn,
   180	      "SELECT user_id, user_name, email, user_role, session_epoch,
   181	              created_at AS user_created, abbreviation, orcid, approved
   182	         FROM user WHERE user_id = ? FOR UPDATE",
   183	      params = list(uid)
   184	    )
   185	    if (nrow(user) == 0) {
   186	      stop_for_unauthorized("User no longer exists")
   187	    }
   188	    if (is.null(user$approved[1]) || is.na(user$approved[1]) || user$approved[1] != 1) {
   189	      stop_for_unauthorized("Account is not active")
   190	    }
   191	    current_epoch <- suppressWarnings(as.numeric(user$session_epoch[1]))
   192	    if (is.na(current_epoch) || token_epoch != current_epoch) {
   193	      stop_for_unauthorized("Session has been revoked. Please sign in again.")
   194	    }
   195	    # Mint with role + claim fields taken from the DB row (not the token).
   196	    auth_generate_token(user[1, ], config)$access_token
   197	  }
   198	
   199	  if (inherits(pool, "Pool")) {
   200	    # API path: hold the FOR UPDATE lock across signing in one transaction.
   201	    # dbWithTransaction commits on success and rolls back on ANY error —
   202	    # including a failure of the commit itself or an interrupt escaping
   203	    # issue() — so the connection is never returned to the pool with an open
   204	    # transaction / row lock.
   205	    conn <- pool::poolCheckout(pool)
   206	    on.exit(pool::poolReturn(conn), add = TRUE)
   207	    access_token <- DBI::dbWithTransaction(conn, issue(conn))
   208	  } else {
   209	    # Test / direct-connection path ONLY: the caller already owns the
   210	    # transaction (e.g. with_test_db_transaction). Production always passes a
   211	    # pool::Pool, so the FOR UPDATE lock is always inside an explicit
   212	    # transaction and is held through signing.
   213	    access_token <- issue(pool)
   214	  }
   215	
   216	  logger::log_info("Token refreshed", user_id = uid)
   217	
   218	  # Return just the access token (string format for backward compatibility)
   219	  access_token
   220	}
   221	
   222	
   223	#' Generate JWT token pair for user
   224	#'
   225	#' Internal helper to create access and refresh tokens with user claims.
   226	#' Uses jose::jwt_encode_hmac for HMAC-SHA256 signing.
   227	#'
   228	#' @param user User object or list with user_id, user_name, email, etc.
   229	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
   230	#' @return List with access_token and refresh_token
   231	auth_generate_token <- function(user, config) {
   232	  key <- charToRaw(config$secret)
   233	
   234	  # Create claim with user info
   235	  claim <- jose::jwt_claim(
   236	    user_id = user$user_id,
   237	    user_name = user$user_name,
   238	    email = user$email,
   239	    user_role = user$user_role,
   240	    user_created = user$user_created,
   241	    abbreviation = user$abbreviation,
   242	    orcid = user$orcid,
   243	    # #535 P0-2: bind the token to the user's current session epoch so a later
   244	    # privilege/state change (which increments session_epoch) invalidates refresh.
   245	    sepoch = user$session_epoch %||% 0,
   246	    iat = as.numeric(Sys.time()),
   247	    exp = as.numeric(Sys.time()) + (config$token_expiry %||% 3600)
   248	  )
   249	
   250	  # Encode JWT
   251	  token <- jose::jwt_encode_hmac(claim, secret = key)
   252	
   253	  # Return both access and refresh (same token for now, can be separated later)
   254	  list(
   255	    access_token = token,
   256	    refresh_token = token
   257	  )
   258	}
   259	
   260	
   160	      # Using [0-9] instead of \d for R compatibility
   161	      orcid_pattern <- "^[0-9]{4}-[0-9]{4}-[0-9]{4}-[0-9]{3}[0-9X]$"
   162	      if (!grepl(orcid_pattern, new_orcid, ignore.case = TRUE)) {
   163	        res$status <- 400
   164	        return(list(
   165	          error = "Invalid ORCID format. Expected: 0000-0000-0000-000X"
   166	        ))
   167	      }
   168	      # Normalize: uppercase X
   169	      updates$orcid <- toupper(new_orcid)
   170	      updated_fields <- c(updated_fields, "orcid")
   171	    }
   172	  }
   173	
   174	  # Check if there's anything to update
   175	  if (length(updates) == 0) {
   176	    res$status <- 400
   177	    return(list(error = "No valid fields provided for update."))
   178	  }
   179	
   180	  # Perform update using existing repository function
   181	  user_update(user_id, updates)
   182	
   183	  res$status <- 200
   184	  return(list(
   185	    message = "Profile updated successfully.",
   186	    updated_fields = updated_fields
   187	  ))
   188	}

   190	#' Best-effort, anti-enumeration password-reset request.
   191	#'
   192	#' Behind `POST /api/user/password/reset/request`. Delegates the actual
   193	#' anti-enumeration/SMTP-hardening logic to
   194	#' `process_password_reset_request()` (functions/user-endpoint-helpers.R).
   195	#'
   196	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$postBody`).
   197	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated with the shared response status).
   198	#' @return List response body.
   199	svc_user_password_reset_request <- function(req, res) {
   200	  # Parse email from JSON body (OWASP: sensitive data should not be in URLs)
   201	  body <- tryCatch(
   202	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   203	    error = function(e) list()
   204	  )
   205	  email_request <- body$email %||% ""
   206	
   207	  user_table <- pool %>%
   208	    tbl("user") %>%
   209	    collect()
   210	
   211	  result <- process_password_reset_request(email_request, user_table, dw)
   212	  res$status <- result$status
   213	  result$body
   214	}
   215	
   216	#' Complete a password reset given a signed, unexpired reset JWT.
   217	#'
   218	#' Behind `POST /api/user/password/reset/change`. Validates the bearer JWT's
   219	#' claims against the current DB row (rather than comparing JWT strings) so
   220	#' `jti`/`nbf` fields never cause a false mismatch.
   221	#'
   222	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$postBody`, `req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION`).
   223	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated on every path).
   224	#' @return List response body.
   225	svc_user_password_reset_change <- function(req, res) {
   226	  # Parse passwords from JSON body (OWASP: passwords MUST NOT be in URLs)
   227	  body <- tryCatch(
   228	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   229	    error = function(e) list()
   230	  )
   231	  new_pass_1 <- body$password %||% ""
   232	  new_pass_2 <- body$password_confirm %||% ""
   233	  jwt <- str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "Bearer ")
   234	  key <- charToRaw(dw$secret)
   235	
   236	  user_jwt <- jwt_decode_hmac(jwt, secret = key)
   237	  user_jwt$token_expired <- (user_jwt$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time()))
   238	
   239	  if (is.null(jwt) || user_jwt$token_expired) {
   240	    res$status <- 401
   241	    return(list(error = "Reset token expired."))
   242	  } else {
   243	    user_table <- pool %>%
   244	      tbl("user") %>%
   245	      collect() %>%
   246	      filter(user_id == user_jwt$user_id) %>%
   247	      mutate(hash = toString(md5(paste0(dw$salt, password)))) %>%
   248	      mutate(reset_posix = as.POSIXct(password_reset_date, tz = "UTC")) %>%
   249	      mutate(timestamp_iat = as.integer(reset_posix)) %>%
   250	      select(user_id, user_name, hash, email, timestamp_iat)
   251	
   252	    # Check user was found
   253	    if (nrow(user_table) == 0) {
   254	      res$status <- 404
   255	      return(list(error = "User not found."))
   256	    }
   257	
   258	    # Validate JWT claims against database values (instead of comparing JWT strings)
   259	    # This properly handles jti/nbf fields that are auto-generated
   260	    # Use first() to extract scalar values from tibble columns

   219	# TRUE when the classified candidate (family + canonical full IP) is inside one of the
   220	# trusted-proxy `cidrs`. IPv4 candidates match only IPv4 CIDRs/addresses and IPv6 only
   221	# IPv6 — evaluated on the CANONICAL address, never the /64 bucket key.
   222	.async_job_submit_ip_trusted <- function(family, canonical, cidrs) {
   223	  if (length(cidrs) == 0L || is.null(family) || is.na(family)) {
   224	    return(FALSE)
   225	  }
   226	  for (c in cidrs) {
   227	    c <- trimws(c)
   228	    cidr_is_v6 <- grepl(":", c, fixed = TRUE)
   229	    if (family == "v4" && !cidr_is_v6 && .async_job_submit_v4_match(canonical, c)) {
   230	      return(TRUE)
   231	    }
   232	    if (family == "v6" && cidr_is_v6 && .async_job_submit_v6_match(canonical, c)) {
   233	      return(TRUE)
   234	    }
   235	  }
   236	  FALSE
   237	}
   238	
   239	# TRUE when `c` is a syntactically valid IPv4/IPv6 CIDR or exact address.
   240	.async_job_submit_valid_cidr <- function(c) {
   241	  c <- trimws(c)
   242	  if (grepl(":", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   243	    if (grepl("/", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   244	      seg <- strsplit(c, "/", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   245	      bits <- if (length(seg) == 2L) suppressWarnings(as.integer(seg[[2]])) else NA_integer_
   246	      return(!is.na(bits) && bits >= 0L && bits <= 128L &&
   247	               !is.null(.async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(seg[[1]])))
   248	    }
   249	    return(!is.null(.async_job_submit_ipv6_hextets(c)))
   250	  }
   251	  if (grepl("/", c, fixed = TRUE)) {
   252	    seg <- strsplit(c, "/", fixed = TRUE)[[1]]
   253	    bits <- if (length(seg) == 2L) suppressWarnings(as.integer(seg[[2]])) else NA_integer_
   254	    return(!is.na(bits) && bits >= 0L && bits <= 32L && !is.na(.async_job_submit_ipv4_num(seg[[1]])))
   255	  }
   256	  !is.na(.async_job_submit_ipv4_num(c))
   257	}
   258	
   259	# Surface (but do not fail boot on) malformed trusted-proxy CIDRs: an invalid entry
   260	# simply never matches (safe — it trusts nothing), so log it for visibility.
   261	local({
   262	  bad <- Filter(function(c) !.async_job_submit_valid_cidr(c), CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS)
   263	  if (length(bad) > 0L && base::exists("log_warn", mode = "function")) {
   264	    log_warn(paste0(
   265	      "CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS has invalid entries (ignored): ",
   266	      paste(bad, collapse = ", ")
   267	    ))
   268	  }
   269	})
   270	
   271	#' Resolve the client fingerprint for submit throttling.
   272	#'
   273	#' Walks `X-Forwarded-For` RIGHT-TO-LEFT and returns the first address that is NOT a
   274	#' known trusted proxy (`CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS`). Our nearest proxy
   275	#' appends the address of the peer it actually saw at the RIGHT, so the first untrusted
   276	#' address from the right is the real client and is NOT spoofable: an attacker can put
   277	#' anything in the leftmost entries, but the rightmost hop it cannot forge is the peer
   278	#' our proxy observed. With the default empty trust set (single-Traefik direct edge)
   279	#' this is simply the rightmost hop. Each candidate must validate as an IP
   280	#' (`.async_job_submit_normalize_ip()`); non-IP tokens (header-alias injection, junk)
   281	#' are skipped. Falls back to a validated `REMOTE_ADDR`, then a constant. Never throws:
   282	#' crafted headers degrade to the `"unknown"` bucket, they cannot fail the request.
   283	#'
   284	#' @param req Plumber request object.
   285	#' @param trusted_cidrs Trusted reverse-proxy source CIDRs (default env).
   286	#' @return Character fingerprint (never empty).
   287	#' @export
   288	async_job_submit_fingerprint <- function(req,
   289	                                         trusted_cidrs = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS) {
   290	  xff <- tryCatch(req$HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR, error = function(e) NULL)
   291	  if (!is.null(xff) && length(xff) == 1L && nzchar(xff)) {
   292	    parts <- trimws(strsplit(as.character(xff), ",", fixed = TRUE)[[1]])
   293	    parts <- parts[nzchar(parts)]
   294	    for (i in rev(seq_along(parts))) {
   295	      p <- .async_job_submit_ip_classify(parts[[i]])
   296	      if (is.na(p$family)) next                                        # non-IP -> ignore
   297	      if (.async_job_submit_ip_trusted(p$family, p$canonical, trusted_cidrs)) next # our proxy
   298	      return(p$key)                                                    # first untrusted from right
   299	    }
   300	  }
   301	  addr <- .async_job_submit_normalize_ip(tryCatch(req$REMOTE_ADDR, error = function(e) NULL))
   302	  if (!is.na(addr)) {
   303	    return(addr)
   304	  }
   305	  "unknown"
   306	}
   307	
   308	# Reserved store keys (control-char prefix -> never a valid IP / "unknown", so they
   309	# cannot collide with a real fingerprint). The overflow bucket collectively throttles
   310	# brand-new callers once the store is saturated with ACTIVE callers; the sweep marker
   311	# time-gates the reclaim scan; the count marker holds the O(1) tracked-bucket count.
   312	.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY <- "\001overflow"
   313	.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY <- "\001sweep_at"
   314	.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY <- "\001count"
   315	
   316	# O(1) tracked-caller count (real fingerprints, EXCLUDING the shared overflow and the
   317	# reserved markers). Maintained on insert/reclaim so the hot path never scans the env.
   318	.async_job_submit_size <- function(store) {
   319	  if (base::exists(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)) {
   320	    base::get(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   321	  } else {
   322	    0L
   323	  }
   324	}
   325	
   326	.async_job_submit_size_add <- function(store, delta) {
   327	  assign(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY, .async_job_submit_size(store) + as.integer(delta), envir = store)
   328	}
   329	
   330	#' Reclaim store space by dropping ONLY fully-idle fingerprints (every timestamp aged
   331	#' out) — an active caller's window is never evicted. Sort-free (`names()`, not the
   332	#' sorting `ls()`), and time-gated to at most once per window so a rotation flood
   333	#' cannot force an O(n) scan on every request. Keeps the O(1) counter in sync.
   334	.async_job_submit_reclaim <- function(store, cutoff, now, window_s) {
   335	  sweep_at <- if (base::exists(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)) {
   336	    base::get(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   337	  } else {
   338	    -Inf
   339	  }
   340	  if ((now - sweep_at) < window_s) {
   341	    return(invisible(NULL))
   342	  }
   343	  reserved <- c(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_COUNT_KEY)
   344	  keys <- setdiff(names(store), reserved)
   345	  removed_real <- 0L
   346	  for (k in keys) {
   347	    ts <- base::get(k, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   348	    if (length(ts) == 0L || max(ts) <= cutoff) {
   349	      rm(list = k, envir = store)
   350	      if (!identical(k, .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY)) {
   351	        removed_real <- removed_real + 1L
   352	      }
   353	    }
   354	  }
   355	  assign(.CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_SWEEP_KEY, now, envir = store)
   356	  if (removed_real > 0L) {
   357	    .async_job_submit_size_add(store, -removed_real)
   358	  }
   359	  invisible(NULL)
   360	}
   361	
   362	#' Sliding-window per-caller submit rate limit.
   363	#'
   364	#' Pure except for the module-level `store`; the clock is injected so tests are
   365	#' deterministic. Records the attempt when allowed. Memory is bounded at `max_tracked`
   366	#' fingerprints: once the store is saturated with ACTIVE callers, a brand-new
   367	#' fingerprint is routed into a single shared overflow bucket (collectively throttled)
   368	#' rather than evicting a legitimate caller's window — so an attacker rotating
   369	#' X-Forwarded-For values can neither exhaust memory nor reset an innocent caller.
   370	#' Invalid `max_n`/`window_s` FAIL CLOSED (`stop()`): the admission guard maps the
   371	#' error to a 503, so an internal misconfiguration can never silently admit.
   372	#'
   373	#' @param fingerprint Caller fingerprint (see async_job_submit_fingerprint()).
   374	#' @param now Current epoch-seconds (injected for tests).
   375	#' @param max_n Max allowed submissions in the window.
   376	#' @param window_s Window length in seconds.
   377	#' @param store Environment mapping fingerprint -> recent timestamps.
   378	#' @param max_tracked Hard cap on distinct tracked fingerprints.
   379	#' @return list(allowed, retry_after, count).
   380	#' @export
   381	async_job_submit_rate_limit <- function(fingerprint,
   382	                                        now = as.numeric(Sys.time()),
   383	                                        max_n = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX,
   384	                                        window_s = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS,
   385	                                        store = .clustering_submit_history,
   386	                                        max_tracked = CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED) {
   387	  if (is.null(fingerprint) || length(fingerprint) != 1L || is.na(fingerprint) || !nzchar(fingerprint)) {
   388	    fingerprint <- "unknown"
   389	  }
   390	  # Invalid limiter parameters are an internal error, not a disable switch: fail CLOSED
   391	  # so the admission guard returns 503 THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE rather than silently admit.
   392	  if (length(max_n) != 1L || !is.finite(max_n) || max_n < 1L ||
   393	        length(window_s) != 1L || !is.finite(window_s) || window_s < 1L) {
   394	    stop("clustering submit throttle misconfigured: max_n and window_s must be finite and >= 1")
   395	  }
   396	  cutoff <- now - window_s
   397	  is_new <- !base::exists(fingerprint, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   398	  # Bound the store BEFORE recording a brand-new fingerprint.
   399	  if (is_new && .async_job_submit_size(store) >= max_tracked) {
   400	    .async_job_submit_reclaim(store, cutoff, now, window_s)
   401	    if (.async_job_submit_size(store) >= max_tracked) {
   402	      fingerprint <- .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY # saturated -> shared bucket
   403	      is_new <- !base::exists(fingerprint, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   404	    }
   405	  }
   406	  prev <- if (!is_new) {
   407	    base::get(fingerprint, envir = store, inherits = FALSE)
   408	  } else {
   409	    numeric(0)
   410	  }
   411	  recent <- prev[prev > cutoff]
   412	  if (length(recent) >= max_n) {
   413	    # The oldest in-window submission ages out at recent[1] + window_s.
   414	    retry_after <- max(1L, as.integer(ceiling((recent[[1]] + window_s) - now)))
   415	    assign(fingerprint, recent, envir = store) # persist the prune
   416	    return(list(allowed = FALSE, retry_after = retry_after, count = length(recent)))
   417	  }
   418	  assign(fingerprint, c(recent, now), envir = store)
   419	  # Count only real distinct callers (never the shared overflow) toward the bound.
   420	  if (is_new && !identical(fingerprint, .CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_OVERFLOW_KEY)) {
   421	    .async_job_submit_size_add(store, 1L)
   422	  }
   423	  list(allowed = TRUE, retry_after = 0L, count = length(recent) + 1L)
   424	}
   425	
   426	#' Admission guard for the public clustering submit routes.
   427	#'
   428	#' The single entry point both submit services call FIRST (before any DB/cache/
   429	#' duplicate work) so an abusive caller is rejected before it can do — or provoke —
   430	#' any expensive work. Derives the caller fingerprint, applies the per-caller
   431	#' throttle, and translates the decision to an HTTP response on `res`:
   432	#'   * allowed  -> `list(admitted = TRUE)` (caller proceeds)
   433	#'   * throttled-> `429` + `Retry-After`, `error = "RATE_LIMITED"`
   434	#'   * internal error -> **fail CLOSED** `503` + `Retry-After`,
   435	#'     `error = "THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE"` (a throttle bug must neither 500 the
   436	#'     endpoint nor silently admit an abusive caller).
   437	#'
   438	#' @param req Plumber request.
   439	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated in place on a block).
   440	#' @return list(admitted = TRUE) or list(admitted = FALSE, response = <payload>).
   441	#' @export
   442	# Emit the fail-closed 503 on a fresh `res`. Kept as one non-throwing helper so every
   443	# error/malformed-decision path routes through exactly one place.
   444	.async_job_submit_unavailable <- function(res) {
   445	  res$status <- 503L
   446	  res$setHeader("Retry-After", "5")
   447	  list(admitted = FALSE, response = list(
   448	    error = "THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE",
   449	    message = "Submission throttling is temporarily unavailable. Please retry shortly.",
   450	    retry_after = 5L
   451	  ))
   452	}
   453	
   454	async_job_submit_admission_guard <- function(req, res) {
   455	  decision <- tryCatch(
   456	    async_job_submit_rate_limit(async_job_submit_fingerprint(req)),
   457	    error = function(e) {
   458	      # Logging must never itself fail the request (log_warn may be absent in a
   459	      # library-light env, or a glue interpolation could throw) -> swallow it.
   460	      try(
   461	        if (base::exists("log_warn", mode = "function")) {
   462	          log_warn("clustering submit throttle failed (fail-closed 503): {conditionMessage(e)}")
   463	        },
   464	        silent = TRUE
   465	      )
   466	      NULL
   467	    }
   468	  )
   469	  # Fail CLOSED on a NULL OR malformed decision (schema-validate before use, so a bad
   470	  # shape can never reach setHeader() with an invalid value and 500 the endpoint).
   471	  valid <- is.list(decision) &&
   472	    length(decision$allowed) == 1L && is.logical(decision$allowed) && !is.na(decision$allowed)
   473	  if (!valid) {
   474	    return(.async_job_submit_unavailable(res))
   475	  }
   476	  if (!isTRUE(decision$allowed)) {
   477	    retry_after <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(decision$retry_after))
   478	    if (length(retry_after) != 1L || is.na(retry_after) || retry_after < 1L) {
   479	      retry_after <- 1L
   480	    }
   481	    res$status <- 429L
   482	    res$setHeader("Retry-After", as.character(retry_after))
   483	    return(list(admitted = FALSE, response = list(
   484	      error = "RATE_LIMITED",
   485	      message = "Too many analysis submissions from your client. Please retry shortly.",
   486	      retry_after = retry_after
   487	    )))
   488	  }
   489	  list(admitted = TRUE)
   490	}
   491	
   492	#' Reset the in-memory submit-throttle store (tests only).
   493	#' @export
   494	async_job_submit_rate_limit_reset <- function(store = .clustering_submit_history) {
   495	  rm(list = ls(envir = store, all.names = TRUE), envir = store)
   496	  invisible(NULL)
   497	}

    19	#* User Signup
    20	#*
    21	#* This endpoint handles user signups. It validates the user's provided info
    22	#* (e.g., username, names, email, ORCID, terms agreement), and if valid, inserts
    23	#* a new user record. Then it sends a confirmation email to notify them of the
    24	#* pending request.
    25	#*
    26	#* # `Details`
    27	#* Checks if user input passes basic validations like name length, email format,
    28	#* etc. On success, the user is added to the database with `approved=0`, and a
    29	#* mail is sent to them. If any validation fails, returns an error.
    30	#*
    31	#* # `Return`
    32	#* Returns an error if data is invalid. Otherwise, sends a confirmation email
    33	#* and a success message.
    34	#*
    35	#* @tag authentication
    36	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
    37	#*
    38	#* @response 200 OK. The signup was successful; user added to DB, email sent.
    39	#* @response 400 Bad Request. If the JSON body is missing, malformed, or empty.
    40	#* @response 404 Not Found. Invalid registration data.
    41	#* @response 415 Unsupported Media Type. If the request is not JSON.
    42	#*
    43	#* @post signup
    44	function(req, res) {
    45	  content_type <- req$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE %||% req$CONTENT_TYPE %||% ""
    46	  media_type <- strsplit(tolower(content_type), ";", fixed = TRUE)[[1]][1]
    47	  if (media_type != "application/json") {
    48	    res$status <- 415
    49	    res$body <- "Content-Type must be application/json."
    50	    return(res)
    51	  }
    52	
    53	  signup_body <- tryCatch(
    54	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
    55	    error = function(e) NULL
    56	  )
    57	  required_fields <- c(
    58	    "user_name",
    59	    "first_name",
    60	    "family_name",
    61	    "email",
    62	    "orcid",
    63	    "comment",
    64	    "terms_agreed"
    65	  )
    66	  if (
    67	    is.null(signup_body) ||
    68	      length(signup_body) == 0 ||
    69	      !all(required_fields %in% names(signup_body))
    70	  ) {
    71	    res$status <- 400
    72	    res$body <- "Malformed or empty JSON body."
    73	    return(res)
    74	  }
    75	
    76	  required_fields_are_scalar_strings <- vapply(
    77	    required_fields,
    78	    function(field) {
    79	      value <- signup_body[[field]]
    80	      is.character(value) && length(value) == 1 && !is.na(value)
    81	    },
    82	    logical(1)
    83	  )
    84	  if (!all(required_fields_are_scalar_strings)) {
    85	    res$status <- 400
    86	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: each required field must be a single string value."
    87	    return(res)
    88	  }
    89	
    90	  # Reject control characters (CR/LF/tab) in any account field. Left unchecked,
    91	  # a CR/LF-bearing field is forged into log lines (the best-effort SMTP-failure
    92	  # logger below prints user_name verbatim) and into email headers once the value
    93	  # is emailed to the user/curators. Printable non-ASCII (accents) is allowed.
    94	  fields_have_control_chars <- vapply(
    95	    required_fields,
    96	    function(field) account_field_has_control_char(signup_body[[field]]),
    97	    logical(1)
    98	  )
    99	  if (any(fields_have_control_chars)) {
   100	    res$status <- 400
   101	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: fields must not contain control characters."
   102	    return(res)
   103	  }
   104	
   105	  # Gate the email through the hardened, anchored validator (not the permissive
   106	  # `.+@.+\\..+` shape used below): SMTP recipient grammar such as
   107	  # `<a@example.com> NOTIFY=SUCCESS` must not create an account whose approval
   108	  # credentials are then handed to smtp_send() as a malformed/injectable address.
   109	  if (!is_valid_email(signup_body[["email"]])) {
   110	    res$status <- 400
   111	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: invalid email address."
   112	    return(res)
   113	  }
   114	
   115	  user <- tibble::as_tibble(signup_body) %>%
   116	    dplyr::mutate(
   117	      terms_agreed = dplyr::case_when(
   118	        terms_agreed == "accepted" ~ "1",
   119	        TRUE ~ "0"
   120	      )
   121	    ) %>%
   122	    dplyr::select(
   123	      user_name,
   124	      first_name,
   125	      family_name,
   126	      email,
   127	      orcid,
   128	      comment,
   129	      terms_agreed
   130	    )
   131	
   132	  input_validation <- tidyr::pivot_longer(user, cols = dplyr::everything()) %>%
   133	    dplyr::mutate(
   134	      valid = dplyr::case_when(
   135	        name == "user_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 5 & nchar(value) <= 20),
   136	        name == "first_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 2 & nchar(value) <= 50),
   137	        name == "family_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 2 & nchar(value) <= 50),
   138	        name == "email" ~ stringr::str_detect(
   139	          value,
   140	          stringr::regex(".+@.+\\..+", dotall = TRUE)
   141	        ),
   142	        name == "orcid" ~ stringr::str_detect(
   143	          value,
   144	          stringr::regex("^(([0-9]{4})-){3}[0-9]{3}[0-9X]$")
   145	        ),
   146	        name == "comment" ~ (nchar(value) >= 10 & nchar(value) <= 250),
   147	        name == "terms_agreed" ~ (value == "1")
   148	      )
   149	    ) %>%
   150	    dplyr::mutate(all = "1") %>%
   151	    dplyr::select(all, valid) %>%
   152	    dplyr::group_by(all) %>%
   153	    dplyr::summarize(valid = as.logical(prod(valid)), .groups = "drop") %>%
   154	    dplyr::select(valid)
   155	
   156	  if (input_validation$valid) {
   157	    # Insert user into DB using parameterized query
   158	    # Build INSERT with explicit column names matching tibble structure
   159	    cols <- names(user)
   160	    placeholders <- paste(rep("?", length(cols)), collapse = ", ")
   161	    sql <- sprintf("INSERT INTO user (%s) VALUES (%s)", paste(cols, collapse = ", "), placeholders)
   162	    db_execute_statement(sql, unname(as.list(user)))
   163	
   164	    # Generate professional HTML email using template
   165	    email_html <- email_registration_request(
   166	      user_info = list(
   167	        user_name = user$user_name,
   168	        email = user$email,
   169	        first_name = user$first_name,
   170	        family_name = user$family_name
   171	      )
   172	    )
   173	
   174	    # The registration request is recorded once the user row is inserted above.
   175	    # The notification email is best-effort: a transient SMTP failure must not
   176	    # fail (or half-complete) the registration — the account already exists and
   177	    # is visible to admins for approval. Log loudly and continue with a 200.
   178	    tryCatch(
   179	      send_noreply_email(
   180	        email_body = email_html,
   181	        email_subject = "SysNDD Registration Request Received",
   182	        email_recipient = user$email,
   183	        email_blind_copy = "curator@sysndd.org",
   184	        html_content = TRUE
   185	      ),
   186	      error = function(e) {
   187	        message(sprintf(
   188	          "[signup] registration recorded for '%s' but notification email failed (non-fatal): %s",
   189	          user$user_name, conditionMessage(e)
   190	        ))
   191	      }
   192	    )
   193	  } else {
   194	    res$status <- 404
   195	    res$body <- "Please provide valid registration data."
   196	    return(res)
   197	  }
   198	}

   200	
   201	#* Authenticate a User with Login
   202	#*
   203	#* Credentials are submitted as a JSON body (POST) instead of query parameters
   204	#* so they never land in access logs, Traefik logs, or browser history.
   205	#*
   206	#* # `Details`
   207	#* Parses `user_name` and `password` from the JSON request body and delegates
   208	#* to `auth_signin`. Returns the JWT access token as a JSON string so the
   209	#* wire format is identical to the legacy `@get` handler — clients only need
   210	#* to switch HTTP method and payload location, not response parsing.
   211	#*
   212	#* # `Return`
   213	#* JWT string on success, error message otherwise.
   214	#*
   215	#* @tag authentication
   216	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
   217	#*
   218	#* @response 200 OK. Returns the JWT.
   219	#* @response 400 Bad Request. If JSON body is missing or malformed.
   220	#* @response 401 Unauthorized. If user or password is wrong or user not approved.
   221	#*
   222	#* @post authenticate
   223	function(req, res) {
   224	  # Parse credentials from JSON body (OWASP: secrets MUST NOT be in URLs)
   225	  body <- tryCatch(
   226	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   227	    error = function(e) list()
   228	  )
   229	  user_name <- body$user_name %||% ""
   230	  password <- body$password %||% ""
   231	
   232	  # Validate inputs before calling service
   233	  if (
   234	    nchar(user_name) < 5 || nchar(user_name) > 20 ||
   235	      nchar(password) < 5 || nchar(password) > 50
   236	  ) {
   237	    res$status <- 400
   238	    res$body <- "Please provide valid username and password."
   239	    return(res)
   240	  }
   241	
   242	  # Call auth service (returns structured response)
   243	  tryCatch(
   244	    {
   245	      result <- auth_signin(user_name, password, pool, dw)
   246	      # Return just the access token for backward compatibility with @get shape
   247	      result$access_token
   248	    },
   249	    error = function(e) {
   250	      res$status <- 401
   251	      res$body <- "User or password wrong."
   252	      return(res)
   253	    }
   254	  )
   255	}
   256	
   257	
   258	#* Authenticate a User (token check)
   259	#*
   260	#* This endpoint verifies the Authorization header for a valid JWT. If valid and
     1	# Authentication Service Layer for SysNDD API
     2	# Provides business logic for signin, verify, and refresh operations
     3	#
     4	# Functions accept pool and config as parameters (dependency injection)
     5	# Uses verify_password from core/security.R for dual-hash support
     6	# Uses jose package for JWT encoding/decoding
     7	# Uses core/errors.R helpers for RFC 9457 errors
     8	
     9	#' Authenticate user and return JWT token
    10	#'
    11	#' Validates credentials against database, checks account status,
    12	#' and generates JWT token pair (access + refresh) on success.
    13	#'
    14	#' @param user_name Username to authenticate
    15	#' @param password Plain text password
    16	#' @param pool Database connection pool
    17	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
    18	#' @return List with access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, and user info
    19	#' @examples
    20	#' \dontrun{
    21	#' result <- auth_signin("johndoe", "password123", pool, config)
    22	#' # Returns: list(access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, user)
    23	#' }
    24	auth_signin <- function(user_name, password, pool, config) {
    25	  # Validate inputs
    26	  if (missing(user_name) || is.null(user_name) || nchar(trimws(user_name)) == 0) {
    27	    stop_for_bad_request("user_name is required")
    28	  }
    29	  if (missing(password) || is.null(password) || nchar(password) == 0) {
    30	    stop_for_bad_request("password is required")
    31	  }
    32	
    33	  # Look up user (include password for verification)
    34	  # Rename created_at to user_created so downstream JWT code works without warning
    35	  user <- pool %>%
    36	    tbl("user") %>%
    37	    filter(user_name == !!user_name) %>%
    38	    dplyr::rename(user_created = created_at) %>%
    39	    collect()
    40	
    41	  if (nrow(user) == 0) {
    42	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid username or password")
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  user <- user[1, ]
    46	
    47	  # Check account status (approved column: 1 = active, 0 = pending)
    48	  if (is.null(user$approved) || user$approved != 1) {
    49	    stop_for_unauthorized("Account is not active")
    50	  }
    51	
    52	  # Verify password using security.R helper (handles legacy + Argon2id)
    53	  if (!verify_password(user$password, password)) {
    54	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid username or password")
    55	  }
    56	
    57	  # Progressive password upgrade if needed
    58	  if (needs_upgrade(user$password)) {
    59	    upgrade_password(pool, user$user_id, password)
    60	  }
    61	
    62	  # Generate JWT token pair
    63	  token <- auth_generate_token(user, config)
    64	
    65	  logger::log_info("User signed in", user_id = user$user_id, user_name = user$user_name)
    66	
    67	  list(
    68	    access_token = token$access_token,
    69	    refresh_token = token$refresh_token,
    70	    token_type = "Bearer",
    71	    expires_in = config$token_expiry %||% 3600,
    72	    user = list(
    73	      user_id = user$user_id,
    74	      user_name = user$user_name,
    75	      user_role = user$user_role,
    76	      email = user$email
    77	    )
    78	  )
    79	}
    80	
    81	
    82	#' Verify JWT token and return user info
    83	#'
    84	#' Validates token signature and expiration without database lookup.
    85	#' Returns user claims if valid, signals error if invalid/expired.
    86	#'
    87	#' @param jwt JWT token string (without "Bearer " prefix)
    88	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret
    89	#' @return List with user info (user_id, user_name, email, user_role, etc.)
    90	#' @examples
    91	#' \dontrun{
    92	#' user_info <- auth_verify("eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5...", config)
    93	#' # Returns: list(user_id, user_name, email, user_role, ...)
    94	#' }
    95	auth_verify <- function(jwt, config) {
    96	  if (missing(jwt) || is.null(jwt) || nchar(jwt) == 0) {
    97	    stop_for_unauthorized("Token is required")
    98	  }
    99	
   100	  # Validate and decode token
   101	  user <- auth_validate_token(jwt, config)
   102	
   103	  if (is.null(user)) {
   104	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid or expired token")
   105	  }
   106	
   107	  # Check expiration
   108	  if (user$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   109	    stop_for_unauthorized("Token has expired")
   110	  }
   111	
   112	  # Return user info (excluding internal fields)
   113	  list(
   114	    user_id = user$user_id,
   115	    user_name = user$user_name,
   116	    email = user$email,
   117	    user_role = user$user_role,
   118	    user_created = user$user_created,
   119	    abbreviation = user$abbreviation,
   120	    orcid = user$orcid,
   121	    exp = user$exp
   122	  )
   123	}
   124	
   125	
   126	#' Refresh JWT token with new expiration
   127	#'
   128	#' Validates existing token and issues new token with extended expiry.
   129	#' Requires token to be valid (not expired).
   130	#'
   131	#' @param refresh_token Current JWT refresh token
   132	#' @param pool Database connection pool (unused but kept for consistency)
   133	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
   134	#' @return New JWT token string
   135	#' @examples
   136	#' \dontrun{
   137	#' new_token <- auth_refresh("eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5...", pool, config)
   138	#' # Returns: "eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5..."
   139	#' }
   140	auth_refresh <- function(refresh_token, pool, config) {
   141	  if (missing(refresh_token) || is.null(refresh_token) || nchar(refresh_token) == 0) {
   142	    stop_for_bad_request("refresh_token is required")
   143	  }
   144	
   145	  # Validate signature + decode the presented token.
   146	  claims <- auth_validate_token(refresh_token, config)
   147	  if (is.null(claims)) {
   148	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   149	  }
   150	  if (is.null(claims$exp) || claims$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   151	    stop_for_unauthorized("Refresh token has expired")
   152	  }
   153	
   154	  # #535 P0-2: a token that predates session-epoch support carries no `sepoch`.
   155	  # Reject it rather than treating it as epoch 0 — otherwise a pre-deploy
   156	  # (possibly compromised) token could be refreshed into a fresh epoch-0 token
   157	  # and renewed indefinitely. This forces exactly one post-deploy sign-in.
   158	  if (is.null(claims$sepoch) || length(claims$sepoch) != 1L) {
   159	    stop_for_unauthorized("Session predates revocation support. Please sign in again.")
   160	  }
   161	  token_epoch <- suppressWarnings(as.numeric(claims$sepoch))
   162	  if (is.na(token_epoch)) {
   163	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   164	  }
   165	
   166	  # Validate the subject id before querying.
   167	  uid <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(claims$user_id))
   168	  if (length(uid) != 1L || is.na(uid) || uid <= 0L) {
   169	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   170	  }
   171	
   172	  # #535 P0-2: read CURRENT account state, verify it, and sign the new token
   173	  # under a single row lock (`SELECT ... FOR UPDATE`) so the read-check-sign is
   174	  # serialized against any concurrent privilege/state mutation. Without the
   175	  # lock a refresh could read the pre-demotion row and then sign a stale-role
   176	  # token after the demotion commits (TOCTOU). Never trust the token's claims.
   177	  issue <- function(conn) {
   178	    user <- DBI::dbGetQuery(
   179	      conn,
   180	      "SELECT user_id, user_name, email, user_role, session_epoch,
   181	              created_at AS user_created, abbreviation, orcid, approved
   182	         FROM user WHERE user_id = ? FOR UPDATE",
   183	      params = list(uid)
   184	    )
   185	    if (nrow(user) == 0) {
   186	      stop_for_unauthorized("User no longer exists")
   187	    }
   188	    if (is.null(user$approved[1]) || is.na(user$approved[1]) || user$approved[1] != 1) {
   189	      stop_for_unauthorized("Account is not active")
   190	    }
   191	    current_epoch <- suppressWarnings(as.numeric(user$session_epoch[1]))
   192	    if (is.na(current_epoch) || token_epoch != current_epoch) {
   193	      stop_for_unauthorized("Session has been revoked. Please sign in again.")
   194	    }
   195	    # Mint with role + claim fields taken from the DB row (not the token).
   196	    auth_generate_token(user[1, ], config)$access_token
   197	  }
   198	
   199	  if (inherits(pool, "Pool")) {
   200	    # API path: hold the FOR UPDATE lock across signing in one transaction.
   201	    # dbWithTransaction commits on success and rolls back on ANY error —
   202	    # including a failure of the commit itself or an interrupt escaping
   203	    # issue() — so the connection is never returned to the pool with an open
   204	    # transaction / row lock.
   205	    conn <- pool::poolCheckout(pool)
   206	    on.exit(pool::poolReturn(conn), add = TRUE)
   207	    access_token <- DBI::dbWithTransaction(conn, issue(conn))
   208	  } else {
   209	    # Test / direct-connection path ONLY: the caller already owns the
   210	    # transaction (e.g. with_test_db_transaction). Production always passes a
   211	    # pool::Pool, so the FOR UPDATE lock is always inside an explicit
   212	    # transaction and is held through signing.
   213	    access_token <- issue(pool)
   214	  }
   215	
   216	  logger::log_info("Token refreshed", user_id = uid)
   217	
   218	  # Return just the access token (string format for backward compatibility)
   219	  access_token
   220	}
     1	# api/services/user-account-endpoint-service.R
     2	#
     3	# Endpoint service for the account-mutation routes in
     4	# endpoints/user_endpoints.R: approval, role change, delete, and the
     5	# Administrator bulk-field update. `require_role()` gates and the
     6	# admin-target shield (`assert_not_targeting_admin()`, #5) stay in the
     7	# endpoint shells; these `svc_` functions hold the request-processing logic
     8	# behind them.
     9	
    10	#' Fetch the approval-relevant columns for a single target user.
    11	#'
    12	#' Used by the `PUT /api/user/approval` shell before the existence check and
    13	#' admin-target shield.
    14	#'
    15	#' @param user_id_approval Integer target user id.
    16	#' @return Zero- or one-row tibble.
    17	svc_user_fetch_for_approval <- function(user_id_approval) {
    18	  pool %>%
    19	    tbl("user") %>%
    20	    select(user_id, user_name, approved, first_name, family_name, email, user_role) %>%
    21	    filter(user_id == user_id_approval) %>%
    22	    collect()
    23	}
    24	
    25	#' Approve or reject a pending user application.
    26	#'
    27	#' Behind `PUT /api/user/approval`, called after the shell has already
    28	#' fetched `user_table` (existence-checked) and cleared the admin-target
    29	#' shield.
    30	#'
    31	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$user_id` for the audit log line).
    32	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated on already-active/email-failure paths).
    33	#' @param user_table Single-row tibble for the target user.
    34	#' @param user_id_approval Integer target user id.
    35	#' @param status_approval Logical: `TRUE` approves, `FALSE` rejects.
    36	#' @return List response body.
    37	svc_user_approval_apply <- function(req, res, user_table, user_id_approval, status_approval) {
    38	  # Early return: already approved
    39	  if (as.logical(user_table$approved[1])) {
    40	    res$status <- 409
    41	    return(list(error = "User account already active."))
    42	  }
    43	
    44	  # Handle rejection (simpler path first)
    45	  if (!status_approval) {
    46	    db_execute_statement(
    47	      "DELETE FROM user WHERE user_id = ?",
    48	      list(user_id_approval)
    49	    )
    50	    log_info("User rejected and deleted: user_id={user_id_approval}, by={req$user_id}")
    51	    return(list(message = "User application rejected.", user_id = user_id_approval))
    52	  }
    53	
    54	  # Handle approval
    55	  user_password <- random_password()
    56	  user_initials <- generate_initials(
    57	    user_table$first_name,
    58	    user_table$family_name
    59	  )
    60	
    61	  # Hash password with Argon2id before storing
    62	  hashed_password <- hash_password(user_password)
    63	
    64	  # Update user approval status, password, and abbreviation
    65	  user_update(user_id_approval, list(approved = 1, abbreviation = user_initials))
    66	  user_update_password(user_id_approval, hashed_password)
    67	
    68	  # Sanitize the stored user_name before logging: a legacy row predating the
    69	  # signup control-char guard could otherwise forge log lines (#535 S8).
    70	  log_info("User approved: user_id={user_id_approval}, user_name={sanitize_log_value(user_table$user_name)}, by={req$user_id}")
    71	
    72	  # Generate and send email with error handling
    73	  email_result <- tryCatch({
    74	    email_html <- email_account_approved(
    75	      user_name = user_table$user_name,
    76	      temp_password = user_password,
    77	      login_url = paste0(dw$base_url, "/Login")
    78	    )
    79	
    80	    # The approval email carries the temporary password; deliver it to the USER
    81	    # ONLY. BCCing it to the shared curator mailbox would let any reader there
    82	    # sign in as the newly approved user (#535 S8).
    83	    send_noreply_email(
    84	      email_body = email_html,
    85	      email_subject = "Welcome to SysNDD - Your Account Has Been Approved!",
    86	      email_recipient = user_table$email,
    87	      html_content = TRUE
    88	    )
    89	
    90	    list(success = TRUE)
    91	  }, error = function(e) {
    92	    log_error("Email send failed for user_id={user_id_approval}: {e$message}")
    93	    list(success = FALSE, error = e$message)
    94	  })
    95	
    96	  # Return response with email status
    97	  if (email_result$success) {
    98	    return(list(
    99	      message = "User approved successfully.",
   100	      user_id = user_id_approval,
   101	      user_name = user_table$user_name,
   102	      email_sent = TRUE
   103	    ))
   104	  } else {
   105	    # User is approved but email failed - alert curator
   106	    res$status <- 200
   107	    return(list(
   108	      message = "User approved but email delivery failed. Please contact user manually.",
   109	      user_id = user_id_approval,
   110	      user_name = user_table$user_name,
   111	      email = user_table$email,
   112	      email_sent = FALSE,
   113	      email_error = email_result$error
   114	    ))
   115	  }
   116	}
   117	
   118	#' Apply a role assignment once permission tiering has been decided.
   119	#'
   120	#' Behind `PUT /api/user/change_role`, called after the shell's admin-target
   121	#' shield check.
   122	#'
   123	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$user_role`).
   124	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated on the 403 path).
   125	#' @param user_id_role Integer target user id.
   126	#' @param role_assigned Character role to assign.
   127	#' @return List response body, or nothing (Plumber default) on success.
   128	svc_user_change_role <- function(req, res, user_id_role, role_assigned) {
   129	  if (req$user_role == "Administrator") {
   130	    # Admin can assign any role
   131	    user_update(user_id_role, list(user_role = role_assigned))
   132	  } else if (role_assigned %in% c("Curator", "Reviewer", "Viewer")) {
   133	    # Curator can assign non-Administrator roles
   134	    user_update(user_id_role, list(user_role = role_assigned))
   135	  } else {
   136	    res$status <- 403
   137	    return(list(error = "Insufficient rights. Curators cannot assign Administrator role."))
   138	  }
   139	}

   141	#' Delete a user account by id.
   142	#'
   143	#' Behind `DELETE /api/user/delete` (Administrator-only; no admin-target
   144	#' shield needed since only Administrators can reach this route).
   145	#'
   146	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated on every non-200 path).
   147	#' @param user_id Target user id (character/integer, as received from Plumber).
   148	#' @return List response body.
   149	svc_user_delete <- function(res, user_id) {
   150	  user_id <- as.integer(user_id)
   151	
   152	  if (!is.numeric(user_id) || user_id <= 0) {
   153	    res$status <- 400
   154	    return(list(error = "Invalid user_id provided."))
   155	  }
   156	
   157	  # Check if user exists
   158	  exist_result <- db_execute_query(
   159	    "SELECT COUNT(*) as count FROM user WHERE user_id = ?",
   160	    list(user_id)
   161	  )
   162	
   163	  if (exist_result$count == 0) {
   164	    res$status <- 404
   165	    return(list(error = "User not found."))
   166	  }
   167	
   168	  # Delete user
   169	  delete_result <- tryCatch(
   170	    {
   171	      db_execute_statement(
   172	        "DELETE FROM user WHERE user_id = ?",
   173	        list(user_id)
   174	      )
   175	    },
   176	    error = function(e) {
   177	      NULL
   178	    }
   179	  )

   190	#' Best-effort, anti-enumeration password-reset request.
   191	#'
   192	#' Behind `POST /api/user/password/reset/request`. Delegates the actual
   193	#' anti-enumeration/SMTP-hardening logic to
   194	#' `process_password_reset_request()` (functions/user-endpoint-helpers.R).
   195	#'
   196	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$postBody`).
   197	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated with the shared response status).
   198	#' @return List response body.
   199	svc_user_password_reset_request <- function(req, res) {
   200	  # Parse email from JSON body (OWASP: sensitive data should not be in URLs)
   201	  body <- tryCatch(
   202	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   203	    error = function(e) list()
   204	  )
   205	  email_request <- body$email %||% ""
   206	
   207	  user_table <- pool %>%
   208	    tbl("user") %>%
   209	    collect()
   210	
   211	  result <- process_password_reset_request(email_request, user_table, dw)
   212	  res$status <- result$status
   213	  result$body
   214	}

   216	#' Complete a password reset given a signed, unexpired reset JWT.
   217	#'
   218	#' Behind `POST /api/user/password/reset/change`. Validates the bearer JWT's
   219	#' claims against the current DB row (rather than comparing JWT strings) so
   220	#' `jti`/`nbf` fields never cause a false mismatch.
   221	#'
   222	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$postBody`, `req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION`).
   223	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated on every path).
   224	#' @return List response body.
   225	svc_user_password_reset_change <- function(req, res) {
   226	  # Parse passwords from JSON body (OWASP: passwords MUST NOT be in URLs)
   227	  body <- tryCatch(
   228	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   229	    error = function(e) list()
   230	  )
   231	  new_pass_1 <- body$password %||% ""
   232	  new_pass_2 <- body$password_confirm %||% ""
   233	  jwt <- str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "Bearer ")
   234	  key <- charToRaw(dw$secret)
   235	
   236	  user_jwt <- jwt_decode_hmac(jwt, secret = key)
   237	  user_jwt$token_expired <- (user_jwt$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time()))
   238	
   239	  if (is.null(jwt) || user_jwt$token_expired) {
   240	    res$status <- 401
   241	    return(list(error = "Reset token expired."))
   242	  } else {
   243	    user_table <- pool %>%
   244	      tbl("user") %>%
   245	      collect() %>%
   246	      filter(user_id == user_jwt$user_id) %>%
   247	      mutate(hash = toString(md5(paste0(dw$salt, password)))) %>%
   248	      mutate(reset_posix = as.POSIXct(password_reset_date, tz = "UTC")) %>%
   249	      mutate(timestamp_iat = as.integer(reset_posix)) %>%
   250	      select(user_id, user_name, hash, email, timestamp_iat)
     1	# api/functions/user-endpoint-helpers.R
     2	
     3	#' Shared password complexity rule for the change and reset flows
     4	#'
     5	#' A candidate password must be longer than 7 characters and contain at least
     6	#' one lowercase letter, one uppercase letter, one digit, and one of the
     7	#' permitted special characters (`!@#$%^&*`).
     8	#'
     9	#' @param password Candidate password string.
    10	#' @return `TRUE` when the password satisfies every rule, otherwise `FALSE`.
    11	#' @export
    12	password_meets_complexity <- function(password) {
    13	  nchar(password) > 7 &&
    14	    grepl("[a-z]", password) &&
    15	    grepl("[A-Z]", password) &&
    16	    grepl("\\d", password) &&
    17	    grepl("[!@#$%^&*]", password)
    18	}
    19	
    20	#' Validate a new-password pair for the change/reset flows
    21	#'
    22	#' Confirms the new password and its confirmation match, optionally differ from
    23	#' the current password (password-change flow only), and satisfy the shared
    24	#' complexity rule. The reset flow has no current password and omits `old_pass`.
    25	#'
    26	#' @param new_pass_1 The proposed new password.
    27	#' @param new_pass_2 The confirmation of the new password.
    28	#' @param old_pass Optional current password. When supplied, the new password
    29	#'   must differ from it; the reset flow passes `NULL`.
    30	#' @return `TRUE` when the pair is valid, otherwise `FALSE`.
    31	#' @export
    32	new_password_valid <- function(new_pass_1, new_pass_2, old_pass = NULL) {
    33	  (new_pass_1 == new_pass_2) &&
    34	    (is.null(old_pass) || new_pass_1 != old_pass) &&
    35	    password_meets_complexity(new_pass_1)
    36	}
    37	
    38	#' Process a password-reset REQUEST (email a one-time reset link, best-effort)
    39	#'
    40	#' Pure, side-effect-injectable core of `POST /api/user/password/reset/request`.
    41	#' The handler collects the `user` table and delegates here so the flow can be
    42	#' unit-tested without a live SMTP relay or database.
    43	#'
    44	#' Behaviour (see `test-unit-password-reset-request.R`):
    45	#' - Syntactically invalid email -> `400` (a client input error, not enumeration).
    46	#' - Any other outcome -> a SINGLE generic `200` response, whether or not the
    47	#'   email matches an account and whether or not the mail is delivered. This
    48	#'   makes the endpoint impossible to use for account enumeration.
    49	#' - Email delivery is BEST-EFFORT: a send failure (most commonly an SMTP
    50	#'   outage) is logged loudly and swallowed, so the endpoint never returns a
    51	#'   `500`. This mirrors the signup (#470) and admin-approval email hardening;
    52	#'   the reset flow was previously the only email path that let an SMTP error
    53	#'   propagate as an opaque error to a locked-out user.
    54	#'
    55	#' The reset-token semantics (JWT claim, `md5(salt+password)` fingerprint,
    56	#' `password_reset_date` stamp, `iat`/`exp`) are byte-identical to the historic
    57	#' inline handler so the sibling `POST .../password/reset/change` still
    58	#' validates tokens minted here.
    59	#'
    60	#' @param email_request Raw email string from the request body.
    61	#' @param user_table Collected `user` table tibble (needs `user_id`,
    62	#'   `user_name`, `email`, `password`).
    63	#' @param dw Config object (`secret`, `salt`, `refresh`, `base_url`).
    64	#' @param send_email Mailer, injectable for tests. Defaults to
    65	#'   `send_noreply_email`.
    66	#' @param update_reset_date Reset-date writer, injectable for tests. Defaults to
    67	#'   stamping `password_reset_date` via `user_update`.
    68	#' @return `list(status = <int>, body = <list>)` for the handler to emit.
    69	#' @export
    70	process_password_reset_request <- function(
    71	  email_request,
    72	  user_table,
    73	  dw,
    74	  send_email = send_noreply_email,
    75	  update_reset_date = function(user_id, ts) {
    76	    user_update(user_id, list(password_reset_date = as.character(ts)))
    77	  }
    78	) {
    79	  generic_ok <- list(
    80	    status = 200L,
    81	    body = list(
    82	      message = paste0(
    83	        "If an account exists for that email address, ",
    84	        "a password reset link has been sent."
    85	      )
    86	    )
    87	  )
    88	
    89	  if (!is_valid_email(email_request)) {
    90	    return(list(status = 400L, body = list(error = "Invalid Parameter Value Error.")))
    91	  }
    92	
    93	  # Case-insensitive lookup, first match only. Emails are unique in practice,
    94	  # but a case-only collision must not produce a vector-valued JWT claim.
    95	  matched <- user_table %>%
    96	    dplyr::mutate(email_lower = stringr::str_to_lower(.data$email)) %>%
    97	    dplyr::filter(.data$email_lower == stringr::str_to_lower(email_request)) %>%
    98	    dplyr::slice(1L)
    99	
   100	  if (nrow(matched) == 0L) {
   101	    return(generic_ok) # unknown email: identical generic response
   102	  }
   103	
   104	  # Known account: mint the reset token, stamp the reset date, and email the
   105	  # link. The whole block is best-effort — any failure (SMTP outage, transient
   106	  # DB error) is logged and swallowed so the caller always receives `generic_ok`
   107	  # and the endpoint never 500s.
   108	  tryCatch(
   109	    {
   110	      ts <- Sys.time()
   111	      key <- charToRaw(
   112	        if (is.list(dw$secret)) as.character(dw$secret[[1]]) else as.character(dw$secret)
   113	      )
   114	
   115	      update_reset_date(matched$user_id, ts)
   116	
   117	      claim <- jose::jwt_claim(
   118	        user_id = matched$user_id,
   119	        user_name = matched$user_name,
   120	        email = matched$email,
   121	        hash = toString(md5(paste0(dw$salt, matched$password))),
   122	        iat = as.integer(ts),
   123	        exp = as.integer(ts) + dw$refresh
   124	      )
   125	      jwt <- jose::jwt_encode_hmac(claim, secret = key)
   126	      reset_url <- paste0(dw$base_url, "/PasswordReset/", jwt)
   127	
   128	      email_html <- email_password_reset(
   129	        reset_url = reset_url,
   130	        user_name = matched$user_name,
   131	        expiry_minutes = round(dw$refresh / 60)
   132	      )
   133	
   134	      send_email(
   135	        email_body = email_html,
   136	        email_subject = "Reset Your SysNDD Password",
   137	        email_recipient = matched$email,
   138	        html_content = TRUE
   139	      )
   140	    },

     1	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
     2	# api/bootstrap/load_modules.R
     3	#
     4	# Part of the Phase D.D6 extract-bootstrap refactor.
     5	#
     6	# Loads every R source file required by the running API into the
     7	# global environment, in the correct order:
     8	#   1. functions/* (repositories, helpers, clients, etc.)
     9	#   2. core/* (security, errors, responses, middleware, filters)
    10	#   3. services/* (transactional orchestration)
    11	#
    12	# Source order matters. Repository functions are loaded BEFORE
    13	# services so that any `svc_`/`service_`-prefixed function in
    14	# services/* can still call the underlying repository helpers.
    15	# (A service that accidentally drops its prefix will shadow the
    16	# repository function — see CLAUDE.md.)
    17	#
    18	# Mirai daemon workers do NOT use this module. They re-source a
    19	# hand-picked subset of functions/* via `everywhere({...})` in
    20	# api/bootstrap/setup_workers.R. Changes here do not automatically
    21	# propagate to workers — update setup_workers.R as well when a
    22	# function file is needed inside a daemon.
    23	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    24	
    25	#' Source a file into .GlobalEnv with a helpful error if missing.
    26	#'
    27	#' `source(..., local = FALSE)` puts the bindings into the global
    28	#' environment — that is what endpoint files expect at runtime.
    29	#' Top-level `source("...", local = TRUE)` in start_sysndd_api.R
    30	#' previously had the same effect by accident of being at the top
    31	#' level of the script; here we make the intent explicit.
    32	#'
    33	#' @param path Relative path from api/ to the source file.
    34	#' @noRd
    35	.bootstrap_source <- function(path) {
    36	  if (!file.exists(path)) {
    37	    stop(sprintf("bootstrap: source file not found: %s", path))
    38	  }
    39	  source(path, local = FALSE)
    40	  invisible(NULL)
    41	}

    25	#' @param pool The shared DBI pool; closed by the exit hook.
    26	#' @param logging_temp_file Path to the Plumber access log file; the
    27	#'   postroute hook passes this to `log_message_to_db()` so entries
    28	#'   can be correlated with the on-disk logs.
    29	#' @return A Plumber router ready to be started with `pr_run()`.
    30	#' @export
    31	bootstrap_mount_endpoints <- function(api_spec, pool, logging_temp_file) {
    32	
    33	  # Named closure for the exit hook so the pool reference travels
    34	  # via closure instead of via a global lookup.
    35	  cleanupHook <- function(pr) {
    36	    pr %>%
    37	      plumber::pr_hook("exit", function() {
    38	        pool::poolClose(pool)
    39	        message("Disconnected from DB")
    40	        mirai::daemons(0) # Shutdown mirai daemon pool
    41	        message("Shutdown mirai daemon pool")
    42	      })
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  # Build a mounted endpoint sub-router that inherits the API's RFC 9457 error
    46	  # and 404 handling. Plumber does NOT propagate the root router's error/404
    47	  # handlers to mounted sub-routers (each router keeps its own), so a thrown
    48	  # classed error (e.g. stop_for_bad_request() -> error_400) or an unknown
    49	  # sub-path would otherwise fall back to plumber's default opaque
    50	  # `{"error":"500 ..."}` / `{"error":"404 ..."}` instead of being mapped to the
    51	  # correct status + problem+json by errorHandler / notFoundHandler. Attaching
    52	  # them here keeps error and not-found responses consistent across every
    53	  # /api/<subpath>. Static guard: tests/testthat/test-unit-endpoint-error-handler.R
    54	  mount_endpoint <- function(file) {
    55	    plumber::pr(file) %>%
    56	      plumber::pr_set_error(errorHandler) %>%
    57	      plumber::pr_set_404(notFoundHandler)
    58	  }
    59	
    60	  plumber::pr() %>%
    61	    # Install error handler middleware
    62	    plumber::pr_set_error(errorHandler) %>%
    63	    # Install 404 handler for non-existent routes (RFC 9457 compliant)
    64	    plumber::pr_set_404(notFoundHandler) %>%
    65	    # Insert doc info in pr_set_api_spec
    66	    plumber::pr_set_api_spec(function(spec) {
    67	      # Read version info from version_spec.json
    68	      version_info <- jsonlite::fromJSON("version_spec.json")
    69	      spec$info$title <- version_info$title
    70	      spec$info$description <- version_info$description
    71	      spec$info$version <- version_info$version
    72	
    73	      if (!is.null(version_info$contact)) {
    74	        spec$info$contact <- version_info$contact
    75	      }
    76	      if (!is.null(version_info$license)) {
    77	        spec$info$license <- version_info$license
    78	      }
    79	
    80	      spec$components$securitySchemes$bearerAuth$type <- "http"
    81	      spec$components$securitySchemes$bearerAuth$scheme <- "bearer"
    82	      spec$components$securitySchemes$bearerAuth$bearerFormat <- "JWT"
    83	      spec$security[[1]]$bearerAuth <- ""
    84	
    85	      # Insert example requests from your api_spec.json (optional)
    86	      spec <- update_api_spec_examples(spec, api_spec)
    87	
    88	      # Enhance with modular schemas and standard error responses
    89	      spec <- enhance_openapi_spec(
    90	        spec,
    91	        config_dir = "config/openapi",
    92	        add_error_responses = TRUE,
    93	        public_paths = c(
    94	          "/api/health", "/api/version", "/api/about",
    95	          "/api/seo/routes", "/api/seo/gene", "/api/seo/entity", "/api/seo/static",
    96	          "/__docs__", "/__swagger__"
    97	        )
    98	      )
    99	
   100	      spec
   101	    }) %>%
   102	    ####################################################################
   103	    # Attach filters
   104	    ####################################################################
   105	    plumber::pr_filter("cors", corsFilter) %>%
   106	    plumber::pr_filter("require_auth", require_auth) %>%
   107	    ####################################################################
   108	    # Attach exit hook
   109	    ####################################################################
   110	    cleanupHook() %>%
   111	    ####################################################################
   112	    # Mount health endpoint for Docker HEALTHCHECK
   113	    ####################################################################
   114	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/health", mount_endpoint("endpoints/health_endpoints.R")) %>%
   115	    ####################################################################
   116	    # Mount version endpoint for API version discovery
   117	    ####################################################################
   118	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/version", mount_endpoint("endpoints/version_endpoints.R")) %>%
   119	    ####################################################################
   120	    # Mount each endpoint file at /api/<subpath>
   121	    ####################################################################

   123	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/review", mount_endpoint("endpoints/review_endpoints.R")) %>%

   141	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/auth", mount_endpoint("endpoints/authentication_endpoints.R")) %>%
   142	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/about", mount_endpoint("endpoints/about_endpoints.R")) %>%
   143	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/seo", mount_endpoint("endpoints/seo_endpoints.R")) %>%
   144	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/admin/analysis", mount_endpoint("endpoints/admin_analysis_snapshot_endpoints.R")) %>%
   145	    plumber::pr_mount("/api/admin/ontology", mount_endpoint("endpoints/admin_ontology_mapping_endpoints.R")) %>%

     1	# Authentication and Authorization Middleware for SysNDD API
     2	# Provides centralized JWT validation and role-based access control via Plumber filters
     3	#
     4	# Usage:
     5	#   source("core/middleware.R")
     6	#   pr_filter("require_auth", require_auth)
     7	#
     8	# Exports:
     9	#   - require_auth: Filter for JWT validation and user context attachment
    10	#   - require_role: Helper function for endpoint-level role enforcement
    11	#   - AUTH_ALLOWLIST: Public endpoints that bypass authentication

    13	library(jose)

    17	# Public endpoints that bypass authentication
    18	# These endpoints are accessible without Bearer tokens
    19	AUTH_ALLOWLIST <- c(

    21	  "/api/entity/hash",
    22	  "/api/jobs/clustering/submit",
