    55	
    56	#' Authentication Filter
    57	#'
    58	#' Validates JWT tokens for protected endpoints. Implements allowlist pattern
    59	#' for public endpoints and provides public read access for GET requests.
    60	#'
    61	#' Authentication flow:
    62	#' 1. OPTIONS requests (CORS preflight) -> forward
    63	#' 2. Paths in AUTH_ALLOWLIST -> forward
    64	#' 3. GET requests without auth -> forward (public read access)
    65	#' 4. All other requests -> require valid Bearer token
    66	#'
    67	#' On successful authentication, attaches to req object:
    68	#' - req$user_id: Numeric user ID
    69	#' - req$user_role: String user role (Viewer, Reviewer, Curator, Administrator)
    70	#' - req$user_name: String user name
    71	#'
    72	#' @param req Plumber request object
    73	#' @param res Plumber response object
    74	#' @return Forwards to next filter/endpoint on success, returns 401 error on failure
    75	#'
    76	#' @examples
    77	#' \dontrun{
    78	#' pr_filter("require_auth", require_auth)
    79	#' }
    80	require_auth <- function(req, res) {
    81	  # OPTIONS requests (CORS preflight) always forward
    82	  if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "OPTIONS") {
    83	    log_debug("require_auth: OPTIONS request, forwarding")
    84	    return(plumber::forward())
    85	  }
    86	
    87	  # Check if path is in allowlist (public endpoints)
    88	  if (req$PATH_INFO %in% AUTH_ALLOWLIST) {
    89	    log_debug("require_auth: Path in allowlist, forwarding", path = req$PATH_INFO)
    90	    return(plumber::forward())
    91	  }
    92	
    93	  # GET requests without auth get public read access
    94	  if (req$REQUEST_METHOD == "GET" && is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
    95	    log_debug("require_auth: GET without auth, forwarding (public read)")
    96	    return(plumber::forward())
    97	  }
    98	
    99	  # All other cases require authentication
   100	  if (is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   101	    log_warn("require_auth: Missing authorization header",
   102	             method = req$REQUEST_METHOD,
   103	             path = req$PATH_INFO)
   104	    res$status <- 401
   105	    stop(error_unauthorized("Authorization header missing. Please provide a Bearer token."))
   106	  }
   107	
   108	  # Extract and validate Bearer token
   109	  token <- stringr::str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "^Bearer\\s+")
   110	
   111	  # Decode JWT using global secret (dw$secret is approved global)
   112	  key <- charToRaw(if (is.list(dw$secret)) as.character(dw$secret[[1]]) else as.character(dw$secret))
   113	
   114	  tryCatch({
   115	    user <- jose::jwt_decode_hmac(token, secret = key)
   116	
   117	    # Check token expiration
   118	    if (!is.null(user$exp) && user$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   119	      log_warn("require_auth: Token expired", user_id = user$user_id)
   120	      res$status <- 401

exec

     2	#
     3	# This file contains all authentication-related endpoints extracted from the
     4	# original sysndd_plumber.R. It follows the Google R Style Guide conventions
     5	# where possible (e.g., two-space indentation, meaningful function names, etc.).
     6	#

     8	# for example:
     9	# source("functions/database-functions.R", local = TRUE)
    10	
    11	# Note: All required modules (security.R, db-helpers.R, auth-service.R)
    12	# are sourced by start_sysndd_api.R before endpoints are loaded.
    13	# Functions are available in the global environment.

    19	#* User Signup
    20	#*
    21	#* This endpoint handles user signups. It validates the user's provided info
    22	#* (e.g., username, names, email, ORCID, terms agreement), and if valid, inserts
    23	#* a new user record. Then it sends a confirmation email to notify them of the
    24	#* pending request.
    25	#*
    26	#* # `Details`
    27	#* Checks if user input passes basic validations like name length, email format,
    28	#* etc. On success, the user is added to the database with `approved=0`, and a
    29	#* mail is sent to them. If any validation fails, returns an error.
    30	#*
    31	#* # `Return`
    32	#* Returns an error if data is invalid. Otherwise, sends a confirmation email
    33	#* and a success message.
    34	#*
    35	#* @tag authentication
    36	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
    37	#*
    38	#* @response 200 OK. The signup was successful; user added to DB, email sent.
    39	#* @response 400 Bad Request. If the JSON body is missing, malformed, or empty.
    40	#* @response 404 Not Found. Invalid registration data.
    41	#* @response 415 Unsupported Media Type. If the request is not JSON.
    42	#*
    43	#* @post signup
    44	function(req, res) {
    45	  content_type <- req$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE %||% req$CONTENT_TYPE %||% ""
    46	  media_type <- strsplit(tolower(content_type), ";", fixed = TRUE)[[1]][1]
    47	  if (media_type != "application/json") {
    48	    res$status <- 415
    49	    res$body <- "Content-Type must be application/json."
    50	    return(res)
    51	  }
    52	
    53	  signup_body <- tryCatch(
    54	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
    55	    error = function(e) NULL
    56	  )
    57	  required_fields <- c(
    58	    "user_name",
    59	    "first_name",
    60	    "family_name",
    61	    "email",
    62	    "orcid",
    63	    "comment",
    64	    "terms_agreed"
    65	  )
    66	  if (
    67	    is.null(signup_body) ||
    68	      length(signup_body) == 0 ||
    69	      !all(required_fields %in% names(signup_body))
    70	  ) {
    71	    res$status <- 400
    72	    res$body <- "Malformed or empty JSON body."
    73	    return(res)
    74	  }
    75	
    76	  required_fields_are_scalar_strings <- vapply(
    77	    required_fields,
    78	    function(field) {
    79	      value <- signup_body[[field]]
    80	      is.character(value) && length(value) == 1 && !is.na(value)
    81	    },
    82	    logical(1)
    83	  )
    84	  if (!all(required_fields_are_scalar_strings)) {
    85	    res$status <- 400
    86	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: each required field must be a single string value."
    87	    return(res)
    88	  }
    89	
    90	  # Reject control characters (CR/LF/tab) in any account field. Left unchecked,
    91	  # a CR/LF-bearing field is forged into log lines (the best-effort SMTP-failure
    92	  # logger below prints user_name verbatim) and into email headers once the value
    93	  # is emailed to the user/curators. Printable non-ASCII (accents) is allowed.
    94	  fields_have_control_chars <- vapply(
    95	    required_fields,
    96	    function(field) account_field_has_control_char(signup_body[[field]]),
    97	    logical(1)
    98	  )
    99	  if (any(fields_have_control_chars)) {
   100	    res$status <- 400
   101	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: fields must not contain control characters."
   102	    return(res)
   103	  }
   104	
   105	  # Gate the email through the hardened, anchored validator (not the permissive
   106	  # `.+@.+\\..+` shape used below): SMTP recipient grammar such as
   107	  # `<a@example.com> NOTIFY=SUCCESS` must not create an account whose approval
   108	  # credentials are then handed to smtp_send() as a malformed/injectable address.
   109	  if (!is_valid_email(signup_body[["email"]])) {
   110	    res$status <- 400
   111	    res$body <- "Malformed JSON body: invalid email address."
   112	    return(res)
   113	  }
   114	
   115	  user <- tibble::as_tibble(signup_body) %>%
   116	    dplyr::mutate(
   117	      terms_agreed = dplyr::case_when(
   118	        terms_agreed == "accepted" ~ "1",
   119	        TRUE ~ "0"
   120	      )
   121	    ) %>%
   122	    dplyr::select(
   123	      user_name,
   124	      first_name,
   125	      family_name,
   126	      email,
   127	      orcid,
   128	      comment,
   129	      terms_agreed
   130	    )
   131	
   132	  input_validation <- tidyr::pivot_longer(user, cols = dplyr::everything()) %>%
   133	    dplyr::mutate(
   134	      valid = dplyr::case_when(
   135	        name == "user_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 5 & nchar(value) <= 20),
   136	        name == "first_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 2 & nchar(value) <= 50),
   137	        name == "family_name" ~ (nchar(value) >= 2 & nchar(value) <= 50),
   138	        name == "email" ~ stringr::str_detect(
   139	          value,
   140	          stringr::regex(".+@.+\\..+", dotall = TRUE)
   141	        ),
   142	        name == "orcid" ~ stringr::str_detect(
   143	          value,
   144	          stringr::regex("^(([0-9]{4})-){3}[0-9]{3}[0-9X]$")
   145	        ),
   146	        name == "comment" ~ (nchar(value) >= 10 & nchar(value) <= 250),
   147	        name == "terms_agreed" ~ (value == "1")
   148	      )
   149	    ) %>%
   150	    dplyr::mutate(all = "1") %>%
   151	    dplyr::select(all, valid) %>%
   152	    dplyr::group_by(all) %>%
   153	    dplyr::summarize(valid = as.logical(prod(valid)), .groups = "drop") %>%
   154	    dplyr::select(valid)
   155	
   156	  if (input_validation$valid) {
   157	    # Insert user into DB using parameterized query
   158	    # Build INSERT with explicit column names matching tibble structure
   159	    cols <- names(user)
   160	    placeholders <- paste(rep("?", length(cols)), collapse = ", ")
   161	    sql <- sprintf("INSERT INTO user (%s) VALUES (%s)", paste(cols, collapse = ", "), placeholders)
   162	    db_execute_statement(sql, unname(as.list(user)))
   163	
   164	    # Generate professional HTML email using template
   165	    email_html <- email_registration_request(
   166	      user_info = list(
   167	        user_name = user$user_name,
   168	        email = user$email,
   169	        first_name = user$first_name,
   170	        family_name = user$family_name
   171	      )
   172	    )
   173	
   174	    # The registration request is recorded once the user row is inserted above.
   175	    # The notification email is best-effort: a transient SMTP failure must not
   176	    # fail (or half-complete) the registration — the account already exists and
   177	    # is visible to admins for approval. Log loudly and continue with a 200.
   178	    tryCatch(
   179	      send_noreply_email(
   180	        email_body = email_html,
   181	        email_subject = "SysNDD Registration Request Received",
   182	        email_recipient = user$email,
   183	        email_blind_copy = "curator@sysndd.org",
   184	        html_content = TRUE
   185	      ),
   186	      error = function(e) {
   187	        message(sprintf(
   188	          "[signup] registration recorded for '%s' but notification email failed (non-fatal): %s",
   189	          user$user_name, conditionMessage(e)
   190	        ))
   191	      }
   192	    )
   193	  } else {
   194	    res$status <- 404
   195	    res$body <- "Please provide valid registration data."
   196	    return(res)
   197	  }
   198	}

   201	#* Authenticate a User with Login
   202	#*
   203	#* Credentials are submitted as a JSON body (POST) instead of query parameters
   204	#* so they never land in access logs, Traefik logs, or browser history.
   205	#*
   206	#* # `Details`
   207	#* Parses `user_name` and `password` from the JSON request body and delegates
   208	#* to `auth_signin`. Returns the JWT access token as a JSON string so the
   209	#* wire format is identical to the legacy `@get` handler — clients only need
   210	#* to switch HTTP method and payload location, not response parsing.
   211	#*
   212	#* # `Return`
   213	#* JWT string on success, error message otherwise.
   214	#*
   215	#* @tag authentication
   216	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
   217	#*
   218	#* @response 200 OK. Returns the JWT.
   219	#* @response 400 Bad Request. If JSON body is missing or malformed.
   220	#* @response 401 Unauthorized. If user or password is wrong or user not approved.
   221	#*
   222	#* @post authenticate
   223	function(req, res) {
   224	  # Parse credentials from JSON body (OWASP: secrets MUST NOT be in URLs)
   225	  body <- tryCatch(
   226	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   227	    error = function(e) list()
   228	  )
   229	  user_name <- body$user_name %||% ""
   230	  password <- body$password %||% ""
   231	
   232	  # Validate inputs before calling service
   233	  if (
   234	    nchar(user_name) < 5 || nchar(user_name) > 20 ||
   235	      nchar(password) < 5 || nchar(password) > 50
   236	  ) {
   237	    res$status <- 400
   238	    res$body <- "Please provide valid username and password."
   239	    return(res)
   240	  }
   241	
   242	  # Call auth service (returns structured response)
   243	  tryCatch(
   244	    {
   245	      result <- auth_signin(user_name, password, pool, dw)
   246	      # Return just the access token for backward compatibility with @get shape
   247	      result$access_token
   248	    },
   249	    error = function(e) {
   250	      res$status <- 401
   251	      res$body <- "User or password wrong."
   252	      return(res)
   253	    }
   254	  )
   255	}

   258	#* Authenticate a User (token check)
   259	#*
   260	#* This endpoint verifies the Authorization header for a valid JWT. If valid and
   261	#* not expired, returns the user data. Otherwise, returns an error.
   262	#*
   263	#* # `Details`
   264	#* Uses auth_verify service function to validate JWT token.
   265	#*
   266	#* # `Return`
   267	#* User info if token is valid; 401 otherwise.
   268	#*
   269	#* @tag authentication
   270	#* @serializer json list(na="string")
   271	#*
   272	#* @response 200 OK. Returns user_id, user_name, email, etc.
   273	#* @response 401 Unauthorized. If token is missing or invalid/expired.
   274	#*
   275	#* @get signin
   276	function(req, res) {
   277	  if (is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   278	    res$status <- 401
   279	    return(list(error = "Authorization http header missing."))
   280	  }
   281	
   282	  jwt <- str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "Bearer ")
   283	
   284	  tryCatch(
   285	    {
   286	      # Call auth_verify service function
   287	      auth_verify(jwt, dw)
   288	    },
   289	    error = function(e) {
   290	      res$status <- 401
   291	      return(list(error = "Authentication not successful."))
   292	    }
   293	  )

   180	  # Perform update using existing repository function
   181	  user_update(user_id, updates)
   182	
   183	  res$status <- 200
   184	  return(list(
   185	    message = "Profile updated successfully.",
   186	    updated_fields = updated_fields
   187	  ))
   188	}
   189	
   190	#' Best-effort, anti-enumeration password-reset request.
   191	#'
   192	#' Behind `POST /api/user/password/reset/request`. Delegates the actual
   193	#' anti-enumeration/SMTP-hardening logic to
   194	#' `process_password_reset_request()` (functions/user-endpoint-helpers.R).
   195	#'
   196	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$postBody`).
   197	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated with the shared response status).
   198	#' @return List response body.
   199	svc_user_password_reset_request <- function(req, res) {
   200	  # Parse email from JSON body (OWASP: sensitive data should not be in URLs)
   201	  body <- tryCatch(
   202	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   203	    error = function(e) list()
   204	  )
   205	  email_request <- body$email %||% ""
   206	
   207	  user_table <- pool %>%
   208	    tbl("user") %>%
   209	    collect()
   210	
   211	  result <- process_password_reset_request(email_request, user_table, dw)
   212	  res$status <- result$status
   213	  result$body
   214	}
   215	
   216	#' Complete a password reset given a signed, unexpired reset JWT.
   217	#'
   218	#' Behind `POST /api/user/password/reset/change`. Validates the bearer JWT's
   219	#' claims against the current DB row (rather than comparing JWT strings) so
   220	#' `jti`/`nbf` fields never cause a false mismatch.
   221	#'
   222	#' @param req Plumber request (needs `req$postBody`, `req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION`).
   223	#' @param res Plumber response (mutated on every path).
   224	#' @return List response body.
   225	svc_user_password_reset_change <- function(req, res) {
   226	  # Parse passwords from JSON body (OWASP: passwords MUST NOT be in URLs)
   227	  body <- tryCatch(
   228	    jsonlite::fromJSON(req$postBody),
   229	    error = function(e) list()
   230	  )
   231	  new_pass_1 <- body$password %||% ""
   232	  new_pass_2 <- body$password_confirm %||% ""
   233	  jwt <- str_remove(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION, "Bearer ")
   234	  key <- charToRaw(dw$secret)
   235	
   236	  user_jwt <- jwt_decode_hmac(jwt, secret = key)
   237	  user_jwt$token_expired <- (user_jwt$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time()))
   238	
   239	  if (is.null(jwt) || user_jwt$token_expired) {
   240	    res$status <- 401
     1	# api/functions/user-endpoint-helpers.R
     2	
     3	#' Shared password complexity rule for the change and reset flows
     4	#'
     5	#' A candidate password must be longer than 7 characters and contain at least
     6	#' one lowercase letter, one uppercase letter, one digit, and one of the
     7	#' permitted special characters (`!@#$%^&*`).
     8	#'
     9	#' @param password Candidate password string.
    10	#' @return `TRUE` when the password satisfies every rule, otherwise `FALSE`.
    11	#' @export
    12	password_meets_complexity <- function(password) {
    13	  nchar(password) > 7 &&
    14	    grepl("[a-z]", password) &&
    15	    grepl("[A-Z]", password) &&
    16	    grepl("\\d", password) &&
    17	    grepl("[!@#$%^&*]", password)
    18	}
    19	
    20	#' Validate a new-password pair for the change/reset flows
    21	#'
    22	#' Confirms the new password and its confirmation match, optionally differ from
    23	#' the current password (password-change flow only), and satisfy the shared
    24	#' complexity rule. The reset flow has no current password and omits `old_pass`.
    25	#'
    26	#' @param new_pass_1 The proposed new password.
    27	#' @param new_pass_2 The confirmation of the new password.
    28	#' @param old_pass Optional current password. When supplied, the new password
    29	#'   must differ from it; the reset flow passes `NULL`.
    30	#' @return `TRUE` when the pair is valid, otherwise `FALSE`.
    31	#' @export
    32	new_password_valid <- function(new_pass_1, new_pass_2, old_pass = NULL) {
    33	  (new_pass_1 == new_pass_2) &&
    34	    (is.null(old_pass) || new_pass_1 != old_pass) &&
    35	    password_meets_complexity(new_pass_1)
    36	}
    37	
    38	#' Process a password-reset REQUEST (email a one-time reset link, best-effort)
    39	#'
    40	#' Pure, side-effect-injectable core of `POST /api/user/password/reset/request`.
    41	#' The handler collects the `user` table and delegates here so the flow can be
    42	#' unit-tested without a live SMTP relay or database.
    43	#'
    44	#' Behaviour (see `test-unit-password-reset-request.R`):
    45	#' - Syntactically invalid email -> `400` (a client input error, not enumeration).
    46	#' - Any other outcome -> a SINGLE generic `200` response, whether or not the
    47	#'   email matches an account and whether or not the mail is delivered. This
    48	#'   makes the endpoint impossible to use for account enumeration.
    49	#' - Email delivery is BEST-EFFORT: a send failure (most commonly an SMTP
    50	#'   outage) is logged loudly and swallowed, so the endpoint never returns a
    51	#'   `500`. This mirrors the signup (#470) and admin-approval email hardening;
    52	#'   the reset flow was previously the only email path that let an SMTP error
    53	#'   propagate as an opaque error to a locked-out user.
    54	#'
    55	#' The reset-token semantics (JWT claim, `md5(salt+password)` fingerprint,
    56	#' `password_reset_date` stamp, `iat`/`exp`) are byte-identical to the historic
    57	#' inline handler so the sibling `POST .../password/reset/change` still
    58	#' validates tokens minted here.
    59	#'
    60	#' @param email_request Raw email string from the request body.
    61	#' @param user_table Collected `user` table tibble (needs `user_id`,
    62	#'   `user_name`, `email`, `password`).
    63	#' @param dw Config object (`secret`, `salt`, `refresh`, `base_url`).
    64	#' @param send_email Mailer, injectable for tests. Defaults to
    65	#'   `send_noreply_email`.
    66	#' @param update_reset_date Reset-date writer, injectable for tests. Defaults to
    67	#'   stamping `password_reset_date` via `user_update`.
    68	#' @return `list(status = <int>, body = <list>)` for the handler to emit.
    69	#' @export
    70	process_password_reset_request <- function(
    71	  email_request,
    72	  user_table,
    73	  dw,
    74	  send_email = send_noreply_email,
    75	  update_reset_date = function(user_id, ts) {
    76	    user_update(user_id, list(password_reset_date = as.character(ts)))
    77	  }
    78	) {
    79	  generic_ok <- list(
    80	    status = 200L,
    81	    body = list(
    82	      message = paste0(
    83	        "If an account exists for that email address, ",
    84	        "a password reset link has been sent."
    85	      )
    86	    )
    87	  )
    88	
    89	  if (!is_valid_email(email_request)) {
    90	    return(list(status = 400L, body = list(error = "Invalid Parameter Value Error.")))
    91	  }
    92	
    93	  # Case-insensitive lookup, first match only. Emails are unique in practice,
    94	  # but a case-only collision must not produce a vector-valued JWT claim.
    95	  matched <- user_table %>%
    96	    dplyr::mutate(email_lower = stringr::str_to_lower(.data$email)) %>%
    97	    dplyr::filter(.data$email_lower == stringr::str_to_lower(email_request)) %>%
    98	    dplyr::slice(1L)
    99	
   100	  if (nrow(matched) == 0L) {
   101	    return(generic_ok) # unknown email: identical generic response
   102	  }
   103	
   104	  # Known account: mint the reset token, stamp the reset date, and email the
   105	  # link. The whole block is best-effort — any failure (SMTP outage, transient
   106	  # DB error) is logged and swallowed so the caller always receives `generic_ok`
   107	  # and the endpoint never 500s.
   108	  tryCatch(
   109	    {
   110	      ts <- Sys.time()
   111	      key <- charToRaw(
   112	        if (is.list(dw$secret)) as.character(dw$secret[[1]]) else as.character(dw$secret)
   113	      )
   114	
   115	      update_reset_date(matched$user_id, ts)
   116	
   117	      claim <- jose::jwt_claim(
   118	        user_id = matched$user_id,
   119	        user_name = matched$user_name,
   120	        email = matched$email,

codex
The first concrete gap is deployment-critical: the plan documents new `AUTH_*` variables but never modifies the API service’s explicit Compose environment map. In the supported front-proxy topology, that can collapse every user into the proxy’s shared bucket and turn a few requests into broad auth denial. I’m checking whether the existing S6 tests and Traefik assumptions expose any additional bypasses or false-green paths.

    70	test_that("fingerprint uses the proxy-appended (rightmost) XFF hop by default, not the spoofable first", {
    71	  # Single-Traefik direct edge (empty trust set): Traefik appends the real client as
    72	  # the LAST entry; leftmost entries are client-supplied and must not be trusted.
    73	  req <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "9.9.9.9, 10.0.0.1", REMOTE_ADDR = "172.18.0.5")
    74	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(req), "10.0.0.1")
    75	  # A spoofed leftmost value cannot change the appended hop.
    76	  spoof <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "1.1.1.1, 10.0.0.1")
    77	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(spoof), "10.0.0.1")
    78	})

    80	test_that("fingerprint walks past TRUSTED proxies and is unspoofable under a front proxy", {
    81	  # A front proxy (10.9.0.0/24) sits in front of Traefik. Real chain reaching us:
    82	  # "<real-client>, <front-proxy-ip>". Walk right-to-left, skip the trusted front
    83	  # proxy, select the real client.
    84	  cidrs <- "10.9.0.0/24"
    85	  legit <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "203.0.113.7, 10.9.0.5")
    86	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(legit, trusted_cidrs = cidrs), "203.0.113.7")
    87	  # A DIRECT attacker (bypassing the front proxy) hits Traefik and forges a
    88	  # trusted-CIDR IP on the left; Traefik appends the attacker's real peer at the
    89	  # right. The rightmost UNTRUSTED hop (the attacker) is selected -> not spoofable.
    90	  attack <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "203.0.113.7, 10.9.0.5, 198.51.100.66")
    91	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(attack, trusted_cidrs = cidrs), "198.51.100.66")
    92	  # If every hop is a trusted proxy, fall back to REMOTE_ADDR.
    93	  allproxy <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "10.9.0.5", REMOTE_ADDR = "172.18.0.5")
    94	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(allproxy, trusted_cidrs = cidrs), "172.18.0.5")
    95	})
    96	
    97	test_that("an IPv6 trusted proxy is matched on the FULL address, not the /64 key", {
    98	  # A front proxy in 2001:db8:abcd::/48 appended the real IPv6 client. The trust check
    99	  # must evaluate the full proxy address (not the /64-collapsed bucket key) or the
   100	  # proxy is treated as a client and everyone behind it shares one quota.
   101	  cidr6 <- "2001:db8:abcd::/48"
   102	  legit <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "2001:4860:4860::8888, 2001:db8:abcd:1::5")
   103	  # Real client is grouped to its /64; the trusted proxy hop is skipped.
   104	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(legit, trusted_cidrs = cidr6), "2001:4860:4860:0::/64")
   105	  # Exact IPv6 trusted address also matches.
   106	  expect_equal(
   107	    async_job_submit_fingerprint(legit, trusted_cidrs = "2001:db8:abcd:1::5"),
   108	    "2001:4860:4860:0::/64"
   109	  )
   110	  # A direct IPv6 attacker forging a trusted-CIDR hop on the left cannot be skipped:
   111	  # the rightmost untrusted hop (its real address) is selected.
   112	  attack <- list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "2001:db8:abcd:1::5, 2001:dead:beef::9")
   113	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(attack, trusted_cidrs = cidr6), "2001:dead:beef:0::/64")
   114	})

   151	test_that("IPv6 rotation within a /64 collapses to one throttle bucket", {
   152	  # An attacker with a /64 allocation can rotate 2^64 addresses; grouping by the
   153	  # /64 network prefix keeps them one caller instead of 2^64 fresh buckets.
   154	  a <- async_job_submit_fingerprint(list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "2001:db8:abcd:1::1"))
   155	  b <- async_job_submit_fingerprint(list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "2001:db8:abcd:1::dead:beef"))
   156	  expect_equal(a, b)              # same /64 -> same key
   157	  expect_match(a, "/64$")
   158	  c <- async_job_submit_fingerprint(list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "2001:db8:abcd:2::1"))
   159	  expect_false(identical(a, c))   # different /64 -> different key
   160	})

   162	test_that("IPv6 /64 is compression-invariant and rejects malformed addresses", {
   163	  ip <- function(x) async_job_submit_fingerprint(list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = x))
   164	  # SAME address, different valid compressions -> ONE /64 key (no quota multiplication).
   165	  full <- ip("2001:0db8:0000:0001:0000:0000:0000:0005") # uncompressed, leading zeros
   166	  mid  <- ip("2001:db8:0:1::5")                          # "::" spans the interface bits
   167	  expect_equal(full, mid)
   168	  expect_equal(full, "2001:db8:0:1::/64")
   169	  # "::" that lands INSIDE the /64 prefix still expands to the correct hextets.
   170	  expect_equal(ip("2001::1:0:0:0:5"), "2001:0:0:1::/64")
   171	  # Malformed IPv6 is rejected (falls back to REMOTE_ADDR / "unknown"), not keyed.
   172	  expect_equal(async_job_submit_fingerprint(
   173	    list(HTTP_X_FORWARDED_FOR = "a:b", REMOTE_ADDR = "10.0.0.7")), "10.0.0.7")
   174	  expect_equal(ip("2001:::1"), "unknown")           # double "::"
   175	  expect_equal(ip("2001:db8:zzzz::1"), "unknown")   # non-hex hextet
   176	})

   191	test_that("admission guard admits under the limit and blocks with 429 over it", {
   192	  async_job_submit_rate_limit_reset()

   194	  # Default module limit is 5 per 60s. First 5 admit, 6th -> 429 + Retry-After.

   196	    res <- mock_res()
   197	    adm <- async_job_submit_admission_guard(req, res)
   198	    expect_true(adm$admitted)
   199	  }
   200	  res <- mock_res()
   201	  adm <- async_job_submit_admission_guard(req, res)
   202	  expect_false(adm$admitted)
   203	  expect_equal(res$status, 429)
   204	  expect_equal(adm$response$error, "RATE_LIMITED")
   205	  expect_true(!is.null(res$headers[["Retry-After"]]))
   206	  expect_gte(as.integer(res$headers[["Retry-After"]]), 1L)
   207	  async_job_submit_rate_limit_reset()

   210	test_that("admission guard fails CLOSED (503) on an internal throttle error", {
   211	  # A throttle bug must neither 500 the endpoint nor silently admit an abusive
   212	  # caller: an internal error is caught and mapped to 503 THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE.
   213	  orig <- async_job_submit_rate_limit
   214	  async_job_submit_rate_limit <<- function(...) stop("boom")
   215	  on.exit(async_job_submit_rate_limit <<- orig, add = TRUE)
   216	  res <- mock_res()
   217	  adm <- async_job_submit_admission_guard(list(REMOTE_ADDR = "10.0.0.1"), res)
   218	  expect_false(adm$admitted)

   224	test_that("the store is bounded against fingerprint rotation (memory-DoS guard)", {
   225	  st <- new.env(parent = emptyenv())
   226	  # Simulate rotation: many distinct fingerprints, each allowed once, at t=1000.
   227	  for (i in 1:50) {
   228	    async_job_submit_rate_limit(sprintf("ip-%d", i), now = 1000,
   229	      max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 10L)
   230	  }
   231	  # Bounded: <= 10 tracked callers (the 50 rotated IPs collapsed into the shared
   232	  # overflow bucket), and total bindings never approach 50.
   233	  expect_lte(.async_job_submit_size(st), 10L)
   234	  expect_lt(length(ls(envir = st, all.names = TRUE)), 50L)
   235	  # After the window, a fresh caller reclaims the fully-expired buckets.
   236	  async_job_submit_rate_limit("newcomer", now = 2000,
   237	    max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 10L)
   238	  expect_lte(.async_job_submit_size(st), 10L)
   239	})
   240	
   241	test_that("saturation routes new fingerprints to a shared overflow bucket, never evicting an active caller", {
   242	  st <- new.env(parent = emptyenv())
   243	  # Establish an active caller that has already spent 2 of 3 submissions.
   244	  async_job_submit_rate_limit("1.2.3.4", now = 1000, max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 3L)
   245	  async_job_submit_rate_limit("1.2.3.4", now = 1001, max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 3L)
   246	  # Saturate with distinct rotating callers within the same window.
   247	  for (i in 1:30) {
   248	    async_job_submit_rate_limit(sprintf("10.0.0.%d", i), now = 1002,
   249	      max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 3L)
   250	  }
   251	  # The active caller's window was NOT reset by the flood: it still has its 3rd (last)
   252	  # submission available, then the 4th is throttled.
   253	  r3 <- async_job_submit_rate_limit("1.2.3.4", now = 1003, max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 3L)
   254	  expect_true(r3$allowed)
   255	  r4 <- async_job_submit_rate_limit("1.2.3.4", now = 1004, max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 3L)
   256	  expect_false(r4$allowed)
   257	  # The rotating callers collapsed into ONE overflow bucket that is itself throttled.
   258	  denied <- async_job_submit_rate_limit("10.0.0.99", now = 1005, max_n = 3L, window_s = 60L, store = st, max_tracked = 3L)
   259	  expect_false(denied$allowed)
   260	})
   261	
   262	test_that("admission guard fails CLOSED (503) on a malformed (non-NULL) decision", {
   263	  orig <- async_job_submit_rate_limit
   264	  async_job_submit_rate_limit <<- function(...) list(nonsense = TRUE) # no valid $allowed
   265	  on.exit(async_job_submit_rate_limit <<- orig, add = TRUE)
   266	  res <- mock_res()
   267	  adm <- async_job_submit_admission_guard(list(REMOTE_ADDR = "10.0.0.1"), res)
   268	  expect_false(adm$admitted)
   269	  expect_equal(res$status, 503L)
   270	  expect_equal(adm$response$error, "THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE")
   271	})
   272	
   273	test_that("invalid env values fall back to safe defaults (not disable/corrupt)", {
   274	  expect_equal(.async_job_submit_env_int("NOPE_UNSET_VAR_XYZ", 5L, 0L), 5L)
   275	  withr::with_envvar(c(SOME_BAD = "abc"), expect_equal(.async_job_submit_env_int("SOME_BAD", 5L, 0L), 5L))
   276	  withr::with_envvar(c(SOME_NEG = "-3"), expect_equal(.async_job_submit_env_int("SOME_NEG", 60L, 1L), 60L))
   277	  withr::with_envvar(c(SOME_OK = "7"), expect_equal(.async_job_submit_env_int("SOME_OK", 5L, 0L), 7L))
   278	})

     1	# tests/testthat/test-unit-base-exists-get-guard.R
     2	#
     3	# Static guard: any call to exists()/get() that passes `inherits =` MUST be
     4	# namespaced as base::exists / base::get.
     5	#
     6	# Why: the live API runtime attaches packages (e.g. biomaRt -> AnnotationDbi)
     7	# that mask base `exists`/`get` with S4 generics which reject the base R
     8	# `inherits =` argument. A bare `exists("dw", envir = .GlobalEnv, inherits =
     9	# FALSE)` then throws `unused arguments (envir, inherits)`, which 500'd
    10	# GET /api/llm/config (the masked-verb failure mode documented in AGENTS.md,
    11	# same class as biomaRt::select masking dplyr::select).
    12	#
    13	# Pure test (no DB / no network) -- runs on host:
    14	#   cd api && Rscript --no-init-file -e \
    15	#     "testthat::test_file('tests/testthat/test-unit-base-exists-get-guard.R')"
    16	
    17	guarded_source_files <- function() {
    18	  root <- get_api_dir()
    19	  dirs <- file.path(root, c("endpoints", "functions", "services", "core"))
    20	  dirs <- dirs[dir.exists(dirs)]
    21	  unlist(lapply(dirs, list.files, pattern = "\\.R$", full.names = TRUE))
    22	}
    23	
    24	# An offending line passes `inherits` to a *bare* exists()/get() call --
    25	# i.e. one not already namespaced as `base::exists` / `base::get` (and not part
    26	# of some other `pkg::exists` call).
    27	bare_inherits_offenders <- function(verb, files) {
    28	  offenders <- character()
    29	  bare <- paste0("(^|[^:[:alnum:]_.])", verb, "\\(")
    30	  namespaced <- paste0("base::", verb, "\\(")
    31	  for (f in files) {
    32	    src <- readLines(f, warn = FALSE)
    33	    for (i in seq_along(src)) {
    34	      line <- src[i]
    35	      if (!grepl("\\binherits\\b", line)) next
    36	      if (!grepl(bare, line)) next
    37	      if (grepl(namespaced, line)) next
    38	      offenders <- c(offenders, paste0(basename(f), ":", i, ": ", trimws(line)))
    39	    }
    40	  }
    41	  offenders
    42	}
    43	
    44	test_that("exists() with inherits= is base:: namespaced", {
    45	  offenders <- bare_inherits_offenders("exists", guarded_source_files())
    46	  expect_identical(
    47	    offenders, character(),
    48	    info = paste(
    49	      "Use base::exists() when passing inherits= (masked-verb guard):",
    50	      paste(offenders, collapse = " | ")
    51	    )
    52	  )
    53	})
    54	
    55	test_that("get() with inherits= is base:: namespaced", {
    56	  offenders <- bare_inherits_offenders("get", guarded_source_files())
    57	  expect_identical(
    58	    offenders, character(),
    59	    info = paste(
    60	      "Use base::get() when passing inherits= (masked-verb guard):",
    61	      paste(offenders, collapse = " | ")
    62	    )
    63	  )
    64	})
     1	# tests/testthat/test-unit-endpoint-error-handler.R
     2	#
     3	# Static guard for RFC 9457 error consistency across mounted endpoints.
     4	#
     5	# Plumber does NOT propagate the root router's error handler to mounted
     6	# sub-routers — each `plumber::pr()` keeps its own. So a thrown classed error
     7	# (e.g. stop_for_bad_request() -> error_400) inside an endpoint mounted with a
     8	# bare `plumber::pr("endpoints/x.R")` falls back to plumber's default opaque
     9	# `{"error":"500 ..."}` instead of being mapped to the correct status +
    10	# application/problem+json by core/filters.R::errorHandler.
    11	#
    12	# bootstrap/mount_endpoints.R must therefore route EVERY endpoint sub-router
    13	# through the `mount_endpoint()` helper, which attaches errorHandler. This is a
    14	# pure source-text check (no DB), so it runs on the host.
    15	
    16	library(testthat)
    17	
    18	mount_path <- file.path(get_api_dir(), "bootstrap", "mount_endpoints.R")
    19	mount_src <- readLines(mount_path, warn = FALSE)
    20	mount_blob <- paste(mount_src, collapse = "\n")
    21	
    22	test_that("mount_endpoint helper attaches the RFC 9457 error + 404 handlers", {
    23	  expect_match(mount_blob, "mount_endpoint\\s*<-\\s*function\\(file\\)")
    24	  # The helper body must wire pr_set_error(errorHandler) ...
    25	  expect_match(mount_blob, "plumber::pr\\(file\\)\\s*%>%\\s*\\n\\s*plumber::pr_set_error\\(errorHandler\\)")
    26	  # ... and pr_set_404(notFoundHandler) so sub-path 404s are RFC 9457 too.
    27	  expect_match(mount_blob, "plumber::pr_set_404\\(notFoundHandler\\)")
    28	})
    29	
    30	test_that("every endpoint sub-router is mounted through mount_endpoint()", {
    31	  mount_lines <- grep("pr_mount\\(", mount_src, value = TRUE)
    32	  # Sanity: the API mounts many endpoint files.
    33	  expect_gt(length(mount_lines), 20)
    34	
    35	  # No endpoint sub-router may be mounted with a bare plumber::pr("endpoints/...")
    36	  # — that bypasses errorHandler. All must go through mount_endpoint().
    37	  bare <- grep('plumber::pr\\("endpoints/', mount_lines, value = TRUE)
    38	  expect_identical(
    39	    bare,
    40	    character(0),
    41	    info = paste(
    42	      "These mounts bypass the RFC 9457 errorHandler (use mount_endpoint()):\n",
    43	      paste(bare, collapse = "\n")
    44	    )
    45	  )
    46	
    47	  # Every endpoint mount routes through the helper.
    48	  endpoint_mounts <- grep('mount_endpoint\\("endpoints/', mount_lines, value = TRUE)
    49	  expect_gt(length(endpoint_mounts), 20)
    50	})
     1	library(testthat)
     2	
     3	`%||%` <- function(a, b) if (is.null(a)) b else a
     4	
     5	extract_plumber_handler <- function(file_path, decorator_regex, envir) {
     6	  src_lines <- readLines(file_path, warn = FALSE)
     7	  dec_line <- grep(decorator_regex, src_lines)
     8	  if (length(dec_line) != 1L) {
     9	    stop(
    10	      "Expected exactly one decorator match for ",
    11	      decorator_regex,
    12	      ", found ",
    13	      length(dec_line),
    14	      "."
    15	    )
    16	  }
    17	  dec_line <- dec_line[[1L]]
    18	
    19	  parsed <- parse(file = file_path, keep.source = TRUE)
    20	  srcrefs <- attr(parsed, "srcref")
    21	  if (is.null(srcrefs)) {
    22	    stop("Unable to read source refs for ", file_path)
    23	  }
    24	
    25	  handler_expr <- NULL
    26	  for (i in seq_along(parsed)) {
    27	    start_line <- srcrefs[[i]][1L]
    28	    if (start_line > dec_line) {
    29	      handler_expr <- parsed[[i]]
    30	      break
    31	    }
    32	  }
    33	  if (is.null(handler_expr)) {
    34	    stop("No top-level expression found after decorator line ", dec_line)
    35	  }
    36	
    37	  eval(handler_expr, envir = envir)
    38	}
    39	
    40	make_mock_res <- function() {
    41	  res <- new.env(parent = emptyenv())
    42	  res$status <- 200L
    43	  res$body <- NULL
    44	  res
    45	}
    46	
    47	make_mock_req <- function(
    48	  post_body = "",
    49	  content_type = NULL,
    50	  user_id = NULL,
    51	  user_role = NULL,
    52	  authorization = NULL
    53	) {
    54	  req <- list(postBody = post_body)
    55	  if (!is.null(content_type)) {
    56	    req$CONTENT_TYPE <- content_type
    57	    req$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE <- content_type
    58	  }
    59	  if (!is.null(user_id)) {
    60	    req$user_id <- user_id
    61	  }
    62	  if (!is.null(user_role)) {
    63	    req$user_role <- user_role
    64	  }
    65	  if (!is.null(authorization)) {
    66	    req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION <- authorization
    67	  }
    68	  req
    69	}

   128	extract_post_signup <- function(envir) {
   129	  extract_plumber_handler(
   130	    auth_file_path(),
   131	    decorator_regex = "^#\\*\\s+@post\\s+signup\\s*$",
   132	    envir = envir
   133	  )
   134	}
   135	
   136	extract_put_password_update <- function(envir) {
   137	  extract_plumber_handler(
   138	    user_file_path(),
   139	    decorator_regex = "^#\\*\\s+@put\\s+password/update\\s*$",
   140	    envir = envir
   141	  )
   142	}

   144	test_that("authentication endpoints expose the hard-cut route surface", {
   145	  src <- readLines(auth_file_path(), warn = FALSE)
   146	  password_src <- readLines(user_file_path(), warn = FALSE)
   147	  signup_idx <- grep("^#\\*\\s+@post\\s+signup\\s*$", src)
   148	  password_idx <- grep("^#\\*\\s+@put\\s+password/update\\s*$", password_src)
   149	
   150	  expect_true(any(grepl("^#\\*\\s+@post\\s+signup\\s*$", src)))
   151	  expect_false(any(grepl("^#\\*\\s+@get\\s+signup\\s*$", src)))
   152	
   153	  expect_true(any(grepl("^#\\*\\s+@post\\s+authenticate\\s*$", src)))
   154	  expect_false(any(grepl("^#\\*\\s+@get\\s+authenticate\\s*$", src)))
   155	
   156	  expect_length(signup_idx, 1L)
   157	  expect_length(password_idx, 1L)
   158	  signup_idx <- signup_idx[[1L]]
   159	  password_idx <- password_idx[[1L]]
   160	
   161	  signup_blob <- paste(src[signup_idx:min(length(src), signup_idx + 35L)], collapse = "\n")
   162	  expect_match(signup_blob, "req\\$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE")
   163	  expect_match(signup_blob, "res\\$status\\s*<-\\s*415")
   164	  expect_match(signup_blob, "res\\$status\\s*<-\\s*400")
   165	
   166	  password_blob <- paste(
   167	    password_src[password_idx:min(length(password_src), password_idx + 35L)],
   168	    collapse = "\n"
   169	  )
   170	  expect_match(password_blob, "req\\$HTTP_CONTENT_TYPE")
   171	  expect_match(password_blob, "res\\$status\\s*<-\\s*415")
   172	  expect_match(password_blob, "res\\$status\\s*<-\\s*400")
   173	})

     1	# tests/testthat/test-integration-auth.R
     2	# Integration tests for authentication endpoints
     3	#
     4	# These tests validate JWT token generation and validation logic.
     5	# They test the auth logic at the function level rather than HTTP level
     6	# to avoid requiring a running API server during tests.
     7	#
     8	# Rollback audit (Phase C unit C9, v11.0):
     9	#   This file is exempt from wrapping in `with_test_db_transaction`
    10	#   because the tests are non-transactional and never write to the
    11	#   database: they exercise JWT crypto primitives (create_test_jwt,
    12	#   jose::jwt_decode_hmac, auth_header) that read the shared secret
    13	#   from config but do not touch any SysNDD tables. No rollback
    14	#   scope is therefore applicable. The C9 orphan absorption keeps
    15	#   this file green under `scripts/verify-test-gate.sh --extended`.
    16	
    17	library(testthat)
    18	library(jose)
    19	
    20	# =============================================================================
    21	# JWT Token Generation Tests
    22	# =============================================================================
    23	
    24	test_that("create_test_jwt generates a valid JWT token", {
    25	  token <- create_test_jwt()
    26	
    27	  # Token should be a non-empty string
    28	  expect_true(is.character(token))
    29	  expect_true(nchar(token) > 50)
    30	
    31	  # Token should have 3 parts (header.payload.signature)
    32	  parts <- strsplit(token, "\\.")[[1]]
    33	  expect_equal(length(parts), 3)
    34	})
    35	
    36	test_that("create_test_jwt encodes correct user information", {
    37	  token <- create_test_jwt(
    38	    user_id = 42,
    39	    user_name = "admin_user",
    40	    user_role = "Administrator"
    41	  )
    42	
    43	  decoded <- decode_test_jwt(token)
    44	
    45	  expect_equal(decoded$user_id, 42)
    46	  expect_equal(decoded$user_name, "admin_user")
    47	  expect_equal(decoded$user_role, "Administrator")
    48	})
    49	
    50	test_that("create_test_jwt sets correct expiration for valid token", {
    51	  token <- create_test_jwt(expired = FALSE)
    52	  decoded <- decode_test_jwt(token)
    53	
    54	  # Token should expire in the future
    55	  expect_true(decoded$exp > as.numeric(Sys.time()))
    56	})
    57	
    58	test_that("create_test_jwt creates expired token that fails validation", {
    59	  token <- create_test_jwt(expired = TRUE)
    60	  
    61	  # Decoding an expired token should throw error about expiration
    62	  expect_error(
    63	    decode_test_jwt(token),
    64	    "expired"
    65	  )
    66	})
    67	
    68	
    69	# =============================================================================
    70	# JWT Token Validation Tests
    71	# =============================================================================
    72	
    73	test_that("JWT token can be decoded with correct secret", {
    74	  token <- create_test_jwt()
    75	  secret <- get_test_config("secret")
    76	  key <- charToRaw(secret)
    77	
    78	  # Should decode without error
    79	  decoded <- jose::jwt_decode_hmac(token, secret = key)
    80	
    81	  expect_true(is.list(decoded))
    82	  expect_true("user_id" %in% names(decoded))
    83	})
    84	
    85	test_that("JWT token fails to decode with wrong secret", {
    86	  token <- create_test_jwt()
    87	  wrong_key <- charToRaw("wrong_secret_key_12345")
    88	
    89	  # Should throw error with wrong secret
    90	  expect_error(
    91	    jose::jwt_decode_hmac(token, secret = wrong_key)
    92	  )
    93	})
    94	
    95	test_that("auth_header formats token correctly", {
    96	  token <- "test.jwt.token"
    97	  header <- auth_header(token)
    98	
    99	  expect_equal(header, "Bearer test.jwt.token")
   100	})
   101	
   102	
   103	# =============================================================================
   104	# Token Expiration Logic Tests
   105	# =============================================================================
   106	
   107	test_that("expired token is rejected by decode", {
   108	  token <- create_test_jwt(expired = TRUE)
   109	
   110	  # Should throw error when trying to decode expired token
   111	  expect_error(
   112	    decode_test_jwt(token),
   113	    "expired"
   114	  )
   115	})
   116	
   117	test_that("valid token is not expired", {
   118	  token <- create_test_jwt(expired = FALSE)
   119	  decoded <- decode_test_jwt(token)
   120	
   121	  # Check expiration - should be in the future
   122	  is_expired <- decoded$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())
   123	
   124	  expect_false(is_expired)
   125	})

/bin/bash -lc 'rg -n "forwardedHeaders|trustedIPs|insecure|X-Forwarded|strip-xff|CLUSTERING_SUBMIT|api:" docker-compose*.yml .env.example documentation/09-deployment.qmd | head -n 500' in /home/bernt-popp/development/sysndd/.claude/worktrees/535-auth-endpoint-rate-limit
 succeeded in 0ms:
documentation/09-deployment.qmd:382:- Public clustering submission also has a **per-caller admission throttle** (#535 S6) layered on the global cap: a sliding-window submit rate limit keyed on the client IP. `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX` (default `5`) submissions per `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_WINDOW_SECONDS` (default `60`); over the limit the public submit routes (`POST /api/jobs/clustering/submit`, `POST /api/jobs/phenotype_clustering/submit`) return `429` + `Retry-After` (`RATE_LIMITED`). The throttle runs **first**, before any DB/cache work. There is deliberately **no env kill-switch**: a stray or invalid `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_PER_CALLER_MAX` (including `0`, negative, or non-numeric) falls back to the safe default `5` rather than silently disabling the control, and all limits are clamped to sane ceilings (`MAX ≤ 1000`, `WINDOW 5..86400s`, `MAX_TRACKED ≤ 200000`) so a typo cannot make per-caller state unbounded. A non-IP value in the selected hop is discarded (falls back to `REMOTE_ADDR`), and IPv6 is grouped to its `/64` so an allocation is one caller. Under a rotation flood, memory stays bounded at `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_MAX_TRACKED` (default `20000`) fingerprints — brand-new callers collapse into one shared overflow bucket instead of evicting an active caller. On any internal throttle error (including a misconfigured limit) the guard **fails closed** (`503 THROTTLE_UNAVAILABLE` + `Retry-After`).
documentation/09-deployment.qmd:383:  - **Client-IP resolution (trusted-proxy walk):** the throttle walks `X-Forwarded-For` **right-to-left** and takes the first address that is NOT a configured trusted proxy (`CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS`, comma-separated IPv4 CIDRs / exact IPs). Our nearest proxy appends the peer it actually saw at the right, so the first untrusted address from the right is the real client and is **not spoofable** — an attacker can forge leftmost entries (even valid trusted-CIDR IPs) but never the rightmost hop the proxy observed. In the shipped Compose, **Traefik is the direct edge** (it publishes `:80`) and `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS` is **empty**, so nothing upstream is trusted and the rightmost (Traefik-appended) hop — the real client — is used. Plumber folds the underscore aliases `X_Forwarded_For` / `X-Forwarded_For` / `X_Forwarded-For` into the *same* CGI field as the canonical header, so the `api` router carries an `api-strip-xff-alias` Traefik headers middleware (in `docker-compose.yml`) that **deletes those aliases** before forwarding, leaving only Traefik's canonical chain.
documentation/09-deployment.qmd:384:  - **If you deploy behind an institutional reverse proxy / load balancer in front of Traefik** (so Traefik's direct peer is that proxy, not the client): set `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS` to the **front-proxy source CIDR(s)** so the walk skips them and selects the real client, and also allowlist those CIDRs on the Traefik web entrypoint (`--entryPoints.web.forwardedHeaders.trustedIPs=<proxy-cidr,...>`) so Traefik preserves the client IP the front proxy set. Restrict direct ingress to Traefik's port so a client cannot bypass the front proxy. Verify with the live two-proxy path (two distinct client IPs must throttle independently). Without the trusted-CIDR configuration, every client behind that proxy fingerprints as the shared front-proxy address and one abusive caller `429`s everyone (collateral throttling — an availability degradation, never a bypass).

Our nearest proxy appends the peer it actually saw at the right, so the first untrusted address from the right is the real client and is **not spoofable** — an attacker can forge leftmost entries (even valid trusted-CIDR IPs) but never the rightmost hop the proxy observed. In the shipped Compose, **Traefik is the direct edge** (it publishes `:80`) and `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS` is **empty**, so nothing upstream is trusted and the rightmost (Traefik-appended) hop — the real client — is used. Plumber folds the underscore aliases `X_Forwarded_For` / `X-Forwarded_For` / `X_Forwarded-For` into the *same* CGI field as the canonical header, so the `api` router carries an `api-strip-xff-alias` Traefik headers middleware (in `docker-compose.yml`) that **deletes those aliases** before forwarding, leaving only Traefik's canonical chain.
documentation/09-deployment.qmd:384:  - **If you deploy behind an institutional reverse proxy / load balancer in front of Traefik** (so Traefik's direct peer is that proxy, not the client): set `CLUSTERING_SUBMIT_TRUSTED_PROXY_CIDRS` to the **front-proxy source CIDR(s)** so the walk skips them and selects the real client, and also allowlist those CIDRs on the Traefik web entrypoint (`--entryPoints.web.forwardedHeaders.trustedIPs=<proxy-cidr,...>`) so Traefik preserves the client IP the front proxy set. Restrict direct ingress to Traefik's port so a client cannot bypass the front proxy. Verify with the live two-proxy path (two distinct client IPs must throttle independently). Without the trusted-CIDR configuration, every client behind that proxy fingerprints as the shared front-proxy address and one abusive caller `429`s everyone (collateral throttling — an availability degradation, never a bypass).

     1	# docker-compose.playwright.yml
     2	# Playwright-only stack overlay. Activated by `make playwright-stack`.
     3	# Deliberately uses the same service names as docker-compose.yml so the
     4	# overlay applies cleanly via `-f docker-compose.yml -f
     5	# docker-compose.playwright.yml`.
     6	#
     7	# Notes vs the production compose file:
     8	#   - The DB service is named `mysql` (not `db`) in the base compose.
     9	#   - The base compose interpolates ${MYSQL_*}, ${PASSWORD}, ${OMIM_DOWNLOAD_KEY}
    10	#     etc. from the shell or a .env file. The Playwright Makefile target
    11	#     exports these for the duration of the up/down command, so the overlay
    12	#     reads them like the base compose does.
    13	#   - The API container expects to read its config from `api/config.yml`
    14	#     (`sysndd_db` block by default in production mode, see
    15	#     api/start_sysndd_api.R). The dbname there must match `MYSQL_DATABASE`.
    16	#   - Traefik Host() rules in the base compose only match
    17	#     `sysndd.dbmr.unibe.ch`. We override here to allow `localhost` and
    18	#     `127.0.0.1` so Playwright can reach the stack on `http://localhost`.
    19	#   - We deliberately do NOT bring up `mysql-cron-backup` or `worker` for the
    20	#     Playwright suite — they are not required for the deep-flow specs and
    21	#     adding them only increases startup time. If a future spec needs the
    22	#     async worker, add a `worker:` block to this overlay.
    23	#   - Container names, networks, ports, and volumes are remapped to
    24	#     `sysndd_playwright_*` names so the stack does not collide with a
    25	#     developer's running `make dev` stack.
    26

   108	# -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
   109	# Log Cleanup (scheduled DB retention) — issue #105
   110	# -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
   111	# The `log-cleanup` service prunes old rows from the operational request log
   112	# table (`logging`) on a daily schedule. It reuses the API image and connects
   113	# via the same RMariaDB pool/config as the API. Override these to tune it.
   114	#
   115	#   LOG_RETENTION_DAYS    Delete `logging` rows older than this many days (default 30)
   116	#   LOG_CLEANUP_AT        Daily run time, HH:MM in container (UTC) time (default 04:00,
   117	#                         staggered off the 03:00 database backup)
   118	#   LOG_CLEANUP_DRY_RUN   When 1/true/yes/on: count-only, never delete (default false)
   119	#
   120	# The same daily loop also prunes terminal, non-retryable `async_jobs` rows
   121	# (status completed/failed/cancelled AND active_request_hash IS NULL) — #535 S7:
   122	#   ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_DAYS           Delete terminal jobs older than this (default 90)
   123	#   ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_DRY_RUN        Count-only; unrecognized value fails safe (default false)
   124	#   ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_BATCH_SIZE     Candidate PKs read+deleted per batch, clamped <=1000 (default 1000)
   125	#   ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_LOCK_WAIT_SECONDS  Per-batch row+metadata lock wait, clamped <=30 (default 10)
   126	
   127	LOG_RETENTION_DAYS=30
   128	LOG_CLEANUP_AT=04:00
   129	LOG_CLEANUP_DRY_RUN=false
   130	ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_DAYS=90
   131	ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_DRY_RUN=false
   132	ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_BATCH_SIZE=1000
   133	ASYNC_JOB_RETENTION_LOCK_WAIT_SECONDS=10
   134

   146	# - Use strong passwords (16+ characters, mixed case, numbers, symbols)

   148	# - Keep .env file permissions restricted (chmod 600 .env)

     1	# tests/testthat/test-unit-base-exists-get-guard.R
     2	#
     3	# Static guard: any call to exists()/get() that passes `inherits =` MUST be
     4	# namespaced as base::exists / base::get.
     5	#
     6	# Why: the live API runtime attaches packages (e.g. biomaRt -> AnnotationDbi)
     7	# that mask base `exists`/`get` with S4 generics which reject the base R
     8	# `inherits =` argument. A bare `exists("dw", envir = .GlobalEnv, inherits =
     9	# FALSE)` then throws `unused arguments (envir, inherits)`, which 500'd
    10	# GET /api/llm/config (the masked-verb failure mode documented in AGENTS.md,
    11	# same class as biomaRt::select masking dplyr::select).
    12	#
    13	# Pure test (no DB / no network) -- runs on host:
    14	#   cd api && Rscript --no-init-file -e \
    15	#     "testthat::test_file('tests/testthat/test-unit-base-exists-get-guard.R')"
    16	
    17	guarded_source_files <- function() {
    18	  root <- get_api_dir()
    19	  dirs <- file.path(root, c("endpoints", "functions", "services", "core"))
    20	  dirs <- dirs[dir.exists(dirs)]
    21	  unlist(lapply(dirs, list.files, pattern = "\\.R$", full.names = TRUE))
    22	}
    23	
    24	# An offending line passes `inherits` to a *bare* exists()/get() call --
    25	# i.e. one not already namespaced as `base::exists` / `base::get` (and not part
    26	# of some other `pkg::exists` call).
    27	bare_inherits_offenders <- function(verb, files) {
    28	  offenders <- character()
    29	  bare <- paste0("(^|[^:[:alnum:]_.])", verb, "\\(")
    30	  namespaced <- paste0("base::", verb, "\\(")
    31	  for (f in files) {
    32	    src <- readLines(f, warn = FALSE)
    33	    for (i in seq_along(src)) {
    34	      line <- src[i]
    35	      if (!grepl("\\binherits\\b", line)) next
    36	      if (!grepl(bare, line)) next
    37	      if (grepl(namespaced, line)) next
    38	      offenders <- c(offenders, paste0(basename(f), ":", i, ": ", trimws(line)))
    39	    }
    40	  }
    41	  offenders
    42	}
    43	
    44	test_that("exists() with inherits= is base:: namespaced", {
    45	  offenders <- bare_inherits_offenders("exists", guarded_source_files())
    46	  expect_identical(
    47	    offenders, character(),
    48	    info = paste(
    49	      "Use base::exists() when passing inherits= (masked-verb guard):",
    50	      paste(offenders, collapse = " | ")
    51	    )
    52	  )
    53	})
    54	
    55	test_that("get() with inherits= is base:: namespaced", {
    56	  offenders <- bare_inherits_offenders("get", guarded_source_files())
    57	  expect_identical(
    58	    offenders, character(),
    59	    info = paste(
    60	      "Use base::get() when passing inherits= (masked-verb guard):",
    61	      paste(offenders, collapse = " | ")
    62	    )
    63	  )
    64	})

     2	# Provides business logic for signin, verify, and refresh operations

     9	#' Authenticate user and return JWT token
    10	#'
    11	#' Validates credentials against database, checks account status,
    12	#' and generates JWT token pair (access + refresh) on success.
    13	#'
    14	#' @param user_name Username to authenticate
    15	#' @param password Plain text password
    16	#' @param pool Database connection pool
    17	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
    18	#' @return List with access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, and user info
    19	#' @examples
    20	#' \dontrun{
    21	#' result <- auth_signin("johndoe", "password123", pool, config)
    22	#' # Returns: list(access_token, refresh_token, token_type, expires_in, user)
    23	#' }
    24	auth_signin <- function(user_name, password, pool, config) {
    25	  # Validate inputs
    26	  if (missing(user_name) || is.null(user_name) || nchar(trimws(user_name)) == 0) {
    27	    stop_for_bad_request("user_name is required")
    28	  }
    29	  if (missing(password) || is.null(password) || nchar(password) == 0) {
    30	    stop_for_bad_request("password is required")
    31	  }
    32	
    33	  # Look up user (include password for verification)
    34	  # Rename created_at to user_created so downstream JWT code works without warning
    35	  user <- pool %>%
    36	    tbl("user") %>%
    37	    filter(user_name == !!user_name) %>%
    38	    dplyr::rename(user_created = created_at) %>%
    39	    collect()
    40	
    41	  if (nrow(user) == 0) {
    42	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid username or password")
    43	  }
    44	
    45	  user <- user[1, ]
    46	
    47	  # Check account status (approved column: 1 = active, 0 = pending)
    48	  if (is.null(user$approved) || user$approved != 1) {
    49	    stop_for_unauthorized("Account is not active")
    50	  }
    51	
    52	  # Verify password using security.R helper (handles legacy + Argon2id)
    53	  if (!verify_password(user$password, password)) {
    54	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid username or password")
    55	  }
    56	
    57	  # Progressive password upgrade if needed
    58	  if (needs_upgrade(user$password)) {
    59	    upgrade_password(pool, user$user_id, password)
    60	  }
    61	
    62	  # Generate JWT token pair
    63	  token <- auth_generate_token(user, config)
    64	
    65	  logger::log_info("User signed in", user_id = user$user_id, user_name = user$user_name)
    66	
    67	  list(
    68	    access_token = token$access_token,
    69	    refresh_token = token$refresh_token,
    70	    token_type = "Bearer",
    71	    expires_in = config$token_expiry %||% 3600,
    72	    user = list(
    73	      user_id = user$user_id,
    74	      user_name = user$user_name,
    75	      user_role = user$user_role,
    76	      email = user$email
    77	    )
    78	  )
    79	}
    80	
    81	
    82	#' Verify JWT token and return user info
    83	#'
    84	#' Validates token signature and expiration without database lookup.
    85	#' Returns user claims if valid, signals error if invalid/expired.
    86	#'
    87	#' @param jwt JWT token string (without "Bearer " prefix)
    88	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret
    89	#' @return List with user info (user_id, user_name, email, user_role, etc.)
    90	#' @examples
    91	#' \dontrun{
    92	#' user_info <- auth_verify("eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5...", config)
    93	#' # Returns: list(user_id, user_name, email, user_role, ...)
    94	#' }
    95	auth_verify <- function(jwt, config) {
    96	  if (missing(jwt) || is.null(jwt) || nchar(jwt) == 0) {
    97	    stop_for_unauthorized("Token is required")
    98	  }
    99	
   100	  # Validate and decode token
   101	  user <- auth_validate_token(jwt, config)
   102	
   103	  if (is.null(user)) {
   104	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid or expired token")
   105	  }
   106	
   107	  # Check expiration
   108	  if (user$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   109	    stop_for_unauthorized("Token has expired")
   110	  }
   111	
   112	  # Return user info (excluding internal fields)
   113	  list(
   114	    user_id = user$user_id,
   115	    user_name = user$user_name,
   116	    email = user$email,
   117	    user_role = user$user_role,
   118	    user_created = user$user_created,
   119	    abbreviation = user$abbreviation,
   120	    orcid = user$orcid,
   121	    exp = user$exp
   122	  )
   123	}
   124	
   125	
   126	#' Refresh JWT token with new expiration
   127	#'
   128	#' Validates existing token and issues new token with extended expiry.
   129	#' Requires token to be valid (not expired).
   130	#'
   131	#' @param refresh_token Current JWT refresh token
   132	#' @param pool Database connection pool (unused but kept for consistency)
   133	#' @param config Configuration object with JWT secret and expiry
   134	#' @return New JWT token string
   135	#' @examples
   136	#' \dontrun{
   137	#' new_token <- auth_refresh("eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5...", pool, config)
   138	#' # Returns: "eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5..."
   139	#' }
   140	auth_refresh <- function(refresh_token, pool, config) {
   141	  if (missing(refresh_token) || is.null(refresh_token) || nchar(refresh_token) == 0) {
   142	    stop_for_bad_request("refresh_token is required")
   143	  }
   144	
   145	  # Validate signature + decode the presented token.
   146	  claims <- auth_validate_token(refresh_token, config)
   147	  if (is.null(claims)) {
   148	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   149	  }
   150	  if (is.null(claims$exp) || claims$exp < as.numeric(Sys.time())) {
   151	    stop_for_unauthorized("Refresh token has expired")
   152	  }
   153	
   154	  # #535 P0-2: a token that predates session-epoch support carries no `sepoch`.
   155	  # Reject it rather than treating it as epoch 0 — otherwise a pre-deploy
   156	  # (possibly compromised) token could be refreshed into a fresh epoch-0 token
   157	  # and renewed indefinitely. This forces exactly one post-deploy sign-in.
   158	  if (is.null(claims$sepoch) || length(claims$sepoch) != 1L) {
   159	    stop_for_unauthorized("Session predates revocation support. Please sign in again.")
   160	  }
   161	  token_epoch <- suppressWarnings(as.numeric(claims$sepoch))
   162	  if (is.na(token_epoch)) {
   163	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   164	  }
   165	
   166	  # Validate the subject id before querying.
   167	  uid <- suppressWarnings(as.integer(claims$user_id))
   168	  if (length(uid) != 1L || is.na(uid) || uid <= 0L) {
   169	    stop_for_unauthorized("Invalid refresh token")
   170	  }
   171	
   172	  # #535 P0-2: read CURRENT account state, verify it, and sign the new token
   173	  # under a single row lock (`SELECT ... FOR UPDATE`) so the read-check-sign is
   174	  # serialized against any concurrent privilege/state mutation. Without the
   175	  # lock a refresh could read the pre-demotion row and then sign a stale-role
   176	  # token after the demotion commits (TOCTOU). Never trust the token's claims.
   177	  issue <- function(conn) {
   178	    user <- DBI::dbGetQuery(
   179	      conn,
   180	      "SELECT user_id, user_name, email, user_role, session_epoch,
     1	# Logging Sanitization Utilities for SysNDD API
     2	# Provides functions to remove sensitive data before logging
     3	#
     4	# Usage:
     5	#   source("core/logging_sanitizer.R")
     6	#   log_info("Request received", request = sanitize_request(req))
     7	#   log_debug("User data", user = sanitize_user(user_table))
     8	
     9	# Define sensitive field names that should be redacted in logs
    10	# Case-insensitive matching is used when sanitizing
    11	SENSITIVE_FIELDS <- c(
    12	  "password",
    13	  "old_pass",
    14	  "new_pass",
    15	  "new_pass_1",
    16	  "new_pass_2",
    17	  "token",
    18	  "jwt",
    19	  "api_key",
    20	  "secret",
    21	  "authorization"
    22	)
    23	
    24	#' Recursively sanitize sensitive fields in nested lists
    25	#'
    26	#' Traverses list structures and replaces values of sensitive fields
    27	#' with "[REDACTED]". Uses case-insensitive matching for field names.
    28	#'
    29	#' @param obj Object to sanitize (list, vector, or primitive)
    30	#' @return Sanitized object with sensitive field values replaced
    31	#' @examples
    32	#' sanitize_object(list(user = "john", password = "secret123"))
    33	#' # Returns: list(user = "john", password = "[REDACTED]")
    34	sanitize_object <- function(obj) {
    35	  if (is.null(obj)) {
    36	    return(NULL)
    37	  }
    38	
    39	  if (is.list(obj) && !is.null(names(obj))) {
    40	    # Named list - check each field name
    41	    sanitized <- lapply(names(obj), function(name) {
    42	      # Substring/pattern match so compound field names (access_token,
    43	      # refresh_token, password_hash, api_key, ...) are also redacted (LOW-3).
    44	      if (grepl("pass|token|secret|jwt|api_key|authorization|hash",
    45	                tolower(name)) ||
    46	            tolower(name) %in% tolower(SENSITIVE_FIELDS)) {
    47	        "[REDACTED]"
    48	      } else {
    49	        sanitize_object(obj[[name]])
    50	      }
    51	    })
    52	    names(sanitized) <- names(obj)
    53	    return(sanitized)
    54	  } else if (is.list(obj)) {
    55	    # Unnamed list - recurse into elements
    56	    return(lapply(obj, sanitize_object))
    57	  } else {
    58	    # Primitive value - return as-is
    59	    return(obj)
    60	  }
    61	}
    62	
    63	#' Sanitize Plumber request object for safe logging
    64	#'
    65	#' Extracts safe fields from Plumber request and sanitizes potentially
    66	#' sensitive data like headers, args, and body.
    67	#'
    68	#' Safe fields retained: PATH_INFO, REQUEST_METHOD, QUERY_STRING, REMOTE_ADDR
    69	#' Sanitized: headers (especially Authorization), args, body
    70	#'
    71	#' @param req Plumber request object
    72	#' @return Sanitized request object safe for logging
    73	#' @examples
    74	#' \dontrun{
    75	#' log_info("Request received", request = sanitize_request(req))
    76	#' }
    77	sanitize_request <- function(req) {
    78	  if (is.null(req)) {
    79	    return(NULL)
    80	  }
    81	
    82	  # Build safe request object with only safe fields
    83	  req_safe <- list(
    84	    PATH_INFO = req$PATH_INFO %||% NA_character_,
    85	    REQUEST_METHOD = req$REQUEST_METHOD %||% NA_character_,
    86	    # The query string can carry tokens/credentials in legacy transitional
    87	    # flows; never retain it raw in logs (LOW-3).
    88	    QUERY_STRING = if (is.null(req$QUERY_STRING) || req$QUERY_STRING == "") {
    89	      NA_character_
    90	    } else {
    91	      "[REDACTED]"
    92	    },
    93	    REMOTE_ADDR = req$REMOTE_ADDR %||% NA_character_
    94	  )
    95	
    96	  # Sanitize headers (especially Authorization, X-Api-Key)
    97	  if (!is.null(req$HEADERS)) {
    98	    headers_safe <- as.list(req$HEADERS)
    99	    # Redact known sensitive headers
   100	    sensitive_headers <- c("authorization", "x-api-key", "cookie", "x-auth-token")
   101	    for (header_name in names(headers_safe)) {
   102	      if (tolower(header_name) %in% sensitive_headers) {
   103	        headers_safe[[header_name]] <- "[REDACTED]"
   104	      }
   105	    }
   106	    req_safe$HEADERS <- headers_safe
   107	  }
   108	
   109	  # Also check HTTP_ prefixed headers (Plumber convention)
   110	  if (!is.null(req$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION)) {
   111	    req_safe$HTTP_AUTHORIZATION <- "[REDACTED]"
   112	  }
   113	
   114	  # Sanitize args (query parameters and path parameters)
   115	  if (!is.null(req$args)) {
   116	    req_safe$args <- sanitize_object(req$args)
   117	  }
   118	
   119	  # Sanitize body (POST/PUT request body)
   120	  if (!is.null(req$body)) {
   121	    req_safe$body <- sanitize_object(req$body)
   122	  }
   123	
   124	  # Sanitize argsBody (alternative body accessor in Plumber)
   125	  if (!is.null(req$argsBody)) {
   126	    req_safe$argsBody <- sanitize_object(req$argsBody)
   127	  }
   128	
   129	  return(req_safe)
   130	}
   131	
   132	#' Sanitize user data for safe logging
   133	#'
   134	#' Handles both data.frame and list representations of user data.
   135	#' Replaces sensitive fields (password, token) with "[REDACTED]".
   136	#'
   137	#' @param user User data (data.frame or list)
   138	#' @return Sanitized user data safe for logging
   139	#' @examples
   140	#' sanitize_user(list(user_id = 1, password = "secret"))
   141	#' # Returns: list(user_id = 1, password = "[REDACTED]")
   142	sanitize_user <- function(user) {
   143	  if (is.null(user)) {
   144	    return(NULL)
   145	  }
   146	
   147	  if (is.data.frame(user)) {
   148	    # Data frame - sanitize column values
   149	    user_safe <- user
   150	    sensitive_columns <- intersect(tolower(names(user_safe)), tolower(SENSITIVE_FIELDS))
   151	    for (col in names(user_safe)) {
   152	      if (tolower(col) %in% tolower(SENSITIVE_FIELDS)) {
   153	        user_safe[[col]] <- "[REDACTED]"
   154	      }
   155	    }
   156	    return(user_safe)
   157	  } else if (is.list(user)) {
   158	    # List - use recursive sanitization
   159	    return(sanitize_object(user))
   160	  } else {
   161	    # Unknown type - return as-is
   162	    return(user)
   163	  }
   164	}

codex
Two more security properties need explicit proof in the plan: the limiter state is process-local while this deployment supports multiple API replicas, and the global postroute hook currently parses/logs auth bodies after the endpoint returns. I’m validating the proxy behavior against Traefik’s official configuration semantics before assigning severity.

     1	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
     2	# api/bootstrap/load_modules.R
     3	#
     4	# Part of the Phase D.D6 extract-bootstrap refactor.
     5	#
     6	# Loads every R source file required by the running API into the
     7	# global environment, in the correct order:
     8	#   1. functions/* (repositories, helpers, clients, etc.)
     9	#   2. core/* (security, errors, responses, middleware, filters)
    10	#   3. services/* (transactional orchestration)
    11	#
    12	# Source order matters. Repository functions are loaded BEFORE
    13	# services so that any `svc_`/`service_`-prefixed function in
    14	# services/* can still call the underlying repository helpers.
    15	# (A service that accidentally drops its prefix will shadow the
    16	# repository function — see CLAUDE.md.)
    17	#
    18	# Mirai daemon workers do NOT use this module. They re-source a
    19	# hand-picked subset of functions/* via `everywhere({...})` in
    20	# api/bootstrap/setup_workers.R. Changes here do not automatically
    21	# propagate to workers — update setup_workers.R as well when a
    22	# function file is needed inside a daemon.
    23	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    24	
    25	#' Source a file into .GlobalEnv with a helpful error if missing.
    26	#'
    27	#' `source(..., local = FALSE)` puts the bindings into the global
    28	#' environment — that is what endpoint files expect at runtime.
    29	#' Top-level `source("...", local = TRUE)` in start_sysndd_api.R
    30	#' previously had the same effect by accident of being at the top
    31	#' level of the script; here we make the intent explicit.
    32	#'
    33	#' @param path Relative path from api/ to the source file.
    34	#' @noRd
    35	.bootstrap_source <- function(path) {
    36	  if (!file.exists(path)) {
    37	    stop(sprintf("bootstrap: source file not found: %s", path))
    38	  }
    39	  source(path, local = FALSE)
    40	  invisible(NULL)
    41	}

     1	######################################################################
     2	# start_sysndd_api.R
     3	#
     4	# Thin top-level composer for the SysNDD Plumber API.
     5	#
     6	# After the Phase D.D6 extract-bootstrap refactor the heavy lifting
     7	# lives in api/bootstrap/*.R. This script:
     8	#   1. attaches libraries + resolves the environment-specific config
     9	#   2. sources every application module (repositories, core, services,
    10	#      filters) via api/bootstrap/load_modules.R
    11	#   3. builds the DB pool, runs migrations, configures the memoise cache
    12	#   4. spawns the mirai daemon pool and pre-sources worker deps
    13	#   5. mounts every endpoint onto the root router
    14	#   6. starts Plumber
    15	#
    16	# Every bootstrap module returns its result. The composer binds the
    17	# returned value at script top level (which IS .GlobalEnv), so
    18	# endpoints / filters / services that still look up `pool`,
    19	# `serializers`, `migration_status`, `root`, etc. as globals keep
    20	# working unchanged — no super-assignments required anywhere.
    21	#
    22	# Run with: Rscript start_sysndd_api.R
    23	# Override env with: ENVIRONMENT=production Rscript start_sysndd_api.R
    24	######################################################################
    25	
    26	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##

    28	## -------------------------------------------------------------------##
    29	source("bootstrap/init_libraries.R", local = FALSE)
    30	source("bootstrap/load_modules.R",    local = FALSE)
    31	source("bootstrap/create_pool.R",     local = FALSE)
    32	source("bootstrap/run_migrations.R",  local = FALSE)
    33	source("bootstrap/init_globals.R",    local = FALSE)
    34	source("bootstrap/init_cache.R",      local = FALSE)
    35	source("bootstrap/setup_workers.R",   local = FALSE)
    36	source("bootstrap/mount_endpoints.R", local = FALSE)

    38	bootstrap_init_libraries()
